Report on the results of parallel inspections of the value added tax administration between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Foreword
The presented material informs about the course and results of parallel inspections performed by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on value added tax administration and the use of VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System). on value added tax).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so revenues from value added tax affect not only the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
The parallel inspections focused mainly on the control of the procedure of tax administrators in verifying the amount of value added tax paid in business transactions carried out between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of value added tax payers in the individual Member States of the European Union and on the commercial transactions carried out by these payers.
The discrepancy between the data in the VIES system and the data in the value added tax return filed by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and enable the detection of tax evasion or under water.
The benefit of the performed parallel inspections consisted not only in the exchange of information on the progress of financial resp. tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular in verifying the use of the VIES system in controlling the exercise of the right to exemption from value added tax in intra-Community transactions.
The knowledge gained during the implementation of parallel inspections is beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of other parallel inspections in cooperation with the inspection institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the value added tax administration for the period from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of control: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and fulfillment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States
On 12 September 2005, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SAO, CR”) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SAO SR”) concluded an Agreement on Cooperation in Audit Activities.
The subject of the agreement was cooperation in parallel control actions "Value Added Tax Administration", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO, CR for 2005 under No. 05/19 and "Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and recovery of value added tax". and fulfillment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU member states ”, included in the SAO SR plan of control activities under No. 22/2005.
The parallel control actions had the character of a coordinated control.
The result of the joint coordinated inspection was processed in accordance with the European Implementing Regulation No. 31 for INTOSAI inspection standards.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent specified in the concluded contract and in the preparation of a joint final report on the result of parallel inspections.
The purpose of the coordinated inspection was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious business transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter "CR") and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter "SR").
Both parties have contractually agreed to provide each other with information from public sources, from the electronic system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on received and sent requests to verify business transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The inspections were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by the Department of the State Budget and the Territorial Departments of Central Bohemia, Northwestern Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The auditees were the Ministry of Finance and 12 tax offices: the Financial Office in Mladá Boleslav, the Financial Office in Kolín, the Financial Office in Teplice, the Financial Office in Karlovy Vary, the Financial Office in Tábor, the Financial Office in Brno III, the Financial Office in Znojmo, the Financial Office in Zlín, the Financial Office in Šumperk, the Financial Office Ostrava I, the Financial Office for Prague 7 and the Financial Office for Prague 9.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic was performed by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: Bratislava I Tax Office, Komárno Tax Office, Trenčín Tax Office, Prievidza Tax Office, Zvolen Tax Office, Tax Office Dolný Kubín Office, Košice II Tax Office, Košice V Tax Office and Michalovce Tax Office.
Objective of inspections:
The aim of the parallel control actions was to check the progress of financial, resp. tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter "EU") and examine the use of electronic information system VIES, especially in monitoring the .
The audited period of the coordinated inspection was the period from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel inspections In the EU Member States, the electronic VIES system is in place, which allows tax administrations to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt taxable supplies from VAT and in the country of destination to verify that the purchaser duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
VIES is not centralized within the EU, each Member State is developing its own system.
The inspection revealed differences in the national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the following areas:
The summary reports show the values ​​of deliveries of goods to other EU Member States, the values ​​of the services provided are not reported in the summary reports.
Data from summary reports submitted by Czech taxpayers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of tax authorities, where they are compared with data on deliveries of goods to other EU Member States stated in VAT tax returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the summary reports to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In the Slovak Republic, data from summary reports submitted by Slovak taxpayers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers report the value of supplies of goods and the value of services provided to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which allows comparing the values ​​stated in summary reports with the values ​​of supplies of goods under VAT returns and identifying any differences.
In the Slovak Republic, the values ​​of goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported in aggregate on a common line of the VAT return.
As a result, in the Slovak Republic, the system does not allow automatic identification of differences between the values ​​of the supply of goods according to VAT tax returns and summary reports.
Separate reporting of the values ​​of supplies of goods in VAT tax returns makes it possible to use the results of comparing data when checking the exemption of supplies of goods to the EU from VAT.
Delivered data from summary reports submitted by payers in other EU member states are processed at CLO and compared with the value of acquisition of goods stated by payers from the Czech Republic, resp. SR in tax returns for VAT.
In the Slovak Republic, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax administrators themselves decide which cases of differences they will examine.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values ​​of deliveries and acquisitions of goods must be checked by the tax administrator, and forwards the list of these cases to the locally competent tax authorities.
This ensures that for the most significant deviations, it will be checked whether the VAT was declared in the correct amount when purchasing the goods.
The audit also drew attention to some problems in the VAT administration system of complications caused by different reporting of intra-Community transactions (ie supplies and acquisitions of goods by payers from different EU Member States):
Aggregate reports are submitted in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum deadline for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the respective quarter.
Reducing the period for which recapitulative statements are submitted to one month, together with shortening the processing time, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
Tax administrations would thus be able to verify more effectively whether VAT on intra-Community acquisitions was declared at the correct level.
At the same time, filing VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax period (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer reported the same value of supplies of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return.
Differences between the values ​​of delivery of goods reported by payers from the EU and the values ​​of acquisition of goods reported by payers from the Czech Republic, resp. The Slovak Republic was caused, among other things, by different reporting of data on intra-Community supply and acquisition in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in the recapitulative statements, or the reporting of intra-Community supplies in the supplier's recapitulative statement in a quarter other than intra-Community acquisitions in the acquirer's VAT return.
Unification of the conditions for reporting this data within the EU would lead to more efficient control activities of the tax administrations of individual Member States.
The cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was also focused on the examination of selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two states.
A total of 40 cases of business transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax subjects were examined, in which there were doubts about their execution, resp. suspicion of VAT evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR found the following facts, among others:
taxable persons have declared in their VAT returns for the purpose of unauthorized acquisition of an excessive VAT deduction the execution of intra-Community transactions which have not actually taken place;
the taxable persons reported intra-Community supplies in the context of carousel transactions, in which there was an intentional multiple reduction in the value of supplies in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their VAT returns and recapitulative statements intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare tax on the goods acquired;
suppliers have made an intra-Community supply of VAT-exempt goods to taxable persons who have not been registered for VAT in another Member State.
In these cases, the supply should not be exempt from VAT and should be subject to tax in the supplier's country;
Suppliers reported intra-Community supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than those reported by the purchasers in intra-Community acquisitions, with in some cases VAT being declared incorrectly.
The findings of the audit showed that VIES provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
In particular, tax administrations should pay increased attention to the thorough examination of differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax proceedings.
The issue of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic and Slovakia to the EU
Value added tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU were abolished.
Until 30 April 2004, the VAT administrator was the relevant financial, resp. the tax office, with the exception of the import of goods and occasional bus transport in the country, where the customs office was the tax administrator.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., On value added tax (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 235/2004 Coll.”), Resp. Act No. 222/2004 Coll., on value added tax (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 222/2004 Coll.”), the VAT administration on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU member states customs offices on the financial, resp. tax authorities.
The delivery of goods in the Czech Republic pursuant to the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of the goods as owner.
A delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is a delivery of goods that have actually been dispatched or transported to another EU Member State.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 64 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. it is an exempt taxable supply with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are supplied to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 8 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll.
The transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the country to another Member State shall also be considered a supply of goods if the goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 43 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., The supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the acquirer is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
By acquiring goods from another EU member state, in the Czech Republic, in accordance with the provisions of Section 16 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods which are dispatched or transported to the acquirer by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech taxpayer purchases goods at a price excluding VAT and is obliged to declare VAT in the Czech Republic in accordance with the provisions of Section 25 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
Acquisition of goods domestically from another EU member state in the Slovak Republic pursuant to the provisions of Section 11 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll. another Member State.
The tax liability in the Slovak Republic arises for the taxpayer when acquiring goods in the country from another Member State pursuant to the provisions of Section 20 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 49 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., The payer may deduct VAT if the tax is applied by him when acquiring goods in the country from another Member State pursuant to the provisions of Sections 11 and 11a of this Act.
According to the provisions of Section 17 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., Resp. § 45 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll., A trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the subject of the trade is the supply of the same goods between these three persons.
Intra-Community transactions are defined as supplies and acquisitions of goods between VAT payers in different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the following table.
VIES system
In order to monitor the exercise of the right to VAT exemption for intra-Community supplies of goods, a VAT information exchange system has been set up within the EU.
It includes the electronic VIES system, which allows the tax administrations of the EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable supply from VAT and, conversely, whether the acquirer duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralized within the EU.
Each Member State is developing its own VIES system.
The national systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU's common communication network, the so-called CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected to the automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as “ADIS”), in the Slovak Republic to the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as “APV DIS”).
These systems use financial, resp. tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and fees.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU member state obtains information about tax entities that it would not be able to obtain on its own without this cooperation.
The main goal of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax loss.
Pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State designates a central unit within the internal organizational structure in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the administration of VAT, the so-called CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, tasks arising from international cooperation are performed by the Ministry of Finance - Central Finance and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in VAT Administration (hereinafter referred to as the “MF CLO”) was established.
The function of the CLO in the Slovak Republic is performed by the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as the “DR CLO”).
Among other things, these departments communicate with foreign EU administrations, especially in the area of ​​information exchange within the VIES system, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax audits, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter "VAT number") registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to verify a certain intra-Community transaction or to obtain other information related to a specific tax entity, they send financial, resp. tax authorities through MF CLO, resp. DR CLO to EU requests for information.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use for the correct assessment of VAT.
Requests for information are usually sent between the CLOs of the EU Member States in electronic form, using a standardized SCAC form.
Selected audit findings when verifying business transactions
The cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was focused primarily on the examination of selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two states and also on the level of use of information obtained in the form of international financial cooperation, resp. tax authorities.
The SAO, CR requested the SAO SR to examine in 30 cases business transactions carried out between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax subjects.
The SAO SR requested the SAO, CR to examine in 10 cases business transactions carried out between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax subjects.
Examination of intra-Community transactions revealed, among other things:
O
The SAO, CR requested the SAO SR to examine the procedure of the tax administrator, to whom a reply to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak Tax Office requested, via the SCAC form, an inspection of the supply of goods (footwear) in the 3rd quarter of 2004 from a Slovak taxpayer in the amount of 2,847,000 CZK. Sk.
The Tax Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech taxpayer stated the acquisition of goods in this value only in the additional VAT return and delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax subjects in the amount of 2,550,000 CZK by the end of 2004. CZK.
Based on the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the locally competent tax office recognized the Slovak supplier's full right to an excessive VAT deduction arising, inter alia, from this supply.
This tax office did not provide information on suspicion of re-export to the tax authorities of the locally competent customers of goods imported back from the Czech taxpayer.
These facts will be an incentive for further investigation of business activities in connection with possible carousel fraud.
O
The Czech tax administrator requested, via the SCAC form, an inspection of the supply of a technological line to the Slovak Republic in the amount of 4,850,000 CZK. CZK in the 2nd quarter of 2004.
The tax proceedings conducted in the Slovak Republic showed that only a part of the technological line, a component in the amount of 3,395,000 CZK, was delivered. CZK were not delivered.
In examining this case, the SAO SR found that the VAT from the taxable supply was declared by the Slovak tax entity from the amount of 4,850,000 CZK. CZK in the tax return for VAT (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO, CR also found that the Czech taxpayer reported an excessive VAT deduction of CZK 655 thousand in the DAP for the said quarter. CZK, which arose from the application of a VAT deduction from the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
Based on the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office came to the conclusion that the Czech and Slovak tax entities established a business relationship for the purpose of unauthorized acquisition of excessive VAT deduction, questioned the taxable supply and did not recognize the Czech taxpayer part of the tax deduction. CZK.
O
In 2004, the Slovak tax administrator requested, via the SCAC form, an inspection of the supply of goods (copiers) to a Czech taxpayer in the amount of CZK 24,246 thousand. SKK made in December 2002.
In November 2002, the Slovak payer purchased these goods in the Slovak Republic from another tax entity in the amount of CZK 29,667 thousand. Sk and subsequently sold it to a Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity claimed an excessive VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
In a tax investigation conducted in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not file a DAP for the 4th quarter of 2002 or for the following period.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak tax administrator, on the basis of the result of the tax audit, did not recognize the right to an excessive deduction in the amount of CZK 5,541 thousand. SKK applied in the DAP for the month 11/2002 and set the tax liability in the amount of 1,750 thous. Sk.
At the same time, this taxable person was not granted an exemption from VAT on exports of goods in December 2002.
O
The Czech tax administrator received an order from the Ministry of Finance CLO to verify the value of the acquired goods for the 3rd quarter of 2004.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to procure goods (diluent) from the Slovak Republic in the amount of 3,767,000 CZK. Sk.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, did not file a DAP and VAT for the months 7 to 12/2004 was assessed ex officio in the amount of CZK 0.
The Czech tax administrator requested, via the SCAC form, a check on whether the deliveries of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic took place, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In response, the Slovak locally competent tax office sent a copy of the invoice, bills of lading and a request for payment of the invoice.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak taxpayer was granted an exemption with the right to deduct VAT on this supply.
The SAO, CR found that the Czech tax administrator evaluated the response to a request for information received from the Slovak Republic as evidence proving that the company acquired goods from another EU Member State.
Based on further investigation, the tax office in the Czech Republic will request a superior body to review the tax liability.
O
The Slovak company supplied goods (chipboard products) to, among others, an American company, which stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free customs zone.
The operator of this free zone was indicated on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased chipboard tiles in the amount of USD 57,600 (at a unit price of USD 100 / piece) from a Slovak payer, which it placed in a free customs zone.
Subsequently, this company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company in the amount of USD 14,400 (unit price USD 25 / piece) and the goods were exported back to the Slovak Republic.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the free customs zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax inspections of individual tax periods in 2004 and 2005 at the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
Verification of completed transactions was requested from the Czech locally competent tax administrators via several SCAC forms.
The individual answers gradually created a picture of trade and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in carousel trade.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO SR, found that in these business relations there was a deliberate gradual several-fold reduction in the value of goods.
Based on the information obtained, the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic concluded that in this case of carousel trade it is free pricing (ie import of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between importer and exporter), which is not an infringement in Slovakia. VAT Act.
Under current legislation, it is not possible to prevent the payment of excessive VAT deductions to export companies, as they meet all the conditions of the law on the exemption of supplies from VAT.
O
As of 12 July 2005, the Czech taxpayer's VAT registration was canceled.
On 27 October 2005, this entity became a taxpayer again on the basis of a voluntarily submitted application for VAT registration.
The Czech tax entity entered in the DAP for the month of 8/2005 (ie the period when it was not a VAT payer) the value of the acquisition of goods (polygraphic printing machine) from the Slovak Republic in the amount of 1,174 thous. CZK and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to the delivery of goods from the Slovak payer in the amount of 1,530 thousand. Sk, which the Slovak payer stated in the DAP as a supply of goods to another EU member state with the right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the said supply via the SCAC form, because the Slovak supplier did not prove how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, CR found that the Czech taxpayer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and does not reside at the address specified in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the locally competent tax administrator in order to verify the data.
O
The Slovak payer stated in the summary report for the 3rd quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods in the amount of 956 thous. SKK to a tax subject from the Czech Republic.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was marked as incorrect by the VIES system.
Verification in the database of payers revealed that such a VAT number was never assigned in the Czech Republic.
According to the invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was an electrical installation work on real estate in the Czech Republic, it was not a supply of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it was registered in the Czech Republic as a VAT payer.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the above facts via the SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic, inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that the tax entity listed on the invoices as a customer was never registered in the Czech Republic as a VAT payer, did not declare tax on services received from a Slovak entity.
No local investigation or tax audit was carried out at the Czech entity, its current residence is not known.
Based on the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity had become a VAT payer by law by accepting the service.
A tax audit will be carried out at the Slovak tax entity for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2004.
O
The Slovak payer stated in the summary report for the 3rd quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods in the amount of 1,055 thous. To the Czech payer.
According to the invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was an electrical installation work on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not a delivery of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the above facts via the SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic, inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found out that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of delivery and a local investigation was carried out to verify the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in 2004 Q3.
Based on this local investigation, it was found that in the given case it was not really the acquisition of goods, but the acquisition of services, which the Czech entity also reported in the regular DAP.
The Tax Office also found that, as a result of a poor procedure in calculating VAT, the Czech entity did not pay the correct amount of VAT for the tax period of the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The taxable person submits an additional DAP.
By asking the locally competent tax office, the SAO SR found out that the Slovak taxpayer had incorrectly stated the provision of the service in the summary report and that a tax audit would be carried out for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2004.
O
The Czech tax entity has voluntarily registered as a VAT payer since March 10, 2004.
In the first quarter of 2004, DAP filed with a high turnover of input and output.
The locally competent tax administrator initiated tax proceedings, the subject did not cooperate with the tax administrator, therefore, due to the suspicion of involvement in the carousel business, he was assessed VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
This DAP has not been submitted by another payer.
Due to non-fulfillment of obligations arising from the law, his VAT registration was canceled on 4 January 2005.
According to the data from the VIES system, in the 3rd and 4th quarters of 2004 this entity had to purchase goods worth 7,846 thousand CZK from the Slovak payer. Sk.
In order to verify the execution of these transactions, the Czech tax administrator sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic.
By asking the locally competent tax office, the SAO SR found out that the executive officer of the Czech company had denied the execution of the audited transactions and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
Based on the tax proceedings conducted in the Slovak Republic, the intra-Community supply to the Czech Republic reported by the Slovak taxpayer was questioned.
The payer will not be recognized as entitled to exemption from VAT and will be assessed VAT on the above amount.
O
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer was to purchase goods (work clothes) from the Slovak Republic in the 1st quarter of 2005 in the total value of 39,970,000 CZK. Sk.
In this quarter, the Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods from another EU member state only in the DAP for the month of 3/2005, in the amount of CZK 11,292 thousand. CZK.
The locally competent tax administrator conducted a local investigation with the subject in order to verify the data in this DAP.
As the company did not submit any documents or otherwise document the realization of taxable transactions, on June 9, 2005, the tax administrator assessed VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
Due to doubts about the acquisition of goods, the tax administrator sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic in May 2005.
According to the reply to the request for information, the tax administrator in the Slovak Republic had doubts regarding the implementation of business cases, as well as the implementation of the payment.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent the DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out at the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated inspection, the locally competent tax administrator carried out further investigations concerning the Czech entity in the Czech Republic, and at the same time an investigation was conducted by the Police of the Czech Republic.
O
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (work clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered them back to the Slovak Republic to payer No. 4 (see Scheme No. 2).
AND)
In the 4th quarter of 2004, the Czech payer No. 2 was to purchase goods (work clothes) in the amount of 4,847 thousand CZK from the Slovak payer No. 1. CZK and in the 1st quarter of 2005 goods in the amount of 17,050 thous. CZK.
Due to the fact that the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the locally competent tax administrator sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic on 25 May 2005.
In its reply, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the execution of business cases and the execution of the payment.
On 8 June 2005, a request for information concerning goods in the amount of CZK 16,575,000 was delivered to the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic. Sk, which was to be delivered in December 2004 by the Slovak payer No. 1 to the Czech payer No. 2.
The Slovak side requested to check whether the Czech payer No. 2 actually accepted the goods, declared them in the DAP and paid VAT.
The official record prepared by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech taxpayer No. 2 has not resided at an address registered in the Commercial Register for a long time.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax period, he filed DAP for a quarterly tax period.
Due to this fact, the Czech tax administrator could not assess VAT.
Execution of a taxable supply between the Slovak payer No. 1 and the Czech payer No. 2 stated in the application in the amount of 16,575 thous. Due to the above facts, it was not possible to verify SKK.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel business in order to draw an excessive VAT deduction.
B)
The Czech payer No. 3, dealing with the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed a DAP for the tax period of months 1 and 2/2005, in which he reported the delivery of goods (work clothes) to the Slovak payer No. 4 in the total value of 21,935 thousand CZK. CZK.
These work clothes were to be purchased by the Czech payer No. 3 from the Czech payer No. 2 in the period from December 2004 to January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, the subject of which was mainly the verification of whether the Slovak payer No. 4 purchased goods from the Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 in the amount of 1,025,000 CZK. CZK and in the 1st quarter of 2005 in the amount of 21,935 thous. CZK.
The reply to this request for information received from the Slovak Republic showed that in the DAP for the month 12/2004 the Slovak payer No. 4 stated zero value of acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for the months 1 and 2/2005 stated the value of acquisition of goods from another EU member state only in the amount of 1,193 thous. Sk.
The Slovak taxpayer No. 4 did not respond to the invitation to submit tax documents for the tax period of the months 10/2004 to 3/2005.
During a local investigation conducted in the Slovak Republic, it was found that the company is not located at the address specified in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer met all the characteristics of a so-called "lost company" and therefore there was a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent the DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out at the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or refute the existence of the goods.
VAT will be assessed according to the result of the survey.
The case is also being dealt with by the Police of the Czech Republic.
The course of the control action
As part of the preparation of parallel audits, a coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants of this meeting got acquainted with the legislation in the field of VAT in both countries and the integration of the electronic system VIES into national databases.
The result of the meeting was the specification of the scope of cooperation and the determination of the conditions for the selection of control samples.
Both parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: a) verification of the validity and accuracy of the VAT number of persons registered for VAT in the Czech Republic, resp. SR in intra-community deliveries; b) verification of data on intra-community acquisitions specified in the DAP of the payer in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as “SH”) of payers from the Slovak Republic contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic on completed business transactions.
It was further agreed that the selection of tax subjects for inspection will be made in connection with the volume of intra-Community supplies between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intra-Community transactions
The procedure of information processing by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the case of intra-Community supply and acquisition of goods is illustrated in the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intra-Community delivery
If the VAT payer makes an intra-Community supply, he is obliged to submit a SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides in the SH summary information on his deliveries of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in the Slovak Republic is obliged to state in the SH the value of goods that were exempt from tax and delivered from the Czech Republic to other EU Member States during the calendar quarter.
Data on the value of delivered goods are always given in SH in Czech, resp. in Slovak currency broken down by individual tax subjects with the indication of their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Data on services are not entered in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds out that he has provided incorrect data in the SH, he is obliged to submit subsequent SHs.
In the event that the payer in the SR finds out that the data stated in the SH were incomplete or incorrect, he shall submit a corrective SH before the expiry of the deadline for the submission of the SH, after the expiry of this period he is obliged to submit an additional SH.
The VIES system enables the exchange of information on the registration data of VAT payers in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic, resp. The Slovak Republic can verify whether the VAT number of the respective acquirer is registered in the given EU Member State.
Data from submitted SH are on MF CLO, resp. DR CLO system VIES grouped according to individual VAT number of acquirers.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each VAT number of the acquirer and the code of the method of performance from all its Czech, resp. Slovak suppliers, so-called L1QD files.
The data from the L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic (from L1QD files) is shown in the following table.
If the VIES system in another Member State detects an erroneous VAT number of the acquirer in the sent L1QD files, it generates a so-called O_MCTL message, which contains all erroneous VAT numbers with the type of error.
This message is then sent to MF CLO, resp. DR CLO.
The O_MCTL message can contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect VAT number, VAT number is not registered in the given state or was never assigned, the acquirer with a certain VAT number was not a VAT payer in the given quarter, VAT registration of the acquirer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, the MF CLO transmits data from received O_MCTL reports to tax authorities.
If the erroneous VAT number of the EU payer is used in one of the sent SH or subsequent SH lines, a so-called "VAT ID Doubt Notification" is generated at the relevant tax office by the ADIS system.
The tax office checks whether the supply has actually taken place to a VAT-registered payer in another EU Member State and records the result of the verification in the system.
In the Slovak Republic, the DR CLO processes all O_MCTL messages in the VIES system and sends them electronically to the locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of taxpayers who have entered an incorrect VAT number in their SH.
The tax authorities then invite the taxpayer to submit an additional SH and state the valid VAT number, resp. When reporting an invalid VAT number in the submitted SH, the tax office will check the delivery of the goods at the relevant payer.
Data on the number of erroneous VAT numbers relating to intra-Community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are given in the following table.
Of the total number of 41,728 VAT numbers of Czech payers listed in the SH of Slovak payers in the period from the 2nd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005, 929 VAT numbers were incorrect, ie 2.23%.
Of the total number of 62,997 VAT numbers of Slovak payers listed in the SH of Czech payers in the same period, 416 were incorrect VAT numbers, ie 0.66%.
When reporting intra-Community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, Czech VAT payers stated in their SH on average less erroneous VAT numbers than payers from the Slovak Republic.
When examining the activities of financial, resp. It was found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of taxable persons in all cases.
E.g.:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the tax entity's registration in the 4th quarter of 2004 at the request of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, an O_MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer's registration in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the registration was terminated on 1 January 2005;
- The SAO SR also found that 6 tax subjects submitted SHs in which the incorrect VAT number was stated, but the O_MCTL reports did not contain this VAT number.
In the Slovak Republic, the filed SH will be transferred to the electronic form at electronic offices and the data from them will be sent to the CL CLO.
After the subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, the DR CLO will send to the relevant tax authorities the so-called breakdowns of errors in the SH submitted by tax subjects for the relevant quarters.
The SAO SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH as of 26 July 2005 (ie data processed before the start of the inspection) and as of 2 February 2006 (ie data processed after the end of the inspection).
The following table compares the data.
From the above data it is evident that the SAO SR audit had an effect not only on the reduction of the number of SHs with incorrect VAT number (by an average of 199 SH per quarter), but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in SH (by an average of 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-Community supplies stated by the payer in the relevant DAP lines is compared with the value of intra-Community supplies stated by this payer in the quarterly SH.
ADIS automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data obtained in determining the tax liability.
The SAO, CR found that the audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values ​​stated in SH and DAP in these cases amounted to 537,231 thousand. CZK.
From the 3rd quarter of 2004, the ADIS system enabled the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values ​​stated in SH and DAP in the amount of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-community supplies according to SH as a conformity and set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-Community supplies in one quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a non-negligible amount, therefore tax administrators in these cases should not set the compliance of SH and DAP without clarifying the reasons for the differences.
E.g. the tax administrator set a match without verification in the event of a difference in values ​​in the amount of 1,561 thous. CZK.
The examination of differences in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was complicated by the fact that SH for each calendar quarter was submitted by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
For taxpayers with a monthly tax period at the time of filing the DAP for the first two months of the calendar quarter, the tax administrators could not compare the values ​​of intra-Community supplies stated in these DAPs with the values ​​according to SH.
In these cases, the tax administrators learned of a possible discrepancy between the data in the DAP and SH only at the time when the tax liability or excessive deduction of VAT was assessed, or returned.
5.1.2 Intra-Community acquisitions
The VIES system provides, among other things, information on the values ​​of intra-Community transactions carried out within the EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, delivered data from SH submitted by payers from other EU member states (delivered L1QD) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the acquisition value stated by Czech payers in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods reported by the payer in the DAP should be in the range of the minimum and maximum recalculated value L1QD (values ​​L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is lower than the value of L1min, a so-called verification order is generated for the payer with the most significant discrepancies.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax subjects and are handed over to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the transmitted data.
The number of verification orders concerning audited financial authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the following table.
The SAO, CR found that the audited tax authorities did not verify inconsistencies in the values ​​of intra-Community acquisitions in 33 cases, to which the received verification orders pointed.
The total difference between the values ​​stated in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases amounted to at least 148,319 thousand CZK. CZK.
The SAO, CR selected 533 files of tax entities for inspection, for which the audited financial authorities received an order from the Ministry of Finance of the CLO for verification.
The inspection revealed the following most common causes of differences between the values ​​stated in the acquirer's DAP and in the supplier's SH: on the acquirer's side (Czech payer) in 263 cases the acquirer did not state the acquisition of goods in the regular DAP in 6 cases the acquirer stated the value of the acquired goods in the wrong line of the DAP, on the part of the supplier (EU payer) in 88 cases EU payers also included in their SH the values ​​of services provided to the Czech payer, of which in 54 cases it was a payer from the Slovak Republic, in 39 cases suppliers included in SH the delivery of goods in a different tax period than acquirers from the Czech Republic to their DAP, in 22 cases suppliers stated incorrect SH Czech VAT number in SH, in 16 cases suppliers stated incorrect values ​​of goods delivery in SH , in 12 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value of goods delivered to the Czech Republic before 1 May 2004, in 5 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value received ch advances.
On the part of payers from the Slovak Republic, the value of provided services was most often incorrectly included in the SH.
54 such cases were detected at the audited tax authorities.
E.g. during the investigation of the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of 10,974 thous. CZK arose from the fact that the Slovak payer introduced to the SH for the 1st quarter of 2005 the provision of services (construction work and delivery of goods, including assembly in the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values ​​of received advances in SH, eg 2 Slovak payers stated in SH received advances from Czech payers, as a result of which an order was generated to verify the difference in the amount of 3,580 thousand. CZK.
Orders to verify the acquired goods are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently a change in the data from the SH in the EU member states, such as a change in the customer of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
As VIES does not automatically draw attention to these changes, the locally competent tax administrator of the acquirer of the goods does not have to know without any other incentive the facts decisive for the correct assessment of the tax liability on the acquired goods and there is a high probability of VAT evasion.
An inspection of the SAO, the Czech Republic revealed that this situation occurred, for example, in the following cases:
The Slovak payer stated in the SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 the value of the delivery of goods for the Czech payer in the amount of 1,504,000 CZK. Sk.
On 1 February 2005, the tax office locally competent to the Czech payer sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, because the Czech payer acknowledged the acquisition of goods only in the amount of 425 thousand CZK. CZK.
Based on the tax proceedings, the Slovak taxpayer filed an additional SH on March 1, 2005, in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand. Sk and by increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from the amount of 194 thous. Sk to the value of 1 160 thous. Sk.
In their SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004, four Slovak payers stated intra - Community deliveries to payers from the Czech Republic in the total amount of 10,240,000 CZK. SKK (ie CZK 8,183 thousand).
However, the Czech acquirers did not report intra-community acquisitions in the DAP.
Based on the international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer who was not listed in the SH submitted by the Slovak payer.
During the 1st quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased the value of intra - Community supplies for this Czech payer by a total of 10,240,000 CZK in additional SH related to the 2nd quarter of 2004. Sk.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in the submitted DAP for the 2nd quarter of 2004, even though the actual acquirer did not fulfill the obligation to declare intra-Community acquisitions for this quarter.
The SAO, CR found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the above-mentioned Czech taxpayer was additionally assessed VAT for tax periods 5 and 6/2004 in the amount of 3,640,000 CZK. CZK and for the 3rd quarter of 2004 in the amount of 3,305 thous. CZK from acquired goods in these periods.
From the above, it is clear that tax administrations had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences caused by errors in the acquirer's DAP, but also differences caused by different reporting of data on intra-Community supply and acquisition in individual EU Member States.
Unification of the conditions for reporting these data would lead to more efficient control activities of tax administrators.
Acquisition of goods in the Slovak Republic
In the Slovak Republic, the APV DIS system makes it possible to compare data on the value of acquired goods obtained through the VIES system from other EU Member States with data specified in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
The method by which the data is compared is called the "MIN-MAX method".
Using this method, the values ​​of deliveries of goods listed in the SH of payers from other EU Member States are converted by the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the relevant quarter.
The MIN-MAX interval will be created, which is used for comparison with the acquisition values ​​of goods stated in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR CLO will send tax administrators information on the values ​​of intra-Community acquisitions stated in the DAP and the values ​​of deliveries from the EU in the VIES system.
The tax administrator will decide for which VAT registered persons the difference will be verified, taking into account other criteria of the risk analysis.
Based on data provided by DR CLO, the SAO SR selected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods for inspection at the inspected tax offices, of which 25 payers also purchased goods from the Czech Republic, for which the highest differences were found between acquisition values ​​obtained from VIES and values ​​declared in DAP.
The SAO SR's inspection confirmed the fact that the tax administrators did not consistently verify the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the accuracy of the data provided in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
As part of the audit, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations at specific tax entities.
During the audit of the SAO SR at the tax authorities, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies, for which the VIES system showed significant differences in MIN-MAX values ​​when acquiring goods from EU member states, the following facts were found, among other things:
In the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not state the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The Tax Office found out that the company from the Czech Republic had incorrectly entered the VAT number of this payer in the SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while the goods in the value of 19,184 thous. CZK in fact delivered to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, in the 4th quarter of 2004 the Slovak company was to acquire goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria in the amount of MIN 682,692 thousand CZK. Sk and MAX 715 105 ths. Sk.
This company filed a DAP for the given periods, in which it stated the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU in the amount of only 480,599 thousand. Sk.
The tax administrator conducted a local investigation, finding that the tax entity purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not indicate intra-Community deliveries according to the date of issue of invoices, but according to the date of delivery.
Due to other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the tax administrator will request a verification of the value of the delivered goods via SCAC forms.
The acquisition of goods from EU member states in the 4th quarter of 2004 was not reported by the Slovak payer in the DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer had to acquire goods worth MIN 11 286 thousand. Sk and MAX 11 845 thous. Sk.
The tax office conducted a local investigation, the inspection showed that the tax entity did not acquire any goods from EU member states in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The SAO SR recommended that the tax office request an inspection of the supply of goods from EU member states via the SCAC form.
The VIES system reported the delivery of goods for a Slovak customer in the amount of MIN 557 thousand. Sk and MAX 565 ths. Sk.
In the DAP for the tax period of months 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not report any acquisition of goods.
Through a local investigation, the tax administrator found out that on 10 December 2004 the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier from the Czech Republic for the material consumed during the repair of the hydraulic loader.
The SAO SR recommended performing a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not complete the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO SR requested the tax administrator to carry out a tax audit of tax subjects.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax audits are submitted by the tax authorities after their implementation by the SAO SR.
These were, for example, the following cases:
The Slovak acquirer did not state in the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004 the acquisition of goods from EU member states and for the tax period of months 10 to 12/2004 it did not declare any tax and claimed a refund of excess VAT deduction in the total amount of 1,236 thousand. Sk.
The tax administrator conducted a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity purchased goods from the Czech Republic in the amount of 683 thousand. EUR (approx. SKK 27,080 thousand).
The mentioned goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čierna nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer issued an invoice for customers in the Russian Federation in the amount of 683 thousand. EUR, which he did not state in the submitted DAP.
The tax administrator performs a tax audit of the tax subject.
The difference between the data on acquisitions stated in the DAP of the Slovak payer for the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005 and the data on deliveries reported by payers from EU member states in individual quarters was in the total amount of 4,800,000 CZK. Sk.
The tax office found that the tax entity purchased goods from suppliers from the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold these goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by export single customs declarations.
The acquisition of goods in the DAP was not reported by the tax subject; according to the company's managing director, the goods were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine in the transit regime.
The taxable person did not submit any VAT records during the local investigation.
A tax audit was initiated at the payer.
5.2 International exchange of L3 level information
The exchange of information at the L3 level is initiated by the locally competent tax administrators, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as “FIFG”) or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as “SPI”) relating to a specific tax entity or transaction via MF CLO, resp. .
DR CLO to another EU member state. The aim of the ŽOI is, for example, to prove the execution of a given transaction within the framework of intra-community services, verification of a certain VAT number, etc.
In the case of SPI, this is the communication of information important to tax administrators in another EU member state.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the SOI was set in Article 8 of this Regulation at 3 months.
The conditions for the admissibility of applications are governed by the Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15 November 2004, which stipulates that, unless the participating States agree otherwise, the FDI must cover commercial transactions of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
If the ŽOI concerns a commercial transaction with a value of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to reply in view of its workload.
The procedure of processing incoming ZOIs by the Tax Administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of internal time limits set for processing at individual organizational levels, is shown in the following diagram.
In the Slovak Republic, the deadline for the settlement of ZOI by the tax authorities was set internally at 2 months so that the three-month deadline pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No. 1798/2003 could be met.
From 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005, the MF CLO received a total of 29 ŽOI and 3 SPI from the Slovak Republic.
Of the 29 accepted ŽOI, 26 (ie 89.7%) were settled within the set period of 3 months and 3 (ie 10.3%) were settled after this period.
In the same period, the DR CLO from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 accepted ŽOI, 64 (ie 90.1%) were settled within the set period of 3 months, 5 (ie 7.0%) were settled after this period (in the remaining 2 cases it was not possible to determine the settlement period from the submitted materials).
More detailed data on the processing time of ŽOI received by MF CLO, resp. DR CLO contains the following graph.
The reasons for sending ŽOI, stated on the SCAC forms, are given in the following table.
Conclusion
International cooperation examined compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and the use of VIES for the exchange of information between EU Member States, in particular in monitoring the exercise of the right to VAT exemption.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intra-Community transactions carried out between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Examination of selected transactions revealed that, based on the international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries revealed cases of companies making fictitious intra-Community business transactions to obtain excessive VAT deductions, as well as cases where purchasers did not declare VAT correctly.
The audit also revealed differences in the processing and use of data from the VIES system by the tax administrations of both countries.
The audit also pointed to problems caused by different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions of goods in different EU Member States.
Unification of the conditions for reporting these data within the EU would lead to more efficient control activities of the tax administrations of individual Member States.
By checking the financial procedure, resp. tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system, it was found that the financial resp. the tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal authorizations.
Furthermore, it was found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on supplies of goods and on the validity of VAT registration of taxable persons in all cases.
The SAO SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with data processed after the end of the inspection.
From the comparison of these data, it was clear that the SAO SR's inspection had an effect not only on reducing the number of SHs with incorrectly stated VAT numbers, but also on reducing the number of uncorrected errors in the SHs.
In the event of discrepancies in the reported data, the SAO SR requested the tax authorities to carry out local investigations, or to carry out tax audits.
The SAO, CR did not have such a possibility within the valid legal regulation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the audits showed that the VIES system provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to control the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Given that there is still room for tax evasion in this area, increased attention needs to be paid to intra-Community transactions in the administration of VAT.
Communique
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Foreword
This information material provides an overview of the course and results of parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of ​​value added and excise duty administration.
The co - operation between the supreme audit institutions of the two countries was carried out on the basis of an agreement on co - operation in control activities concluded in February 2004.
The topic of parallel audits was chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes contribute significantly to the revenues of the state budgets of both countries.
The construction of value added tax, enabling the refund of the excessive deduction, provides scope for tax fraud, resp. leaks.
High rates of excise duties, especially on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by selling these goods illegally.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively throughout the European Union, the VAT Working Group was created by the supreme audit institutions of the member states of the European Union, in the activities of which the supreme audit institutions of both countries are also actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the inspections carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but especially in the joint effort to identify problem areas in the administration of indirect taxes in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The experience and knowledge gained will be used in the planned controls of indirect taxes, focused primarily on the involvement of tax administrations of both countries in the VIES system, which allows to control the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties for the period of 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the procedure of the tax administrator in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On 11.2. In 2004, an Agreement on Cooperation in Audit Activities was concluded between the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO") and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO SR"). The subject of the agreement was cooperation in parallel inspections "Value Added Tax and Excise Duties", included in the SAO's plan of control activities for 2004 under No. 04/07 and "Control of the procedure of the tax administrator in the administration, control and recovery of value added tax". and excise duties ", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO SR under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent specified in the concluded contract and in the preparation of a joint final report on the result of inspections.
In the contract, both parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, the customs administration database and the files of tax entities kept by tax authorities in the Czech Republic and tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the parties could not obtain taxes on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the State concerned.
The inspections were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Czech Republic"), the inspection was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of South Bohemia, North-East Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The auditees were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected tax offices: the Tax Office for Prague 1, the Tax Office for Prague 3, the Tax Office in České Budějovice, the Tax Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Tax Office in Hodonín, the Tax Office in Jihlava, the Tax Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, Financial Office in Kroměříž, Financial Office in Písek, Financial Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, Financial Office in Velké Meziříčí.
The inspection on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SR”) was carried out by the Tax and Customs Administration Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice Branches at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax Office Bratislava for selected tax subjects, Tax Office Bratislava III, Tax Office Trnava, Tax Office Pú-chov, Tax Office Banská Bystrica I, Tax Office Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax Office Žilina I, Tax Office Žilina II, Tax Office Košice I and Tax Office Košice Office IV.
Objective of the inspection
The aim of the inspections was to verify the fulfillment of financial obligations, resp. tax offices and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duties with a focus on the collection of these taxes in the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns on the relevant financial, resp. tax authorities.
The audited periods were 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
As part of international cooperation, the SAO handed over 22,206 items of single customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as "SAD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and the SAO SR handed over 30,221 SAD items from the Slovak customs database.
A comparison of selected SAD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic was performed.
Out of 5,883 selected SAD items from the Czech customs database, a total of 43% of related SAD items were assigned.
Out of 12,343 selected SAD items from the customs database of the Slovak Republic, a total of 26% of related SAD items were assigned.
Based on unallocated items, the SAD was on the financial, respectively. The tax authorities selected the files of tax entities for which the reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
On the basis of the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and financial, resp. In the territory of the other state, the realization of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified.
The SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic performed a joint pilot inspection at the Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma border customs crossing, during which both parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The inspection did not reveal any deficiencies in the records of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation enabled the examination of trade transactions carried out between trading partners from both countries and pointed to shortcomings in the records of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of inspection results
The audit of the SAO and the SAO SR in the area of ​​international cooperation focused on imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, or other types of goods.
Based on the control of files of tax subjects on selected financial, resp. The SAO asked the SAOs to verify the implementation of exports of goods reported at 40 SADs in the total statistical value of CZK 15,301,093 and the SAO of the Slovak Republic to verify the exports in the statistical value of SKK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO SR found out, among other things, the following facts:
- trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic,
- the error rate in entering data into the customs databases made it impossible to identify some imports, resp. exports,
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, corresponding imports to the Slovak Republic were not proven.
In these cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of unduly applying VAT deductions,
- the taxable persons did not comply with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- in financial activities, resp. shortcomings were identified in the administration of value added tax and excise duties and in their cooperation with customs offices.
In the area of ​​value added tax and excise duties, attention will continue to be paid to international trade in order to effectively minimize tax evasion.
It is especially important to improve the activities of tax administrators in the performance of value added tax administration.
The basis of effective control of excise duties is the control of the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information during the import and export of goods.
3. Description of the situation in the field of value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") was levied by the tax or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out in the country and by the customs authorities on the import of goods.
Tax revenues were for financial, resp. tax authorities due to the difference between the collected own tax liability and the refunded excess VAT deductions.
VAT revenues at customs offices were given by the amount of tax collected by them.
In accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, the tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the tax deductions applied to the financial, resp. tax authorities.
For most financial, resp. excessive deductions of VAT exceeded the tax liability of tax authorities.
In terms of state budget revenues, VAT is one of the key taxes, as it accounted for approximately 31% of the Czech state budget revenues in 2003 and approximately 42% of the Slovak state budget revenues.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic in 2003 amounted to CZK 162.9 billion.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT and the refunded excess VAT deductions totaled CZK 231.4 billion.
The total VAT collection in the Slovak Republic in 2003 amounted to SKK 83.8 billion.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected SKK 187.0 billion for VAT, and the refunded excess VAT deductions totaled SKK 103.2 billion.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "SpD") was carried out by the relevant financial, resp. tax authorities and, in the case of imports of products subject to SPD, customs authorities.
The share of SpD in the tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic in 2003 was approximately 16% and in the Slovak Republic approximately 19%.
The total collection of SpD collected in the Czech Republic by financial and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to CZK 85.6 billion and in the Slovak Republic reached SKK 38.0 billion.
4. The course of the control action
The cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was performed;
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel inspections of VAT and SpD was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO SR in April 2003.
