A coordination meeting took place in November 2003, at which, among other things, the selection of commodities was agreed - types of goods that posed a significant risk of compliance with customs and tax regulations: - alcohol and spirits, tariff items 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products , tariff headings Nos. 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff headings and subheadings Nos 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile telephones and their accessories, tariff subheadings 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
Both parties agreed that the selection of tax subjects for control will be made: a) from unallocated items determined by comparing exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, b) from entities carrying out imports and exports regularly or once in large volumes, c) based on findings from inspections carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
In the first stage, the mechanism of mutual allocation of SAD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities in October 2002.
Subsequently, a part of exports from the Czech Republic was compared with imports to the Slovak Republic in 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol or higher; ethyl alcohol and other spirits, denatured, of any strength,
- 2208 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol; spirits, liqueurs and other spirituous beverages,
- 2401 Unmanufactured tobacco; tobacco waste,
- 2402 Cigars, cheroots, cigarillos and cigarettes, of tobacco or of tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other manufactured tobacco and manufactured tobacco substitutes; homogenized or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and essences (essences),
- 8525 20 91 Transmitting apparatus incorporating receiving equipment: For the cellular network (mobile telephones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmitting apparatus incorporating receiving equipment: Other,
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with the apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling within subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
SAD items from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic were assigned to each other on the basis of compliance of individual SAD paragraphs (eg invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle transporting cargo, date of crossing the state border, tariff item, etc.).
The results of the comparison are shown in the following tables and graphs.
The mutual allocation of individual imports and exports was hampered, among other things, by the fact that trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic declared on one export SAD were declared on several import SADs in the territory of the Slovak Republic, or the export SAD had a different number of items from the import SAD.
Other factors that influenced the success of the assignment were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, as well as the time shift between the records of exports in the customs database of one country and the records of corresponding imports in the customs database of another country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples for the audited financial, resp. tax authorities.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that carried out imports, resp. exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, which could not be identified in both databases.
Furthermore, for the verification of business transactions reported in VAT tax returns, some tax entities were selected for which data on imports, resp. exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic were found in both databases.
4.3. Pilot control at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border customs crossing
The border customs crossing for the performance of pilot control was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of unallocated SAD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Based on a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, the use of checklists was introduced at the border customs crossings between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic on 1 June 1998.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion as much as possible, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transport transporting goods of a commercial nature in the customs area and to create conditions for mutual comparison of customs records.
The joint pilot inspection took place from 8 March 2004 to 26 March 2004 and was aimed at verifying this system of customs control.
Procedure for using checklists at the Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma border customs crossing:
1) Weighing the vehicle, issuing a checklist and handing it over to the driver.
2) Parking the vehicle in the marked sector in the parking lot.
Customs hearing in the check-in hall of the Police of the Czech Republic, the Police of the Slovak Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.
The individual check-in was confirmed by the individual components by imprinting a stamp on the checklist.
3) Delivery of the vehicle to the physical inspection area.
Submission of a control sheet, SAD, or other documents to a customs administration employee - control of the performance of all prescribed acts and documents.
Perform a physical inspection by the appropriate components.
Release of the vehicle from the customs area.
Note: When importing goods into the Czech Republic, the weighing of the vehicle was performed directly by employees of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When importing goods into the Slovak Republic, the weighing of the vehicle was performed by employees of an authorized legal entity.
The vehicles were recorded in the computer records after consideration.

4.4. Selected audit findings when verifying business transactions
Within the framework of international cooperation, the implementation of imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified from the documents of customs administrations and financial, resp. tax authorities in the territory of the other state.
The following was verified for selected tax subjects:
- whether the submitted SADs were registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic,
- fulfillment of the legal conditions for the application of the VAT deduction on importation, refund of the excessive VAT deduction and application of the VAT exemption on exportation.
Verification of business transactions revealed:
1. The SAO SR requested verification of the implementation of alcohol exports in the statistical value of SKK 56,989.
The SAO identified in the customs database of the Czech Republic the corresponding imports in the statistical value of CZK 42,624
2. A company engaged in the import and export of photographic equipment and accessories claimed an excessive VAT deduction of CZK 3,740,664 in its VAT return for the month of December 2002.
In order to control reported exports from the Czech Republic, the SAO collected 3 SADs (16 items) with a statistical value of CZK 1,274,822.
The SAO SR identified 3 corresponding import SADs (17 items) with a statistical value of SKK 1,724,321.
VAT was paid in the Slovak Republic to the relevant customs office.
3. In 2002, a company whose object of business was mainly the trade in optical instruments claimed a total excess VAT deduction of CZK 4,136,000 higher than the tax liability.
To verify the reported business activity, the SAO selected an export SAD (32 items) with a statistical value of CZK 7,154,124.
The SAO SR found that this SAD corresponds to the import SAD (12 items) with a statistical value of SKK 9,653,827.
VAT was paid in the Slovak Republic to the relevant customs office.
4. The company dealing, inter alia, with the purchase of goods for resale and resale, did not report any exports of goods in the VAT and tax returns submitted in 2002 and 2003.
According to the Czech customs database, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 totaled CZK 3,439,888.
Based on these facts, the SAO selected 5 export SADs (5 items) for verification with a total statistical value of CZK 669,839.
The SAO SR identified 5 corresponding import SADs (5 items) in the statistical value of SKK 1,012,656.
The SAO SR's inspection at the relevant tax office proved that the declared imports and the payment of VAT had taken place.
5. The company, whose object of business was, inter alia, the purchase of goods for resale and the sale, manufacture, installation and repair of electrical machinery and apparatus, reported in 2002 in VAT tax returns the export of goods in the amount of CZK 12,966,706.
According to the Czech customs database, the total value of exports in 2002 was CZK 14,474,381.
The SAO submitted 17 export SADs (59 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,975,122.
The SAO SR identified 13 SADs (50 items) in the customs database of the SR in the statistical value of SKK 3,621,370.
The customs database of the Slovak Republic failed to identify the corresponding import SAD for 4 export SADs (9 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 399,776.
The relevant tax office in the Slovak Republic verified these imports with the tax subject.
The tax entity listed on the SAD as an importer in the Slovak Republic stated in the minutes of the local investigation that it did not realize the imports declared on the Czech export SADs.
The SAO SR therefore asked the local competent tax office to carry out a tax audit of VAT and corporate income tax for the 2002 and 2003 tax periods.
6. According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, a company engaged in the import and sale of cigarettes exported tobacco labels in 2002 with a statistical value of CZK 7,338,199 and in 2003 with a statistical value of CZK 12,228,545.
In 2002 and 2003, the company did not report any exports in its VAT returns.
The SAO selected 5 export SADs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,471,598 for verification.
For 4 export SADs (4 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,246,860, the SAO SR identified 7 SADs (7 items) with a statistical value of SKK 2,919,514 in the customs database of the Slovak Republic.
In the customs database of the Slovak Republic, it was not possible to assign the corresponding import to the export SAD (1 item) in the statistical value of CZK 224,738.
7. The software company did not report exports of goods in the 2002 and 2003 VAT returns.
According to the Czech customs database, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 and 2003 totaled CZK 1,630,198.
The SAO selected 9 SADs (9 items) for verification in the SR in the total statistical value of CZK 755,588.
In the Customs Database of the Slovak Republic, the SAO SR identified 8 SADs (8 items) with a statistical value of SKK 915,601.
Corresponding imports could not be assigned to the export SAD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 68,286 in the customs database of the Slovak Republic.
In the above cases, it was not possible to identify in the customs database of the Slovak Republic the corresponding imports to 6 SADs in the statistical value of CZK 692,800.
Of which:
- for 2 export SADs from the customs database of the Czech Republic in the statistical value of CZK 293,024, it was not possible to identify the corresponding import SADs in the customs database of the Slovak Republic (see points 6 and 7).
Due to a certain error in entering data into the customs database, it was not possible to identify some registered imports, eg in cases where the importer's name was missing or there was an error in the tax identification number (hereinafter "VAT number").
Therefore, it cannot be stated with certainty that these exports did not take place.
- for 4 export SADs from the customs database of the Czech Republic, imports corresponding to exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic in the statistical value of CZK 399,776 were not proven (see point 5).
In these cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious export of goods for the purpose of unauthorized application of the VAT deduction.
5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services within the control of selected financial, resp. tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to verify the fulfillment of the obligations of tax subjects in the import and export of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between the financial and customs authorities, the audited financial, resp. files of tax subjects are selected by the tax authorities according to the following criteria:
1. tax subjects were selected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic: a) with the highest volume of imports, b) with the highest amount of assessed VAT, c) with the highest volume of exports,
2. from the records of financial, resp. tax authorities were selected by the tax authorities according to the above: a) applied VAT deductions on import, b) applied excessive VAT deductions, c) the right to a refund of the SPD, d) applied exemption from VAT on export,
3. tax entities for which a tax audit has been performed.
The selection of the sample was made regardless of the country of destination, focusing on risky commodities.
5.2. Control findings in the Czech Republic
An overview of imports into the Czech Republic and exports from the Czech Republic for risky commodities in 2002 and 2003 is given in the following table:
5.2.1. Inspection of a selected sample at tax offices
At the audited financial authorities, the SAO focused mainly on:
- the procedure of the tax authorities in verifying the correctness of the VAT declared,
- cooperation between tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the SAD database at tax offices with a focus on the comparison of the declared value, application of the correct VAT rate in connection with the customs classification of goods or services, or comparison of data on the SAD and attached invoices with data in the customs database,
- comparison of data from VAT tax returns on completed and received transactions from abroad with data in the SAD database at tax offices or in the customs database,
- the method of verifying entitlement to the VAT exemption for the export of goods or the provision of services abroad,
- a comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services provided reported in VAT returns with data from the customs database.
The SAD database at tax offices only contained records on those imports and exports for which tax subjects were obliged to state imports or exports in the tax return.
The files of tax subjects were examined at the audited tax offices, which reported in the tax returns for VAT in 2002 and 2003 imports in the total amount of 60,396,379 thousand CZK. CZK and the corresponding VAT in the total amount of 12,644,052 thous. CZK.
Furthermore, the files of tax subjects reporting exports in the tax returns for the years 2002 and 2003 in the total value of 47,323,111 thousand CZK were checked. CZK.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, tax entities in which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic were inspected in 2002 and 2003 carried out imports into the Czech Republic from the Slovak Republic with a total VAT base of 3,759,352 thousand CZK. CZK, VAT in the amount of 767 607 thous. CZK and exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic with a total statistical value of 1,989,090 thous. CZK.
The detected differences between the records in the SAD database at the tax authorities and in the customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- SAD items that were missing in the Czech customs database were requested directly from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- for SAD items that were missing from the tax office database, it was verified that they were not canceled documents,
- for SAD items for which different values ​​were found between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of tax authorities, the relevant SAD was requested at the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic in writing, including the attached invoices.
During the examination, it was found that the SAD database at tax offices did not contain, for example, records on import SADs in the total value of VAT of 3,622 thousand CZK. CZK and records on export SADs in the total statistical value of 9,359 thous. CZK.
5.2.1.1. Identified differences
A comparison of the SAD database at tax offices and the cumulative tax obligations for 2002 and 2003 in VAT returns for a selected sample of tax entities revealed the following differences:
The differences in values ​​were mainly caused by:
- The time lag between the realization of imports and the exercise of the right to deduct VAT assessed on the import of goods.
The tax subject could claim the right to deduct tax on the import of goods within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the goods were released into the relevant regime, respectively. in the case of a temporary importation scheme, no later than 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the scheme was terminated.
- The time lag between the realization of the export and the moment when the tax subject received the SAD.
The taxable person was obliged to state data on realized exports exempted from the obligation to apply output tax in the VAT return at the earliest for the tax period in which the goods left the country, if he also had a tax document, which was the SAD.
- Failure of taxpayers to fulfill their obligations when reporting imports and exports in VAT tax returns.
In some cases, taxable persons did not provide correct data on imports and exports in their VAT returns.
Due to the fact that tax subjects did not have to attach SAD lists to the submitted VAT tax returns, it was difficult for the tax authorities to control the right to deduct VAT or exemption from VAT.
5.2.2. Cooperation between financial and customs authorities
During the period under review, import or export duties and VAT were repaid or remitted on the basis of a decision of the customs authorities.
Tax entities were obliged by law to reduce the previously claimed right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax refunded by the customs office, in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation regulated the sending of information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT from customs offices to tax offices.
Some audited tax offices received this information, but irregularly or with a significant time lag, and only from some customs offices.
One audited tax office did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the data needed to check compliance with the legal obligation of tax entities.
In 2002, the customs authorities refunded VAT in the amount of more than CZK 319 million and in 2003 in the amount of over CZK 398 million.
The results of the audit pointed to persistent shortcomings in the activities of tax administrators, some systemic errors in the cooperation of tax authorities with customs authorities and non-compliance with certain obligations of taxpayers filing tax returns for VAT and SpD.
Weaknesses were identified in the administration of VAT and SpD, especially in the following areas:
a) upon cancellation of VAT registrations, the fulfillment of the payers' obligation to pay VAT on commercial property registered or which should have been registered on the day of cancellation of the registration, for which the payer claimed tax deduction, was verified only sporadically,
(b) the tax authorities have not consistently exercised the possibility to carry out a tax audit or a local investigation.
In some cases, this led to insufficient verification of the legitimacy of the right to deduct VAT,
c) the official records and minutes of the oral proceedings did not contain all the necessary information to substantiate the excessive VAT deductions applied,
(d) the tax authorities did not sufficiently verify the imports and exports reported in the VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in the SR
5.3.1. Inspection of a selected sample at tax offices
For a selected sample, the SAO SR verified or the tax office performed a tax audit for the tax periods of 2002 and 2003.
After analyzing the submitted tax returns and applications for tax refunds at selected tax entities, the SAO SR requested the tax office to provide the relevant SADs documenting imports and exports, invoices and documents for tax payment.
Subsequently, the SAO SR checked whether the submitted SADs are registered in the customs database of imports and exports and fulfillment of decisive facts and legal conditions when applying the input tax deduction for import, when refunding excessive VAT deduction, when applying exemption from export tax and when refunding SpD.
The SAO SR verified selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the SR and the CR at 10 audited tax offices in the structure according to the number of SAD items and the sum of statistical values ​​given in the following table.
In total, imports in the statistical value of SKK 856.2 million were checked, which represents 5.11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic to the SRO.
Exports of selected commodities were checked in the total statistical value of SKK 176 million, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white goods, packaging technology and software) from EU countries to the Slovak Republic were inspected in the total statistical value of SKK 532.8 million.
5.3.2. Cooperation between tax and customs authorities
During its inspection at the tax authorities, the SAO SR found discrepancies between the data registered in the customs database of the Slovak Republic and the data reported in specific VAT tax returns, eg:
- 2 tax subjects (natural persons) stated in tax returns imports of goods in the total value of SKK 1,589,261, on the basis of which they claimed the right to a refund of excessive VAT deductions.
During local investigations carried out at the initiative of the SAO SR, the tax subjects were unable to prove to the tax office the legitimacy of the application of input tax with the relevant documents on the implementation of imports and payment of VAT,
- the tax subject (s. r. o.) declared in the tax return for the tax period January 2003 the received taxable performance in the amount of SKK 77,167,576, the export of goods in the amount of SKK 18,006,041 and claimed an excessive VAT deduction in the amount of SKK 17,157,101.
The VAT tax returns filed for 2003 show that the difference between the volume of purchases and exports in the amount of SKK 59,161,535, which arose in January 2003, was not settled throughout 2003.
In the above-mentioned cases, the SAO SR requested the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of the applied excessive VAT deductions.
- in another case, a tax entity (s. r. o.) for the tax period January to June 2002 stated in VAT tax returns the export of goods in the total value of SKK 87,199.
Verification in the customs database of the Slovak Republic revealed that the tax entity carried out exports in the mentioned period in the statistical value of SKK 296,747.
The tax office conducted several local inquiries at the company 's headquarters, finding that the company' s managing director (a UK citizen) had traveled and the company had left the leased premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of the SAO SR's inspection, the tax administrator submitted a notification to the authorities involved in criminal proceedings on suspicion of committing a criminal offense of non-payment of tax.
Based on the results of inspections at selected tax offices, the SAO SR states that the biggest problems in the performance of administration and control of VAT and SpD occurred mainly in the following areas:
- non-use of the possibility to carry out VAT tax audits of problematic tax subjects, especially in cases of application of a high value of excessive VAT deductions,
- the tax audit reports did not contain a list of audited documents
- SAD for imports and exports of goods,
- insufficient verification of reported imports and exports of goods in tax returns,
- lengthy proceedings of tax administrations in issuing decisions, especially in the context of assessment proceedings, also with the consequence of the expiry of the right to impose sanctions,
- non-compliance with legal conditions in the provision of tax deferrals,
- non-compensation of VAT arrears within the period for refunding the excess VAT deduction,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and enforcement of tax arrears.
Based on the inspection of the identified deficiencies, the SAO SR requested the relevant tax authorities to perform a VAT tax audit focusing on the justification of the applied excessive VAT deductions for 14 tax entities.
Measures were taken at all audited tax offices to eliminate the deficiencies identified during the inspection, the fulfillment of which will be monitored and controlled by the SAO SR.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation enabled the examination of trade transactions carried out between trading partners from both countries and pointed to shortcomings in the records of imports and exports.
The result of the inspections was also the finding of persistent deficiencies in the fulfillment of obligations of VAT and SpD payers, in financial activities, resp. tax authorities, in a system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs administrations, which ultimately reduced the efficiency and effectiveness of tax controls.
The findings also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have at their disposal basic data on imports and exports from the customs database of the Czech Republic within the tax information system. In the Slovak Republic, there is no similar system for transmitting information on imports and exports of goods between the customs and tax administration.
The procedure for verifying the performance of the VAT and SpD administration was not the same due to different legal regulations and conditions in the territory of both states.
The SAO verified the necessary data from information obtained from the customs administration of the Czech Republic and from documents available at the audited financial offices. The SAO SR verified the execution of business transactions from the documents of tax subjects requested through the tax authorities.
If irregularities were found, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax audits.
The parallel inspections carried out in the area of ​​VAT and SPD assessed the state of administration of these taxes in the period before accession to the European Union and pointed to the need for further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further deepened in the control of financial activities, resp. tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT law.
One of the new obligations related to the delivery of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of a so-called summary report.
This declaration must be submitted by all VAT payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax administrators are obliged to enter data from summary reports into the VIES (VAT Information Exchange System) system, to which tax administrators from the Member States of the European Union have access.
Financial, resp. the tax authorities then have the opportunity to compare these data with the data stated in the submitted VAT tax returns.
This system is also used to verify the validity of the VAT number of persons registered for VAT, to verify the legitimacy of the applied VAT exemption when delivering goods to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel audits showed the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR.
The results of these inspections will be confronted with the outputs of the planned inspections, which will, among other things, focus on examining the VIES system, which is intended to prevent tax evasion in so-called "intra-Community supplies".
Given the importance of VAT and SPD for budget revenues, control activities need to focus primarily on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion on indirect taxes.
Communique
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the results of inspections in asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic
State property and financial resources intended to ensure the activities of the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior
Inspection Action No. 04/23 "State property and financial resources intended for securing the activities of the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior"
Inspection Action No. 15/2004 "Control of the management of state property and funds intended for the provision of asylum and temporary refuge to foreigners in the Slovak Republic"
1. Introduction
Population migration is one of the phenomena that have a global character and have become an integral part of the current development stages of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
It is mainly due to the flight of citizens from their country of origin or last permanent residence from persecution, in particular for racial, religious, national, political, as well as the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their goal is to obtain asylum and integration into society, especially in some of the developed democratic countries in Europe.
A large group also includes foreigners whose reason for migration is unfavorable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The establishment of specific principles for aid to refugees has already led to the adoption of the 1951 Geneva Agreement and the 1967 New York Protocol on the Status of Refugees, which the governments of the signatory countries have undertaken to apply in their foreign policy orientations.
The Czech and Slovak Federal Republic ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the split in 1993, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to comply with the adopted international documents and confirmed their binding nature within the framework of national legislation by a legal act.
Both republics have enshrined the provision of asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic focused on the asylum process and related issues, the results of which are contained in the joint final report.
The co - operation between the supreme audit institutions of the two countries was carried out on the basis of the "Agreement on Co - operation in Control Activities" (hereinafter referred to as the "Agreement") concluded in April 2004.
In the Treaty, both parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing asylum procedures in the other Contracting Party, selected statistics on the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The aim of the parallel control action was to identify the same problem areas and to point out the consequences that follow from this for the area of ​​population migration.
The co-operation consisted in the unification of the program of control actions, in the exchange of information to the extent stipulated by the Treaty and in the preparation of a joint final report on the result of controls.
At the first joint meeting, which took place on 5.4. to 7.4.2004, identical areas of audited issues and control procedures in the preparation of audits were determined.
At the second meeting, which took place on 28.6. to 30.6. 2004, common points for the control program were specified.
At the third joint meeting, which took place during the inspection on 8.11. to 10.11.2004, there was an exchange of experience from ongoing inspections.
The forms of outputs from inspections were specified and the structure and content of the joint final report, which was prepared on 14.2. to 17.2. 2005 at the last joint meeting.
The inspections were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by inspectors of the Department of Defense and Security and selected territorial departments.
The inspected persons were the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as the "MoI") and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as the "SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic, the inspection was carried out by the Defense, Interior and State Offices Section.
The audited entity was the Migration Office of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "MA").
The audited period was 2001, 2002, 2003 (hereinafter the audited period).
In some cases, statistics for a longer period of time are also used in the joint report.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. Evaluation of control activities
The subject of the parallel inspections was: - asylum process, - asylum facilities, - management of financial resources and state property, - internal control system.
The mutual exchange of experience gained between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic took place in the phase of preparation and implementation of audits.
This exchange made it possible to more thoroughly evaluate the submitted documents, to analyze the causes of the identified differences in the provision of the asylum process.
Thus, it was possible to focus on the crucial problems affecting the operation of asylum facilities.
Ultimately, this had a positive effect on the quality of control activities.
2.2 Summary of inspection results
The harmonization of the asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with the documents of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as the "EU") was the subject of evaluation reports of the European Commission on the readiness of both countries to join the EU.
The adoption of legislation in this area continues after the accession of both countries to the EU with the aim of further harmonization with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has a constantly growing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security to asylum seekers in accordance with international agreements.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditures drawn from the state budget of both countries is influenced mainly by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the granting or non-granting of asylum, and also the health status of the applicants.
The amount of some selected benefits is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of participants in asylum proceedings.
During the stay of asylum facilities, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, meals, health care and basic material equipment and hygiene needs.
At the same time, courses are organized as part of leisure activities and conditions are created for applicants for cultural and sports activities.
Asylum facilities include reception centers and residence centers, and in the Czech Republic also integration centers.
The cost per day depends on the occupancy and facilities of the center and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is basically stabilized.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1,000 jobs in the next two years.
The aim is to create the conditions for applicants, the growing number of which is expected to continue in the coming years in connection with the application of the Dublin Convention.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of approved budget expenditures was spent on the provision of services. The decisive expenditures of this item were expenditures on accommodation and meals for applicants in asylum facilities operated on the basis of a contract, expenditures on health care provided to asylum seekers and costs for a permanent security service ensuring the protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditures on salaries, payments for work performed and insurance premiums also contributed significantly to total expenditures.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the migration policy and asylum process was marked by many budgetary measures that addressed the legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditures on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, expenditures on materials and services and expenditures on security services contributed decisively to the use of current expenditures.
The results of the inspection in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic pointed out some similar shortcomings which did not have a significant impact on the financial management and management of state property.
These were shortcomings, especially in the area of ​​using state budget funds, contrary to the purpose for which they were intended by the State Budget Act, when actions having the character of technical improvement of tangible fixed assets were covered from current expenditures.
The law on accounting in the area of ​​inventory and non-compliance with the chart of accounts was also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were also found in the management of state property when it was left for use to another person without a contract.
Failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in the data of the Real Estate Cadastre violated the Real Estate Cadastre Act, and by leaving waste to be disposed of to a person who was not a person authorized to dispose of waste, the Waste Act was violated.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings were also found in the provision of disproportionately high advances for electricity and natural gas consumption, shortcomings in the award of public contracts and in the management of state property, when its registration was not sufficiently ensured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not proven.
The internal control system was ensured in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic in the sense of valid generally binding legal regulations that regulate the method of performing financial control.
No deficiencies were found in the submitted written documentation.
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, despite some shortcomings identified, evaluate positively the approach of SUZ and MÚ in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the findings of the audit, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic state that despite the significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the relevant organizational units of both countries have .
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the inspection were discussed with the interested statutory representatives of the relevant organizational units of the state on the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the audit, we recommend that the positive methodological experience from the audit be used in other joint control events within the framework of international cooperation of supreme audit institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, the right of asylum is based on the Geneva Convention of 1951 (Convention relating to the Status of Refugees and the related New York Protocol of 1967).
The first legal regulation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll., On Refugees.
In the Czech Republic, Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On Asylum and on the Amendment of Act No. 83/1991 Coll., On the Police of the Czech Republic, has been in force since 1 January 2000.
This Act has been amended a total of five times (Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. And Act No. 222/2003 Coll. .).
Two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On Asylum, are currently in the legislative process, and the adoption of further amendments will be linked to European legislation.
At the time of drafting Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On asylum, the area of ​​asylum was part of the 3rd pillar of the EU and asylum documents were political documents in terms of binding force.
Already in the adoption of this law, there was an effort to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A significant change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of asylum issues from the 3rd to the 1st pillar, when the right of asylum became a part of Community law from 1.5. 1999 on the basis of the Amsterdam Treaty.
This shift has created the need to create appropriate legislation, ie. create legal instruments in appropriate legal force.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key Community regulations in the field of asylum were adopted shortly before or only after the accession of the Czech Republic to the EU, and their transposition deadline at the time of the Supreme Audit Office's inspection had not yet expired.
After their implementation into the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission of the manner in which it has transposed it.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure of state authorities in proceedings on granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary refuge in the Slovak Republic was established with effect from 1 January 1996 by Act No. 283 of the National Council of the Slovak Republic. / 1995 Coll., On refugees.
Since 2003, the Act on Refugees has been replaced by Act No. 480/2002 Coll., “On Asylum and on Amendments to Certain Acts, which incorporated the harmonization of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with the Council of Europe Directive 2001/55 / ​​EC of 20 July On minimum standards for providing temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote a balance of efforts between Member States in receiving such persons and bearing the consequences thereof.
After two amendments to Act No. 480/2002 Coll., On Asylum, in 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which means further harmonization of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU legislation in the area of ​​migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the determination of the obligation for asylum seekers to attend a basic Slovak language course during their stay in the integration center, the appointment of a guardian by courts for minors who remain in the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, enabling applicants to enter into employment in the amendment to the law.
The harmonization of the law of the Slovak Republic with the EU law in the area of ​​migration and the asylum process was assessed in the regular reports of the European Commission on the readiness of the Slovak Republic to join the EU.
In 2002, the report drew attention to the insufficient staff capacity of the Municipal Authority, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, matters concerning refugees have been the responsibility of the Ministry of the Interior.
With effect from 1 January 1996, the Ministry of the Interior set up an organizational unit of the SUZ state. The reason was the separation of the performance of state administration in the area of ​​the asylum procedure, which is performed through the Department of Asylum and Migration Policy of the Ministry of the Interior, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of SUZ is to provide the Ministry of the Interior with the provision of accommodation, catering, health and other services to participants in asylum proceedings and asylum seekers.
In the Slovak Republic, the Municipal Authority performs decisive tasks in the area of ​​the asylum process, especially in terms of financial and material and technical support of the asylum process to the extent defined by special regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to deciding on the applications of foreigners for asylum in the first instance of administrative proceedings and the comprehensive operation of asylum facilities in the area of ​​accommodation, catering, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, it prepares concepts for the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the field of creating an asylum system in the Slovak Republic in recent years have been significantly influenced by cooperation and support from the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (hereinafter "UNHCR").
A special benefit was his financial participation in the reconstruction of the housing stock for asylum seekers.
UNHCR also co-financed social, cultural and sporting activities for applicants.
4.1 Development of the number of asylum seekers and results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the graph.
There was a significant increase in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis, and in 2003 there was an increase in the number of refugees from Chechnya.
An overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic is given in Table 1.
During the audited period, a total of 394 cases were granted asylum, of which 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
During the audited period, asylum was not granted in a total of 22,731 cases and in 22,636 cases the asylum procedure was terminated.
Number of participants in the proceedings as of 1.1. it includes both persons to whom a decision has not yet been issued and those to whom the decision has not been transmitted.
Also included are persons who have been forgiven for missing the deadline for filing an appeal, or for whom the previous decision has been annulled and a new one has not yet been issued.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers is constantly growing.
If in 1993 96 applicants were registered, in 2003 it was already 10,358 persons.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, when 8,131 applicants were registered, which represented an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1,556 persons applied for asylum.
Data on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic in the audited period are given in Table 2.
In the audited period, a total of 49 asylums were granted and their number did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants in individual years.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
Asylum proceedings were discontinued in a total of 23,088 cases.
The majority of applicants, by staying without a permit, stayed outside the asylum facility voluntarily left the asylum procedure before its termination.
In 2002 it was more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and in 2003 it was more than 94% of persons.
The length of stay of one applicant in one of the asylum facilities, converted to the average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The findings of the Ministry of Interior also show that the majority of applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic are looking for better living conditions, ie so-called economic migration, which has no support in documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic has signed up.
In these cases, the asylum system is purposefully used by the applicant.
An asylum application based on economic reasons, such as seeking employment or better living conditions, is not a ground for granting asylum.
Such a request should be in accordance with the provisions of § 12 par. 1 letter a) of Act No. 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, assessed as manifestly unfounded and should be decided on within 30 days.
Internationally recognized principles for identifying economic migrants have not yet been established to distinguish them from applicants persecuted in their country of origin and to speed up the asylum process.
Given the above facts, it can be stated that the Slovak Republic is a transit country in terms of international migration and the destination countries for migration were and still are Western European countries.
Following accession to the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement designating the State responsible for examining applications for asylum lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents the submission of multiple targeted asylum applications in several EU countries.
Applicants shall return to the country of first registration after a positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak Republic is part of the external borders of EU countries, therefore the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to create conditions for residence in the Slovak Republic until a decision on granting or not granting asylum is issued.
4.2 Drawing funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security to asylum seekers in accordance with international agreements and national legislation based on them.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditures drawn from the state budget is influenced primarily by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision on granting asylum, as well as their state of health.
The growing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher uptake of statutory benefits for applicants, such as food, pocket money, basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some selected benefits is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, in the audited period, the meal allowance was CZK 58 per person per day, out-of-pocket allowance CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child under 15 years of age.
The costs per asylum seeker per day of stay were on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to the out-of-pocket allowance, asylum seekers accommodated in self-catering accommodation centers and privately accommodated applicants outside asylum facilities may be granted a contribution up to the subsistence level.
Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On asylum, as amended, grants, among other things, in § 84 to municipalities the right to a contribution to cover costs incurred in connection with an asylum facility in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was determined annually by government resolutions and in the audited period was CZK 7 per person per day of stay.
At the same time, municipalities are granted the right to a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
The amount of the contribution in the audited period was CZK 120 per pupil and month, provided that in the given month the person in question attended school for at least 10 days.
In the Slovak Republic, in the audited period, the meal allowance was SKK 70 per person per day, out-of-pocket allowance SKK 12 per person per day and SKK 8 per child under 15 years of age.
The costs per asylum seeker per day of stay were on average SKK 442 in 2001, SKK 447 in 2002 and SKK 445 in 2003.
In accordance with Act No. 480/2002 Coll., On Asylum, municipalities in whose territory an asylum facility is located are provided with a contribution for partial reimbursement of expenses incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and operation of an asylum facility.
So far, municipalities have only partially used the opportunity to apply for a contribution, which is set at SKK 1,500 per bed and calendar year.
National legislation in both countries sets a 90-day period for issuing an asylum decision from the commencement of the asylum procedure, and at the same time allows for an extension of this period in justified cases.
The most common reason for extending the asylum procedure, which affects the amount of state budget expenditures, is the filing of appeals against decisions not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued in the interval between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days from the date of submitting the application for asylum (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum proceedings initiated in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year of their initiation.
Within a period of two years from the commencement of the asylum procedure, 92% of the asylum applications were finally decided.
In the Slovak Republic, according to the data of the Municipal Office, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum use the statutory possibility of extending the time limit by filing an appeal with a court.
In some cases, it was an extension of more than a year, and the court proceedings were not closed at the time of the inspection.
Some contribution to the shortening of the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of joint offices of the Municipal Office and the Border and Alien Police Office of the Police Force in the reception centers in Adamov-Gbelo, Opatovská Nová Ves and Liptovský Vlachy, which took place at the time of inspection from 1.10.2004.
This presupposes a simplification of procedures and a shortening of the time limits for proceedings between the two components of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have set up asylum facilities in which they have gradually created suitable conditions for the provision of services to participants in asylum proceedings.
During the stay, asylum seekers are provided with accommodation, meals, health care, pocket and basic material equipment and hygiene needs.
At the same time, courses are organized as part of leisure activities and conditions are created for applicants for cultural and sports activities.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
SUZ manages and operates asylum facilities and is competent to manage state property in the areas of the reception center Vyšní Lhoty, reception and residence center Červený Újezd, residence centers Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka u Brna, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the buildings of integration asylum centers Jaroměř and Stop near Brno.
At the beginning of 2002, a reception center was established in the transit area of ​​Prague-Ruzyně Airport.
SUZ also ensures the operation of asylum facilities in Stráž pod Ralskem, Seč, Bruntál, Zbýšov and Kašava, which are operated by a legal entity on the basis of Section 80 (3) of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On Asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of the reception centers is 747 places and the total accommodation capacity of the residence centers is 1,977 places.
Reception centers are closed facilities that asylum seekers may not leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic reception procedures specified in Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On Asylum, have been performed.
Violation of the obligation to stay in the reception center is considered a misdemeanor.
The accommodation centers to which asylum seekers come from the reception centers are used to accommodate asylum seekers until the decision on their application for granting or not granting asylum takes legal effect.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers have the opportunity to leave the residential centers, or to stay in private.
Asylum seekers shall be entitled to free accommodation, meals, other services and out-of-pocket expenses at reception and residence centers where they are registered, provided that they have undergone the necessary steps to establish their financial and financial situation, and such conditions shall be that they cannot be fairly demanded of even partial payment for the said services.
Integration asylum centers are used for temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the center on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months with the possibility of extension until they manage to secure adequate housing for them, or they can provide it themselves within the state integration program.
In the integration center, clients pay for all accommodation costs and eat individually.
Persons with recognized refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Costs of asylum facilities
For the comparison of asylum facilities, it was chosen as the best telling indicator of the amount of costs per physical day of stay.
It is based on the actual number of persons who were actually provided with the services provided by the asylum facility each day.
In Table No. 3 and in the graph, the facilities operated by SUZ are marked as own and the facilities operated by legal entities on the basis of Section 80 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., On Asylum, as contractual.
The cost of one day of stay in SUZ's own asylum facility decreases with the increasing occupancy of these facilities. The reason is that the fixed costs of operating the facilities are budgeted for more asylum seekers.
The volume of total costs incurred in providing services for asylum seekers increases in direct proportion to their increasing number.
In 2001 and 2003, applicants in crisis facilities were accommodated in their own asylum facilities.
In part of 2003, extraordinary accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was even used to address the capacity crisis of asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of Chechen nationals from Poland.
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
Expenditures per applicant per day of stay were then lower in these years.
However, long-term maintenance of the high occupancy of these devices is not possible.
The risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the associated need for higher accommodation capacity need to be taken into account.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments when the accommodation capacity is fully occupied.
The form of asylum facilities operated under contract enables the adoption of operational solutions in the area of ​​asylum facilities capacities, if necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centers and accommodation centers.
The Municipal Administration manages the Adamov-Gbely, Rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and Brezová pod Bradlom residential centers.
The total capacity of the reception centers is 470 seats and the residence center 100 seats.
The growing number of asylum seekers was addressed by the Municipal Office by establishing a residence center in Gabčíkov in the leased premises of the Slovak University of Technology in Bratislava with a flexible available capacity from 250 to 940 places.
According to the concluded contract, the lessee also provides services related to the operation of the center.
In this way, the Municipal Office addressed the lack of its own staff.
The residential center was also temporarily established in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jaziercie with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centers had an average occupancy rate of 57% to 62% in the audited period, and an average of 33% to 50% occupancy centers in the audited period.
Occupancy varied according to the season and was highest in the last months of the year, when he applied for asylum by a much larger number of applicants compared to other months of the year.
A further increase in accommodation capacity by approximately 450 places will be possible after the reconstruction of the resorts in Opatovská Nová Ves and Vlachy.
After the completion of the center in Humenné in 2006, the number of seats will increase by another 550 people.
5.2.1 Costs of asylum facilities
Data on the amount of costs for the operation of asylum facilities are given in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another entity that will provide premises and ensure the operation of the facility, including related activities, is one of the ways to ensure at reasonable cost the tasks arising from the stay of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic.
6. Management of financial resources and state property
6.1 Management analysis
In the Czech Republic, the approved budgeted expenditures of SUZ in 2001 were increased by thirteen budgetary measures by 103,077 thous. CZK.
Of which 89 979 ths. CZK (87.29%) were earmarked funds. The majority was intended to address the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (CZK 44,538 thousand) and to provide health care provided to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870 thousand).
In 2002, SUZ expenditures were increased by twenty budget measures by 88,362 thousand CZK. CZK.
Of which 62 282 ths. CZK (70.48%) were earmarked funds, of which the majority (CZK 53,200,000) was earmarked for health care provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, SUZ expenditures were increased by fourteen budgetary measures by a total of 88,078 thousand CZK. CZK.
Of which 82,000 thous. CZK (93.09%) amounted to earmarked funds released from the General Treasury.
Amount 51 000 ths. CZK was intended for health care provided to asylum seekers, 24,000 thous. CZK to address the influx of Chechen refugees and 7,000 thous. CZK for the program of humanitarian evacuations of the disabled population of the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the drawing of selected SUZ expenditures in the audited period is given in Table 5.
From the above overview, it is clear that the highest part of the expenditure was spent on the provision of services.
The amount of expenditures on the purchase of services ranged from 37.07% to 38.23% of total expenditures.
Explosive expenditures in this item were expenditures on accommodation and meals for applicants in asylum facilities operated on the basis of a contract, expenditures on medical care provided to asylum seekers and costs for permanent security services providing security in individual asylum facilities.
Expenditures on salaries, payments for work performed and insurance premiums contributed significantly to the total expenditures of SUZ (23.99% - 24.97%).
Last but not least, purchases of materials accounted for a significant share of SUZ's total expenditures (approximately 14%), with food purchases accounting for the highest share (7.61%? 9.83% of total expenditures).
In the Slovak Republic, the budget management of the Municipal Office for the provision of migration policy and the asylum process was marked by several budgetary measures that addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
The draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure part was characterized in particular in 2001 and 2002 by an imbalance between the requirements of the Municipal Office, which was based on an increase in the number of asylum seekers and the need to finance their legal entitlements, and the resources provided.
During the year, the administrator of the budget chapter addressed the disproportion through several budgetary measures, which increased the limit of current expenditures in 2001 by 41.8% and in 2002 by as much as 71.7%.
An overview of the drawing of selected expenditures of the Municipal Authority in the audited period is given in Table No. 6.
Expenditures on wages, salaries and insurance premiums in the range from 24.47% to 30.51% and expenditures on materials and services in the range from 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditures contributed decisively to the drawing of current expenditures.
Expenditure on security services accounted for more than 10% and expenditure on food purchases from 3.92% to 7.20%.
Another significant part was represented by expenditures for accommodation and catering services with a share from 10.82% to 26.96%.
A relatively low share in the range from 1.03% to 6.25% was accounted for by capital expenditures.
6.2 Identified deficiencies
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic pointed out some similar shortcomings which did not have a significant impact on the management of state funds and property.
These were shortcomings in particular in the following areas: a) the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were intended by the State Budget Act, when actions having the character of technical improvement of tangible fixed assets were covered from current expenditures; b) violation of the Act on Accounting in the field of inventories and non-compliance with the indicative chart of accounts.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were also found in the management of state property, when it was left for use to another person without a proper contract; the Act on the Real Estate Cadastre was violated by failing to meet the deadline for reporting changes to the data of the Real Estate Cadastre; by leaving the waste for disposal to a person who was not a person authorized to dispose of waste, the Waste Act was violated.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings were also found in the provision of disproportionately high advances for electricity and natural gas consumption, shortcomings in the award of public contracts and in the management of state property, when its registration was not sufficiently ensured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not proven.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, as of 1.7. In 2002, an internal control system was introduced in the sense of the provisions of Act No. 320/2001 Coll., On financial control, determining the competencies of individual employees responsible for performing preliminary, ongoing and subsequent control.
At the same time, an internal audit system was introduced and the internal auditor of SUZ was appointed.
Every year, SUZ issues a plan of financial, social and operational technical inspections, the aim of which is a comprehensive verification of the management of financial resources and state property in individual asylum facilities managed by SUZ.
In 2002, 42 management checks were carried out and in 2003 54 were carried out.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct performance of control activities in the departments and organizations of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic in terms of compliance with generally binding legal regulations and internal regulations is ensured by the Office of Control of the Minister.
Within the audited period, no control of the fulfillment of tasks in the area of ​​asylum policy was performed.
The internal control system of the Municipal Authority is focused primarily on the implementation of preliminary and ongoing financial control pursuant to Act No. 502/2001 Coll., On Financial Control and Internal Audit.
The performance of financial control is also regulated by the internal regulations of the Director of the Municipal Authority.
The factual focus of control activities as part of the management of individual departments was set within the annual plan of the Municipal Authority.
The directors of the unions were appointed to be responsible for carrying out inspections in this area.
According to the written documentation submitted, no deficiencies were identified.
Since the effective date of the Regulation of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic No. 28 of 23 April 2004, the Municipal Office is obliged to handle and investigate complaints in accordance with the Complaints Act.
In the near future, it will be necessary to resolve the organizational security of this task.
Communique
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint report on parallel controls on expenditure on the construction of the Prague - Dresden motorway
Foreword
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, it would be difficult to imagine a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe.
Quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and raising the living standards of Europeans.
Creating conditions for fast, safe, reliable and cheap transport of people and cargo is an important task for the state administration.
This is a very demanding task, both organizationally and technically, as well as financially.
European efforts for sustainable mobility often and hardly find compromises with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
The construction of transport infrastructure, even thanks to the necessary measures in favor of the environment, is financially demanding.
Considered procedures and decisions of the state administration in the preparation and acquisition of transport constructions can bring significant savings of public financial resources, which can be used differently for the benefit of citizens.
One of the tasks of control institutions is to actively look for shortcomings that have led to lower than achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures on transport infrastructure constructions.
The control institutions should not only draw the attention of the state administration to the identified shortcomings, but also recommend measures that will lead to an improvement of the situation, for the benefit of the citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
In 2005 and 2006, the two Supreme Audit Institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as Germany and the Czech Republic), the Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as “BRH”) and the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as “SAO”) carried out parallel audits of Dresden (motorway D 8 in the Czech Republic and motorway A 17 in Germany).
The motorways are connected by a border bridge, which is co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to the cooperation with the SAO, the BRH was able to carry out a thorough control of the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with the BRH, the SAO obtained the necessary data on the amount of German costs for bridges and tunnels for comparative purposes.
In 2000, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded an agreement on the construction of a border bridge.
According to the progress of the construction, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, during the award of the contract, the Directorate of Roads and Motorways of the Czech Republic (hereinafter "ŘSD") made mistakes that led to an extension of the competition period and a shortening of the construction time.
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, the ŘSD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
As part of joint inspection work, the prices of bridges on the D 8 and A 17 motorways were compared, based on the conversion per m2 of bridge structure area.
Statistical analysis of prices made it possible to identify bridges with high costs per m2 of area.
The analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in the group of large bridges with a length of over 100 meters.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay that occurred during the tender procedure.
In analyzing the costs of tunnel construction, the inspectors found that the prices of tunnels on the D 8 motorway are significantly higher than the prices of comparable tunnels in Germany.
The BRH and the SAO now have a database of bridge and tunnel prices, which they will be able to rely on for future checks on the effectiveness of the funds used for transport infrastructure.
For the construction of bridges, both inspection institutions recommend: standardization of bridge constructions and the use of composite steel-concrete and special structures only in cases where prestressed reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
The main features of the cooperation were her team spirit and informality.
During the parallel inspection, the inspectors shared their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report informs about the course and results of parallel inspections of funds spent on the construction of a motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The inspections focused on the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of the incurred expenses.
Parallel inspections were performed by the BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel inspections took place in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO inspected the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures in the amount of approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately € 690 million) on the border section of the D 8 motorway, which has the number 0807.
Of this amount, € 64 million from European funds (ISPA) was planned to be used.
In addition to the parallel inspection carried out jointly with the SAO, the BRH inspected the preparation and construction of the A 17 motorway in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the A 17 motorway amounted to around € 670 million, of which € 277 million will be co-financed by European funds (ERDF).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the trans-European transport corridor IV. Dresden - Central and Southern Part of Eastern Europe - Istanbul.
The D 8 motorway leads from Prague via Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
The A 17 motorway leads from the Czech / German state border to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, the border sections of both motorways were under construction.
These sections were put into operation on December 21, 2006.
On the German side, the motorway is completed as far as Dresden, while on the Czech side the D 8 motorway is not completed, because the section No. 0805 in the length of 16.4 km through the Bohemian Central Mountains between Řehlovice and Lovosice is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, section No. 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of ​​České středohoří.
According to forecasts made in the Czech Republic in 2001, the traffic intensity in 2008 at the border section No. 0807 of the D 8 motorway should be 22,940 vehicles per day.
According to German forecasts, in 2010 the intensity of traffic on the Czech border will total about 25,000 vehicles per day.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded an Agreement between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic on the connection of the German A 17 motorway and the Czech D 8 motorway at the common state border by the construction of a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, so the inspection of the construction of this bridge was an important aspect of the parallel inspections carried out by both inspection institutions.
Cooperation between the BRH and the SAO
Since mid-2005, the two Supreme Audit Institutions have been negotiating close cooperation in inspecting the construction of the motorway connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both parties had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1.
Germany contributes financially to the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction is based on ŘSD.
Therefore, BRH itself did not have the opportunity to inspect this construction project.
2.
The SAO did not have the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds had been used economically in terms of the overall level of costs for bridges and tunnels on the D 8.
3.
The SAO needed to ensure the effectiveness of expenditure, taking into account the main technical parameters of the motorway, in particular the layout of bridges and tunnels, which should allow the same quality of driving on both sides of the border.
Following preparatory negotiations, the Agreement on the Coordinated Inspection of the D 8 / A Motorway 17 was signed on 4 January 2006 by the Presidents of the two Supreme Audit Institutions.
Joint working meetings of the BRH and SAO inspectors took place throughout 2006 at intervals of approximately six to eight weeks.
The negotiations addressed current issues and tasks, in particular the preparation of a uniform methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels, the exchange of findings from the inspection of the construction of the border bridge and the preparation of joint reports.
An important feature of the cooperation was the continuous exchange of information.
While the BRH performed most of the work on comparing the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and the tender procedure, the SAO largely prepared a methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal norms for control in the state administration differ in both countries in the way of closing control actions.
For these reasons, the two SAIs have drawn their own audit conclusions on their findings obtained during their audits.
This report reflects the results obtained in the parallel inspections.
The cooperation will end with the signing of the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Construction of a border bridge
In a 2000 agreement, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed on a date for the completion of the construction of the border bridge, if possible in 2005.
The two parties then agreed to postpone this deadline until the end of 2006.
ŘSD acted as investor.
Germany contributes 42.13% financially to the construction of the bridge.
In the period up to 1999, the ŘSD proposed that the border bridge should have a prestressed reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, ŘSD approved a composite steel-concrete structure.
