Compared to a restricted call for tenders, a public tender or a call for tenders gives more competitors the opportunity to participate in the tender procedure.
These types of tenders generate a large number of bids that guarantee the best value for money effect.
The prevention of corruption is significantly strengthened, as the circle of interested parties is not limited by decisions taken in advance by the contracting authority, which thus gives room for manipulation and fixation of prices among bidders.
The studies confirmed the benefits of the German provision on the preference for open procedures or public calls for tenders.
Czech legislation allows contracting authorities to award contracts in an open or restricted procedure.
However, the latest legislation on the Public Procurement Act introduces a ban on contracting authorities to limit the number of tenderers in restricted procedures.
The restricted procedure is now very close to the open procedure.
In Germany, the contracting authority largely complies with the requirement to prefer an open procedure or a public call for competition, while in the Czech Republic some projects were divided in breach of the law in order to circumvent the requirement to select the appropriate type of tender.
However, in the case of some projects implemented in Germany, European limits were not respected, which resulted in the minimum share in pan-European proceedings not being reached.
A satisfactory system has not yet been introduced in the Czech Republic to facilitate the correct calculation of expected costs of construction work and projects.
Where appropriate, contracting authorities should ensure, through more extensive controls, that the requirements for selecting the type of procurement procedure and the volume of contracts awarded in European procedures are met, or should create the conditions necessary to allow the correct calculation of expected costs. .
Preliminary information and notice of initiation
In cases where contracts are awarded in the framework of a European procedure, the contracting authority must publish a report on the procurement procedure.
Prior information and procurement notices are an important basis for European competition.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
The contracting authority must indicate the basic specifications of the intended projects by means of prior notifications.
Prior notices are required for projects where the total cost estimate is equal to or greater than the European limit and where the contracting authority wishes to shorten the deadline for submission of tenders in individual procurement procedures.
The contracting authority is obliged to publish a contract notice with detailed information for all public contracts that require a European procedure.
The information is binding for the contracting authority after publication.
The notification must include, inter alia, the specifications, the time limits for the procedure and for completing the contract, the specific requirements and the selection criteria and their weights.
A common vocabulary for public procurement must be used to describe the subject of the contract.
Preliminary information and contract notices are published in the EU in the Official Journal of the EU and on the contracting authority's profile.
In order to prevent discrimination against foreign candidates, notices at national level should not contain any additional information and should not be published before the text of the notification is sent to the Publications Office of the EU.
Incomplete or inaccurate information in the pre-notification may distort competition or even facilitate manipulation.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have fully implemented EU provisions on prior information and procurement notices into their national legislation.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, preliminary information and notices must also be published in the case of contracts for which a European procedure is not required.
The procurement procedure may not start earlier than one month after the dispatch of the prior notice.
Disclosure of prior information may be waived only in exceptional cases.
In Germany, prior information is not required in cases where a European procedure is not required.
In the case of national proceedings, the public call must be published on the federal government's website and, where appropriate, in the press.
In the case of restricted procedures without competition from participants, the notice must be published if the estimated price of the contract is equal to or higher than € 25,000 (CZK 625 thousand).
Preliminary notices must explain all planned parts of the project.
This is an important requirement given the number of small contracts in Germany.
Dividing projects into smaller parts is not so common in the Czech Republic and this measure is considered less important.
Main control findings
BRH
Prior notice
The contracting authorities published a prior notice of projects which included works to be awarded in a European procedure.
In some open procedures, they shortened the deadline, although the number of days between sending the pre-notification and sending the contract notice was less than 52 days.
In the case of other summary proceedings, the annual deadlines for prior information have expired and should be renewed.
In many cases, the prior notification did not indicate the expected division of the works into several parts.
Notice of the opening of the procurement procedure
Some notifications contained codes from a common dictionary that deviated from the content of the pre-notification or did not specify exactly the work to be carried out.
In rare cases, notices at national level included more information, eg on deadlines, or were published before the notice was published in the Official Journal of the EU.
Ex-ante transparency
One contracting authority hired an external company to publish the national notice.
It published a notice on its platform, the use of which was charged.
However, the contracting authority did not check whether this company had to comply with the requirement to forward the notification to a free internet government portal.
The sample found that only a third of the announcements were actually published on the government portal.
SAO
Notice of the opening of the procurement procedure
During the construction of the wastewater treatment plant, the contracting authority did not set out in the notice of the restricted tender to the construction contractor the criteria according to which it will reduce the large number of tenders for the evaluation procedure.
The contracting authority was not able to document the method of selection (reduction) of tenders for evaluation.
The reduction in the number of offers was made possible by previous legislation.
During the construction of the ring road, the contracting authority for one construction did not define in the notice of initiation of the restricted procedure or in the qualification documentation the values ​​according to which it will assess the degree of fulfillment of qualification criteria or the number of candidates to be invited.
The contracting authority assessed the fulfillment of the qualification in such a way that all six candidates in the restricted procedure fulfilled it, but excluded one of them, stating that they fulfilled only in the last sixth place.
The contracting authority's procedure was not transparent, as it did not publish information in advance on what of the qualification data will be evaluated and how.
Publication of calls
In violation of the law, the contracting authority did not publish a written invitation to submit tenders for construction modifications in former military districts.
Conclusions and recommendations / summary
A two-stage information process with prior information and publication of a notice of initiation is an important tool for meeting the requirements of transparency and strengthening the competitive environment applied in European proceedings.
By extending the obligation to publish prior information in the Czech Republic for national procurement procedures as well, and strengthening this obligation in Germany for limited procedures, both countries have increased the transparency of procurement procedures and improved the competitive environment.
Selection of candidates in restricted procedures
Unlike open procedures, restricted procedures do not allow all potential tenderers to participate.
In restricted procedures, the contracting authority first selects potential suppliers who will be asked to submit a tender.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
EU provisions allow limiting the number of applicants in European restricted procedures.
However, the restricted procedure requires at least five tenderers who will be invited to submit a tender, and in the case of a negotiated procedure with publication, at least three potential tenderers must be invited.
In any case, the number of candidates invited must be wide enough to guarantee real competition.
The selection criteria must be objective and non-discriminatory and must be published in advance.
The selection of potential candidates who will be invited is very prone to manipulation, eg by the preferences of some of them.
Reducing competition to a few bidders can facilitate their collusion.
This has a negative impact on the outcome of the proceedings.
Therefore, the contracting authority must take measures to prevent manipulation and ensure that it has effective control so that this procedure is transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The provisions for the selection of candidates are similar in both countries.
In addition to the requirements of the European Directive, contracting authorities should vary the tenders they invite to submit a tender.
It is also not permissible to restrict competition from a regional point of view.
Contracting authorities must document and justify the selection of tenderers and the selection process.
Different provisions
In Germany, at least three candidates are required to be invited in the case of a restricted procedure and several suitable candidates in the case of a negotiated procedure.
With the exception of two cases, the new Czech regulations do not allow limiting the number of candidates addressed in the case of restricted and negotiated procedures.
In Germany, the "four eyes" principle must be respected when selecting candidates.
While one worker proposes a list of them, another must substantially modify the proposal, eg by deleting the proposed candidate or substituting another.
This is to prevent a situation where an individual can definitively determine the circle of candidates who will take part in the procedure.
In the absence of such a provision, far-reaching illegal agreement between the participants is possible.
The list of candidates who will be invited to submit a tender must be confidential and must not be disclosed.
Authorized independent experts are also obliged to do so.
There is no similar measure or measure for the confidential treatment of the list of candidates in the Czech Republic.
According to German provisions, they may not nominate candidates from an external company, but may make proposals to the contracting authority.
There is no similar requirement in the Czech Republic.
Main control findings
BRH
Number of applicants
Except for a few cases, the requirement to address the minimum number of applicants was met.
The analysis of almost 7,000 contracts for constructions with a value up to the national limit showed that in the case of limited procedures, the contracting authorities invited an average of 6.6 potential bidders and in the case of direct negotiated procedures on average 4.4 bidders.
Change of suppliers and regional restrictions
The contracting authorities, especially in the area of ​​building construction, did not change the circle of candidates addressed, as they had good experience with those with whom they had worked so far.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The contracting authorities argued that, in the case of a closed procedure, they should ensure that they contact candidates whose suitability they have already ascertained in advance.
Although there was no evidence of illegal regional restrictions, the circle of candidates in a closed procedure included a larger proportion of regional candidates than in the case of public proceedings.
The contracting authorities explained this by the low amount of the contract compared to the public tender and the high travel costs for potential tenderers.
The principle of cross-checking and proposals of self-employed professionals
The contracting authorities mostly ignored the obligation to change the list of candidates proposed by self-employed professionals.
They argued in particular for lack of staff, time pressure or inadequate knowledge of a suitable candidate.
In many cases, it was not clear from the records who proposed the candidate who had been asked to take part in the procedure.
An inspection of some samples showed that the list of potential candidates was drawn up by self-employed experts and accepted by the contracting authority without changes.
Thus, the contracting authorities did not sufficiently protect themselves from potential manipulation.
Confidentiality of treatment of lists of potential candidates
For one contracting authority, a list of candidates for invitations to tender was kept in a database to which all employees had access at any time.
This allowed the manipulation or unauthorized disclosure of the names of the candidates expected or accepted, who could then agree on a price.
Documentation
The documentation stated the reasons for the selection of candidates in only a few cases.
SAO
Criteria for selection of candidates
During the construction of the ring road, those interested did not have information on what from the data on their qualifications will be evaluated and in what way.
For the action related to the development and modernization of waterways and ports, the criteria for limiting the number of tenderers were not set out in the contract notice for participation in the restricted procedure.
All eight tenderers met the qualification requirements, but this exceeded the number to which the contracting authority limited participation in the tender procedure.
The Commission then selected candidates at random - by drawing lots, which was legal at the time.
This procedure should have been mentioned as a criterion in the tender notice.
Summary
In view of the high risk of manipulation in the selection of the winning tenderer in restricted procedures, both countries have introduced special measures to prevent unlawful restrictions of competition.
German rules limit such opportunities for manipulation by means of so-called cross-checking (four-eyes principle), by maintaining the confidentiality of the list of candidates and by prohibiting proposals for the selection of candidates from outside companies.
The Czech rules aim to prevent potential restrictions with the aim of manipulation mainly by an unlimited number of applicants.
However, the audit found that some of these rules were not sufficiently applied and that inadmissible restrictions on the number of candidates were not prevented in some cases.
Contracting authorities are obliged to completely eliminate the mentioned shortcomings.
Submission of bids
The procurement phase, in which potential tenderers may prepare tenders on the basis of the tender dossier they have received, begins with the publication of information on the procurement procedure and / or a call for tenderers.
Until the date of opening the envelopes, potential tenderers may submit their tenders to the contracting authority, thus bidding for the contract.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of the procurement procedure.
The contracting authority must follow the national regulations governing this phase of the procedure and prevent potential manipulation.
These regulations apply in particular to the organization and control.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle applies that tender documents, on the basis of which potential suppliers prepare their bids, must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Design offices that are interested in management should not fulfill this role.
The contracting authority must ensure that all candidates receive the same information during this phase of the procurement procedure.
In case of ambiguities in the tender documentation or if other questions arise, only the contracting authority may provide information to the tenderers.
The design offices responsible for drawing up the tender dossier may not provide any information.
Throughout this phase, any contact between the design office and the tenderers must be avoided.
They must remain anonymous throughout, as allowing contact with them may adversely affect competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly must be submitted in a sealed envelope.
Electronically submitted bids must be encrypted.
Different provisions
In Germany, the contracting authority may entrust insured suppliers of external services with the printing and distribution of documentation, and their staff must be bound by professional secrecy.
In Germany, tenders received must be marked with the date of receipt and handed over directly and immediately in their original state (sealed) to the official in charge of their storage.
This staff member must not be involved in the procurement procedure.
Received bids must be locked until the date the envelopes are opened.
In the Czech Republic, the offers received are marked with a serial number.
The contracting authority issues a report with data on the tender, including the number of the tender and information on the preparation of the tender and its receipt.
There are no special regulations on the safekeeping of tenders.
Main control findings
BRH
BRH checked the assignment of the administrative building.
Sending tender documentation
The inspected contracting authorities of the construction administration sent the tender documentation either directly or entrusted its printing and distribution to an external company.
The self-employed did not send any documentation.
Information provided to candidates
In the part of the tender documentation concerning inquiries and obtaining information, the contracting authority did not follow the rule for separate planning from the tender procedure.
Contrary to the relevant regulations, he often did not mention the names of his contact staff in the documentation, but rather the staff of the project management department.
Some notices in the tender procedure even contained the names of companies or self-employed persons who participated in the preparation of the tender dossier.
In rare cases, candidates who asked questions during the procurement procedure did not receive identical information.
Labeling of offers
For contracting authorities, all accepted tenders were stamped and acknowledged of receipt.
However, in some cases in the negotiated procedure, bids were accepted by self-employed professionals, in breach of the one-stop-corruption rule.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to keep them in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
For one contracting authority, tenders were temporarily placed in an open filing cabinet, to which all employees had access.
Another contracting authority placed the box in the hallway without constant supervision, and part of the bids thrown in the box remained there overnight.
The mailbox opening was wide and unsecured, making it accessible not only to employees.
SAO
The SAO did not find any shortcomings in this area.
Summary
In both countries, rules are laid down to prevent contacts, in particular between the companies involved and the design offices cooperating in the procurement procedure, throughout the process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all candidates.
Rules for the prevention of manipulation and corruption are appropriate for the receipt, safekeeping and confidentiality of offers.
In Germany, the relevant requirements are somewhat more elaborated than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the accumulated control records showed breaches of the rules in some areas.
These discrepancies can be easily remedied.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of the envelopes, the offers that have been closed so far are opened, their content is read and published.
The period for which the tenderer is bound by his tender begins at the end of the deadline for submission of envelopes or their opening and ends with the deadline specified by the contracting authority.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
European legislation does not contain any specific provisions dealing with the opening of envelopes.
However, national laws and regulations contain extensive requirements for the protection of bids and competition during this sensitive phase of the entire procurement process.
The principles of "more eyes", transparency and credibility of the process of opening the envelopes are intended to prevent manipulations and modifications to the tenders already submitted.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The envelopes must be opened by several persons appointed by the contracting authority.
Compliance with the "more eyes" principle is intended to prevent individuals from covertly manipulating offers.
Candidates may be present when the envelopes are opened.
When opening, all envelopes must be placed in front of the chairman of the commission and are opened one after the other.
Late bids may not be considered.
To ensure transparency when opening the envelopes, this phase, including the conclusions (results), must be recorded in writing. The record must include, among other things, the names of the tenderers and the prices offered.
The minutes must be read and signed by the group leader.
The minutes may also be signed by the candidates present.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, a commission is being set up to open envelopes.
The participation of independent experts is allowed.
The members of the commission may also be entrusted with the discussion in the subsequent stages of the procedure, ie the evaluation of tenders.
In Germany, the envelopes are opened in the presence of the manager and the recorder.
The manager must be an employee of the contracting authority.
The manager and, in the case of building construction, the recorder may not be participants in the preparatory phase (creation of tender documentation), may not decide on the award of the contract and may not be members in the subsequent processing (management) of the contract.
German regulations require that the record of the opening of envelopes contain not only the offer prices, but also all information on discounts and special (unusual) signs, such as damaged envelopes upon receipt or late arrivals.
In the Czech Republic, in addition to the offer prices, the registration must also contain information on the language of the offer and the tenderer's signature authorization.
German regulations require that all parts of the envelopes to be opened be marked in order to prevent subsequent changes.
Tenders, usually marked in the form of a perforation with the date, must be kept confidential after the opening of the envelopes has been closed and may only be made available to persons who further process them.
There are no similar measures in the Czech Republic.
If a single tender is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope must not be opened and the tenderer must be notified immediately.
In Germany, they do not have this arrangement, and if a single tender is accepted, it is opened and evaluated.
Main control findings
BRH
Principle of cross-checking
During the opening of the envelopes, the contracting authorities followed the principle of four eyes.
The leader and recorder, who was not assigned a different role, were always present.
In rare cases, however, in small negotiated procedures, natural persons opened tenders sent to them without the participation of the contracting authority.
Envelope opening process
the notes from the opening of the envelopes did not always document the course.
In some cases, late tenders were not marked and in some cases signatures were missing.
Marking of received offers
The contracting authorities marked the offers of perforations with a date, which was in accordance with the requirements.
Some of them in the past marked the offers incorrectly, but after notifying the BRH they changed their practice.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
SAO
Deadline for submission of tenders
During road repairs, in one event, the tenderer's offer was handed over to the contracting authority with a one-month delay, which he nevertheless accepted.
Summary
Substantial parts of the provisions on the opening of envelopes are identical in both countries with regard to the principle of "more eyes" and the principle of transparency, and thus make it possible to substantially reduce the risk of corruption and manipulation.
The German rules are more complex in comparison with the Czech Republic, especially the requirements for accurate documentation of the procedure.
Marking, safe storage and respect for the confidentiality of tenders significantly limit the possibility of subsequent changes in the tenders submitted.
In addition, the staff responsible for opening the envelopes may not carry out any other activities related to the contract to be awarded.
The findings, despite the detection of some irregularities, confirm that the rules for opening envelopes are largely applied.
Assessment and evaluation of offers
The contracting authority must examine and evaluate the tenders received within the deadline.
At the same time, they must award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
EU law sets out the process of assessing and evaluating tenders in several steps:
The first step is to check the suitability of the candidates.
They must have a good economic and financial position and the required professional and technical knowledge and skills.
Candidates who have ever been convicted of bribery or fraud must always be excluded from the procurement procedure.
Tenders of non-excluded tenderers must be evaluated in terms of numerical accuracy, technical suitability and value for money on the basis of previously published award criteria.
The contracting authority must determine the most economically advantageous tender and, in particular, examine all significantly low price tenders.
Review and evaluation is particularly sensitive and prone to manipulation.
For example, tenderers may be excluded without a valid reason, or tenders that do not meet the requirements may be left in the competition.
The result of the evaluation may be incorrectly affected by the preference or disadvantage of a tenderer, which may prevent the selection of the most economically advantageous tender.
The contracting authority must therefore take special measures in selecting the persons involved in the process and must ensure that they meet the requirements of good repute and technical knowledge.
It must also make sure that the whole process and the decisions taken are transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
In line with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require a review and evaluation of tenders in successive steps.
During the evaluation, the requirements for proving the suitability of candidates, the evaluation criteria and their weights stated in the notice or in the tender dossier may not be changed.
The criteria set for assessing the suitability of candidates may no longer be used.
Further evaluation can only be performed on the basis of evaluation criteria.
The tenders submitted must first be formally examined to see whether they are complete or whether they do not contain suspicious elements that could encourage manipulation.
If tenderers are excluded from further examination and evaluation of the tenders submitted by them, they must be informed immediately.
If the evaluation of tenders results in a disproportionately low tender price, the tenderer concerned must be given the opportunity to comment on the situation before any tender is rejected.
The reasons for the decision must be transparently documented.
Different provisions
In Germany, tenderers must maintain confidentiality and only eligible persons may take part in the evaluation of tenders.
The mathematical accuracy of the tenders may only be checked by the contracting authority.
Only employees who are not involved in the decision-making phase of the supplier selection or in the project implementation phase can be entrusted with the evaluation.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are commissioned to review and evaluate tenders, they must be aware that tenders are confidential and honestly respect this fact.
They can only make proposals for decisions to the contracting authority.
In the Czech Republic, tenders must be reviewed and evaluated by a commission appointed by the contracting authority, which will draw up a report proposing the conclusion of the contract.
However, in both countries, the final decision depends on the contracting authority.
If, in Germany, the documents and declarations required in connection with the submission of tenders are incomplete, the tenderers concerned must subsequently submit the required documents within six days.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
If tenderers do not comply with this obligation, their tenders must be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority can decide whether to give the tenderer the opportunity to complete the missing documents.
If the tenderer does not provide them, he must be expelled.
In Germany, it is necessary to review not only the total price but also the unit prices.
If the price structure of the tender shows that the prices for parts of the overall project have been estimated disproportionately high or low, tenderers must be asked for an explanation.
If they do not provide explanations and if the contracting authority can prove that the tender contains compensatory prices, such tenders must be excluded.
This is to prevent bidders from submitting price calculations on the assumption that substantial quantitative changes will be made to individual parts of the overall project, which may lead to a significant increase in project costs.
In the Czech Republic, the total price of the work is evaluated and the prices of individual parts are not examined in detail.
Valuation compensation is not a reason to exclude a bid.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a tenderer offering a disproportionately high or low price.
If one or more tenders differ in price by 10% or more from the price estimated by the contracting authority or from other tenders, tenderers must prove that their tender has been credibly and convincingly calculated.
If they are unable to do so, the contracting authority should exclude them.
In the Czech Republic, the tender procedure may be canceled after a price review if only tenders with disproportionately low prices have been received and the tenderers have not substantiated these prices.
If the price of the tender is significantly higher than the contracting authority's estimate, this is not a reason for refusing to award the contract to the tenderer concerned (unlike the German contracting law).
If there is a suspicion in Germany of conduct intended to restrict competition, the contracting authority is obliged to report this fact immediately to the competent superior authority.
He must decide on the further procedure and whether it is appropriate to inform the antitrust authority or law enforcement authorities.
It must also approve (eg when the contract exceeds € 50,000 and the contract has not been awarded to the lowest bidder) whether the contract will be awarded when the contract is negotiated or whether the procurement procedure is canceled.
Czech rules do not regulate this area.
Main control findings
BRH
Checking suitability and award criteria
Most of the procurement procedures examined complied with the relevant requirements.
In the case of some recommendations from potential suppliers made by self-employed persons, the contracting authorities did not check the suitability of the tenderers themselves.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
In some procurement cases, insufficient documentation was provided as to whether the contracting authority took into account all published evaluation criteria or whether the selection decision was based solely on the price criterion.
Selection of interested parties and confidentiality of tenders
Some contracting authorities used the services of unauthorized persons, such as self-employed persons or employees of building authorities.
They were involved in the planning or implementation process of construction projects, performing functions that were to be performed exclusively by the contracting authority.
The contracting authorities sought to substantiate this fact with their insufficient human resources in the sector.
In some cases, self-employed professionals used the services of persons who were not formally bound to maintain the confidentiality of the offers and to exercise due diligence to fulfill their obligations under the contract.
As far as contracting authorities are concerned, as a rule, there was no conclusive evidence as to whether tenders in the custody of self-employed professionals were available only to designated persons.
Review and mathematical control of tenders
Some contracting authorities handed over open envelopes for further verification to self-employed professionals without first carrying out the prescribed examination of tenders and mathematical examination and without documenting the results of these inspections.
In the event of any intention to manipulate, third parties may have made changes to the tenders which could not be identified by the contracting authority.
Examination of the documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the tenders were not adequately identified or where price and product data were missing.
Performance audits
A sample check of one contracting authority revealed that in 75% of procurement cases, the most advantageous tenders deviated by more than 10% from the estimated costs.
One of the twenty tenders was canceled due to inadequate tender prices.
In many cases, there was a lack of records or sufficient documentation on the examination of tenders or on negotiations with tenderers for further clarification.
In many cases, detailed information was also missing, eg on unit prices of the most important invoiced items.
Changes in market prices or increases in material costs were often cited as reasons for deviations.
Contracting authorities have argued that it is difficult to identify and prove countervailing prices.
In the case of one call for tenders made by an entity outside the scope of the normal contracting authorities, a 66% lower price was offered compared to the original cost estimate.
Data on a closer examination of costs or on the reasons for deviations were not recorded.
In clarifying this issue, the contracting authority did not find any indication of price dumping for the tenderer to whom the contract might be awarded.
It was therefore not clear whether the original cost estimate was excessive or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the contracting authority rated this bidder as a "low-cost company" that was unable to meet either the quality requirements or the deadlines.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to a tenderer whose price was 35% higher than the original cost estimate.
The contracting authority did not cancel the tender procedure and put forward an unfounded argument that it could be assumed that the tenderer did not base its pricing on disproportionately high costs.
Suspected irregularities
Two cases of irregularities were found at one contracting authority, and these were reported to the company responsible for technical supervision.
In one tender procedure, two tenderers submitted tenders containing an identical price calculation, which led the contracting authority to exclude both tenders.
The inspections did not reveal any significant deficiencies in the application of other provisions.
SAO
Verification of suitability
For many construction projects, such as university buildings, roads and railways, contracting authorities did not exclude tenderers from participating in the tender procedure, even though they did not meet the contracting authority's requirements set out in the tender conditions or provided the required qualification or or explain the reason for the exclusion of the candidate who met the requirements.
Evaluation
In the case of the construction of a wastewater treatment plant, the individual evaluation criteria of the tender procedure for the construction contractor were set, but the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For the action in the field of railway infrastructure development, the weights of the evaluation criteria were not set at the beginning of the management when awarding the contract, but only at the beginning of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the assessment of the "shortening construction time" criterion was not carried out correctly.
For the second and third place tenderers, a greater reduction in construction time was incorrectly mentioned in the evaluation than was indicated in their tenders.
Documentation of the reasons for the selection of the candidate
For three events related to housing support, the contracting authority did not document on the basis of which criteria it assessed the accepted offers and how it selected the most suitable one.
The correctness of the selection of suppliers of small-scale contracts associated with the construction of the ring road with an estimated price of up to 500 thousand.
CZK could not be verified, as the suppliers were selected only on the basis of telephone consultations on the price and date of performance, but documents on these negotiations were not prepared.
Summary
In both countries, the rules for verifying and evaluating tenders comply with EU requirements.
However, they differ with regard to the specific management steps and the selection of individuals involved in the proceedings.
In contrast to the Czech Republic, in Germany these steps in the procurement process are governed by stricter and more detailed requirements, especially as regards the application of the cross-principle and the protection of tenders.
The same applies to the rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, in some cases of inspections, it was found that the essential steps of the process in verifying and evaluating tenders were not documented at all and, if so, only partially.
The absence of control tools and transparency in decision-making during the examination and evaluation of tenders allows manipulation.
The inspections revealed serious defects, such as the transmission of tenders to third parties without prior proper verification and documentation of the tenders by the contracting authority.
Where contracting entities entrust a third party with the performance of functions related to the examination and evaluation of tenders, appropriate measures and increased control of measures against increased possibilities for manipulation are necessary.
In all cases, the audited German contracting authorities did not use the complete set of available tools when checking the eligibility of prices and did not deal with their own price structure.
In the Czech Republic, shortcomings were found in the evaluation of the suitability of tenders and the use of evaluation criteria.
Completion of the tender procedure
After reviewing and evaluating the tenders, the procurement process is completed by awarding the contract or canceling the procedure.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
In the case of a European procedure, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the award decision.
Suppliers shall have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited period of 10 or 15 days and to request a review, if appropriate.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The period of 10 days applies to electronic submission and 15 days to other submissions.
The contract may not be concluded before the expiry of this period or before the decision of the review procedure.
If the review body rejects the complaint and upholds the decision, candidates and tenderers must be given the opportunity to have the correctness of the exercise of the award right reviewed by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting authority will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by the swift implementation of procurement decisions.
The contracting authority must duly document the course of the procedure.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have implemented management information obligations.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure rests with the contracting authority.
However, it cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of a properly performed verification and evaluation.
The contracting authority is to conclude the contract within the specified time.
The reason is the fact that the tenderer is not bound by his tender after this deadline.
The content of the contract must not deviate from the winning bid.
Unsuccessful tenderers should be informed of the result in good time, stating the reason why their tender has not been accepted.
Cancellation of the tender procedure is permissible only if certain conditions are met, eg if the prices in the tenders do not correspond to the specifications.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory waiting period of 10 or 15 days before concluding a contract applies to both European and national proceedings.
In Germany, the equivalent provision only applies to European proceedings.
In all other procedures in Germany, tenderers cannot be informed of the award of a contract before a decision on its EU provision and a review has been made.
In the Czech Republic, the tender procedure must be canceled if a single tender has been received or only one tender has met the requirements for its consideration and evaluation.
In Germany, a contract must be awarded even if a single tender has been received, provided that this tender meets the conditions set out in the tender dossier and is cost-effective.
Main control findings
BRH
The inspections found few inconsistencies in the completion of the audited procurement processes.
In some cases in European proceedings, companies authorizing letters were received before the expiry of the notification period, which may invalidate the contract.
Also in several cases of open procedures, the letters of authority contained modifications incompatible with the content of the tender, such as new deadlines.
In some cases, contracting authorities did not meet the deadlines for the award of the contract.
In one open procedure, the contracting authority selected the second most advantageous tender because the tenderer offering a price more than 50% lower no longer wished to fulfill the contract at the price originally offered.
SAO
During the reconstruction and construction of the university, in one case the contracting authority did not conclude a work contract with the contractor in accordance with the draft contract contained in the tender of the selected tenderer.
For some road repairs, road construction, motorway and ring road projects, contracts were concluded later than required by law.
In the case of construction modifications in former military districts, the contracting authority sent a notice of the selection of the most suitable tender to all tenderers only after the expiry of the legal deadline.
Summary
Both countries have implemented EU rules on the termination of procurement procedures.
Legal protection of unsuccessful candidates helps to reduce corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act includes the institute of legal protection even in cases of contracts below EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that the limited time limit for concluding the contract was exceeded.
This can have adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting authorities should eliminate such shortcomings when closing a procurement procedure.
Documentation, notifications, information obligations
The procurement process, with all its various stages, relevant findings and decisions, including the relevant justifications, must be documented in a transparent manner.
Completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
Data on procurement procedures are summarized in EU statistics.
Requirements of European law and prevention of corruption
The obligation to document the procurement procedure is in line with the basic requirement of the principle of transparency, applied at EU level.
Only proper and time-relevant documentation on decision-making and justification guarantees transparency in the procurement process and, above all, guarantees effective legal protection of the interests of each tenderer in cases where the value of the contract exceeds European limits.
Proper documentation is also an essential part of anti-corruption measures, as the obligation to give detailed reasons for individual decisions and their justification significantly reduces the scope for manipulation.
In the case of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must notify their completion to the EU’s Office of Official Publications within 48 days of the date of award of the contract.
The Office publishes the notification in the Official Journal of the EU and thus fulfills the requirement of transparency.
The contracting authority must summarize the essential details of its procurement procedures and communicate them to the European Commission through the relevant national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission publishes annual statistics, which provide an overview of the development of the single market in construction.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have fully transposed the provisions of the European Law on Documentation and Notification Obligations into their national legislation.
The provisions on documentation and notification for European statistics are almost identical in both countries.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to notify the award of a contract applies not only to European procedures but also to national procedures.
The notice period is only 15 days from the conclusion of the contract.
In Germany, the obligation to notify procurement procedures, in addition to those which are mandatory under European law, applies only to limited procedures exceeding the limit of 25 thousand. € (625 thousand CZK) and direct proceedings exceeding the limit of 15 thousand CZK € (375 thousand CZK) including VAT.
Only participants in the proceedings are informed below this limit.
Main control findings
BRH
Documentation
A large number of assignments were not fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, such as the reasons for the supply specifications and national rules.
In one case, the contracting authority did not explain why it had concluded a contract with a tenderer whose tender did not contain the required particulars.
In several cases, some required records were also missing.
Publication of the award of the contract
In some European proceedings, the contracting authority erred in publishing the notice.
In the case of several entries, there was no evidence of publication of the notice.
Notification obligation
The statistically validated files included the required minimum of information and were created and sent on time.
Preliminary transparency
In most cases, the contracting authority published information on the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting authority, the contract information was not disclosed due to a communication error.
It took the contracting authority half a year to notice the errors.
As a result, the outcome of the proceedings was not disclosed during this period.
SAO
Documentation
For events related to the organization of a major sporting event, significant deficiencies were found in the documentation on the course of the tender procedure, such as incorrect data on bid prices in the minutes of the evaluation committee meeting.
In addition, some documents on the opening of the envelopes were not signed.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the preparation of repairs and maintenance of roads, construction of the motorway and the ring road, the contract award notice was sent after the deadline or was not published.
Summary
The provisions on documentation and notification and notification obligations include European requirements and are almost identical in both countries.
This generally ensures the transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
The Czech reporting obligations are somewhat stricter compared to the German ones.
The inspections revealed shortcomings that significantly reduced the value of documentation as a means of preventing corruption.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
Contracting authorities should further enhance the transparency of their procurement procedures and fully comply with the notification and notification requirements.
Summary evaluation and recommendations
The parallel audits of the SAO and the BRH were focused on two areas that are essential for the public procurement process in both the Czech Republic and Germany, namely the application of EU procurement law and the prevention of corruption.
EU legislation provides an opportunity for international competition within the EU to create a single European market.
The aim of measures to prevent corruption is not only to avoid or at least reduce it, but also to prevent financial damage and possible loss of confidence in the integrity of the government.
The findings of the audit institutions of both audit institutions - the SAO and the BRH - with regard to the application of the procurement law of both countries and the comparison of its respective provisions give an internal view of common and different elements that may help both countries in further development and application of this law.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries have transposed EU public procurement law into their national legislation.
In both countries, there is thus an important common basis for public procurement and meeting the basic requirements of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting authorities reinforce these requirements in part with very extensive measures.
The Czech Republic has applied the provisions on public procurement requiring European procedures to procedures that are below EU limits and are therefore governed by national legislation.
However, inspections have shown that contracting authorities do not always fully comply with all relevant provisions of EU requirements.
German contracting authorities should continue to improve the quality of their procurement procedures in order to eliminate these inconsistencies, taking into account the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, inspections identified risks affecting economy and value for money.
In particular, the incomplete definition of the subject of the public contract, which resulted in additional work that was often awarded in violation of the law, insufficient definition of the estimated price and the required qualifications to narrow the possible circle of bidders and thus reduce competition, especially in transport construction.
Corruption prevention
The joint inspections were not aimed at detecting cases of corruption.
The reason was that the BRH and the SAO do not have sufficient tools for this.
However, they can examine whether the competent authorities of both countries are taking measures to reduce corruption and manipulation in public procurement and how these measures are being applied.
Regarding corruption prevention, the two countries focused on different aspects.
Above all, the German provisions leave room for wide and unrestricted competition, transparency and controls as a central element in preventing corruption.
Czech regulations primarily aim at strengthening the transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany, there are general principles for the prevention of corruption, which apply to the entire federal administration.
These principles have also been incorporated into public procurement requirements and have been adopted to meet the specific needs of such procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, sometimes even very precisely, the ways in which the requirements for the prevention of corruption during the procurement procedure and for the selection of persons included in it are met.
In the opinion of the BRH, the principle of preference for open tenders and calls for participation is a particularly suitable tool for significantly reducing the risk of corruption in public procurement, while restricting competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Risk analysis and adequate control (especially the principle of cross-checking), transparency requirements, tender documentation and various organizational measures are also effective mechanisms for preventing corruption and manipulation.
Therefore, BRH does not feel the need for substantial changes to the current provisions, which public institutions must comply with when awarding public contracts.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
Irregularities found in some areas highlighted weaknesses in complying with certain requirements.
Therefore, contracting authorities should provide their employees with further training to familiarize them with anti-corruption requirements and further increase their awareness in this area.
A significant part of the identified weaknesses relates to activities that the construction administration has delegated to private entrepreneurs.
However, the absence of adequate controls in the delegation of powers increases the risk of their abuse.
Activities prone to manipulation and corruption should therefore be outsourced to third parties only if the administration can guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against unauthorized interference.
SAO
In the Czech Republic, anti-corruption strategies have been adopted at the governmental level, which also significantly affect the area of ​​public procurement.
The SAO's audits took place at a time when one of the most important parts of this strategy had been implemented, namely a significant amendment to the Public Procurement Act and the adoption of related implementing regulations.
The adopted strategy and new legislation can be effective steps to improve the situation.
Under the new regulations, for example, the contracting authority must justify the effectiveness of the public contract, the determination of the estimated value of the public contract, the adequacy of qualification requirements, the determination of basic evaluation criteria and the method of evaluation of tenders.
Recommendation
Overall, both the SAO and the BRH have a favorable opinion on how to implement EU requirements.
Their widespread application in practice has confirmed that the EU's requirements for competition, equal treatment and transparency form an appropriate basis for public procurement within the EU.
The transnational model introduced in the EU can also serve as a basis for similar projects aimed at facilitating and promoting international competition.
Taking into account the great potential of material and intangible damages resulting from manipulation and corruption in connection with the award of public contracts, the BRH and the SAO insist that it is the duty of contracting authorities to continue measures against corruption and manipulation and improve them where possible.
In particular, the organizational structures and processes of procurement procedures should be continuously monitored for weaknesses and risks in order to identify the need for corrective action and to respond appropriately.
In comparison with the practice in Germany, it turned out that the share of open tenders in the Czech Republic should increase, which gives room to competition and significantly reduces the possibility of corrupt behavior.
Partial procurement can also have a positive impact on the price achieved, where this is permissible and appropriate for the contracting authority. A higher number of bidders puts pressure on the price achieved.
Ensuring its organization also has an impact on the course of the procurement procedure.
In Germany, it is provided by special state organizations, while in the Czech Republic, with the exception of transport constructions, it is organized by central authorities themselves or through contracted organizations.
Both the SAO and the BRH wish to further develop knowledge in their work where appropriate, and to address it with their parliament and government beyond their joint project.
In addition, they are convinced that the principles of procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will also be of interest at the level of the International Organization of Supreme Audit Institutions (INTOSAI), as these principles and findings are of general importance for effectively combating corruption and guaranteeing that public contracts are awarded in a well-functioning and fair competition regime and that value for money is achieved.
Side dishes
JOINT FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel inspections of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint final report
May 2017
The Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Foreword
The presented joint report informs about the course and result of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012–2015.
Cooperation between the supreme audit institutions of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO SR and the SAO CR in the performance of parallel controls focused on the administration of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen on the basis of the fact that both EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to find out how it is applied at the national level, how the excise administration system is set up and how the systems in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefit of the inspections carried out was the exchange of experiences, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Last but not least, the benefit was that the international comparability of data on the efficiency and effectiveness of excise administration is very limited without the implementation of parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrík,
president
chairman
Of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel inspections of the SPD administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legal regulation of excise duties in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic and their administration is in accordance with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences were found between the adjustment of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic; in the Czech Republic, verification of the economic stability of applicants for permits and mandatory marking and coloring of selected mineral oils and some other oils contributes to the effective administration of excise duties; In the Slovak Republic, the distribution of control stamps is simpler than in the Czech Republic and is less burdensome for the tax administrator.
In the fight against excise tax evasion, the supervision of the movement of raw tobacco, resp. tobacco raw materials, implementation of the institute of fuel distributor and registration of sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Revenues from excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's goals of reducing labor taxation, introducing eco-saving measures and reducing tobacco and alcohol dependence have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, partly because excise tax rate indexation has not been introduced in both countries.
This results in a reduction in the importance of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of growing purchasing power, a real reduction in the tax burden on excise duties.
The introduction of environmental measures has been financially supported by the state for a long time, but these measures have a negative impact on excise tax revenues, which will have to be replaced in the future by other revenues or reductions in state expenditures.
Administrative expenditures on the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have been growing for a long time, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency is declining.
In the Slovak Republic, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditures on the electronic administration of excise duties (IT expenditures) and expenditures on wages of employees performing permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
The electronic administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic did not have a significant effect on reducing the number of tax administrators.
The SAO CR and the SAO SR recommend the FR SR to reconsider the justification for the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the efficiency of administrative expenditures was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures in the audited period that would lead to a reduction in the personnel intensity of the excise tax administration.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in individual years of the audited period was similar, while the number of comparable tax entities in the Slovak Republic is about a third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical performance of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is more administratively demanding than in the Czech Republic and, due to the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities, also more expensive.
The electronic administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of excise tax returns is fully electronic, in the Czech Republic, documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are submitted electronically.
Both methods of electronic support support the effective administration of excise duties, and therefore the SAO CR and the SAO SR recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditures for the implementation of the EMCS system could not be compared, as the FR SR provided data on expenditures only for the system upgrade in the period 2011–2015, but the expenditures were also incurred before this period.
Expenditures incurred in the mentioned period only for the upgrade of EMCS in the Slovak Republic were about 20% higher than expenditures incurred in the Czech Republic both for the introduction of EMCS and for the upgrade of this system in more than ten years.
Excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic did not achieve comparable values ​​of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the Slovak Republic the administration of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of the electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duty (EMCS) has made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but to a lesser extent in the Slovak Republic, as significantly higher expenditures were incurred on the introduction and modernization of the system than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The co-operation of both control institutions took place on the basis of the Agreement on Co-operation in the performance of parallel controls focused on the administration of excise duties dated 18 August 2015.
The SAO CR and the SAO SR have agreed to carry out parallel inspections, which will be primarily focused on the issue of excise tax administration and the results of which will enable analysis, mutual comparison and evaluation of the findings.
Common audit questions were agreed on which the parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject and goals of parallel control:
The aim of the parallel audits was to compare the performance of excise administrators, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the excise administration process.
In particular, the following main audit questions were to be answered:
Did the excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic achieve comparable values ​​of qualitative indicators while incurring comparable expenditures?
Has the introduction of the electronic Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) streamlined the administration of excise duties and has the costs of implementing it been spent effectively?
The performed parallel inspections were to identify the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, especially in the area of ​​legislation and the setting of the organizational structure.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The General Directorate of Customs (GDC) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (FR of the Slovak Republic) have joined the joint declaration on mutual cooperation of the Visegrad Four countries. rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint actions to increase the effectiveness of fraud detection and the sharing of experiences and best practices.
1 The EMCS is operated in accordance with Decision No 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on computerising the movement and surveillance of excisable products.
Identification of the inspection performed by the SAO CR
Inspection number: 15/33
Subject of control: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the audit: The objective of the SAO CR's audit was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, especially in monitoring shipments in the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and in securing tax (customs debts); verify whether the system of administration of excise duties is set up in such a way as to ensure the efficiency of the collection of state budget revenues.
Controlled period: 2012–2015 and, in the case of factual connections, also the previous and subsequent periods
Person inspected: General Directorate of Customs
Identification of the inspection performed by the SAO SR
Inspection number: KA-023/2016/1050
Subject of control: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the audit: The objective of the audit was an independent and objective review of whether the FR SR and customs offices (CÚ) in the administration of excise duties operate economically, efficiently and effectively in accordance with generally binding legal regulations.
Control period: 2012-2015
Controlled entity: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation for excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Excise tax administration legislation is divided into the level of EU legislation (see Annex 1) and the level of national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118 / EC, on the general arrangements for excise duty and repealing Directive 92/12 / EEC, defines excise duty and lays down basic rules for the administration of taxes and for the treatment of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive makes it possible to impose consumption taxes on other products as well.
EU legislation regulates in particular the minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for individual types of selected products, production, storage, processing and holding of taxable products, tax liability, tax exemptions and refunds, supervision of transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and maintenance of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows for the establishment of control procedures and institutes at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Excise tax legislation in the Czech Republic
Definition of legal regulations in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legal regulation of excise duties is concentrated in the Act on Excise Duties (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.), Which regulates the administration of taxes on mineral oils, taxes on alcohol, taxes on tobacco products, taxes on beer, taxes on wine and intermediate products. and taxes on raw tobacco.
This law defines the forms of handling products subject to excise duty, taxpayers, permitting procedures, conditions for the transport of products, tax returns and sanctions for violations of legal regulations.
The Act and related decrees further regulate some other conditions for the handling of mineral oils (labeling of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and storage of raw tobacco for purposes other than tobacco production.
Taxes on other energy products (ie natural gas and some other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in sections 45 to 47 of Act No. 261/2007 Coll., On the stabilization of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are also contained in special legal regulations. Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, issue, distribution of fuels and keeping records of fuels released for free tax circulation.
Act No. 61/1997 Coll., On alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll., On mandatory labeling of alcohol, and relevant implementing regulations stipulate mandatory labeling of alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for handling control tapes and conditions for handling alcohol (ie for production, processing, sale or other transfer , transport, transportation, storage, acceptance, use, holding, import or export of alcohol).
Procedures for tax proceedings, which are not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., The Tax Code.
Sanctions are imposed in accordance with Act No. 500/2004 Coll., Administrative Procedure Code.
Conditions for issuing a trade license (concession) to operate the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, processing and sale of fermented alcohol, potable alcohol and spirits" are regulated by Act No. 455/1991 Coll., On trade licensing (Trade Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has used the power to introduce control procedures and institutes for the control of transport of selected products in free tax circulation and for supervising compliance with legal regulations in the handling of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as in the handling of selected products for which tax has already been taken away.
These include monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and raw tobacco, the labeling of some other mineral oils, the labeling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic has used the right to apply excise duty to other products and has introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
Based on the Resolution of the Government of the Czech Republic of 3 October 2012 No. 735, on the implementation of the “Zero Tolerance Plan for the Black Market in Spirits”, major legislative changes were made in the Czech Republic in 2012–2015, introducing a number of measures against tax fraud on excise duty on alcohol.
In the same period, there were also fundamental changes in the legislation on the tax on mineral oils, the tax on tobacco products and the criminalization of the preparation of tax cuts.
Criminal law protection of tax revenues
With effect from 1 July 2016, the criminal offense of preparing the crime of "reduction of tax, fee and similar mandatory payment" is introduced. The amendment made should enable police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, such as the deployment of operational investigative measures.
General provisions of the administration of excise duties
With effect from 1 January 2015, the issuance of a permit for the handling of products subject to excise duty pursuant to the Act on Excise Duties is conditional on: reliability; debtlessness; economic stability; the authorization to operate a trade enabling the pursuit of an authorization-related activity; situations where the petitioner is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The aim of the legal regulation was mainly to solve the problem of the occurrence of tax arrears, namely by reducing the entities authorized to dispose of products subject to excise duty taxation.
The condition of economic stability now allows the tax administrator to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both within the permitting procedure and after the issuance of the permit.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities that do not have sufficient financial income to properly fulfill their tax obligations from disposing of selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the petitioner, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labor productivity) were determined, on the basis of which a financial analysis is performed.
In addition to these indicators, it also depends on the administrative discretion of the tax administrator with regard to the individual conditions of the proceedings.
The law stipulates the periodicity of verification of the fulfillment of the condition of economic stability due to the topicality of data - the verification takes place once a year in connection with the deadline for filing income tax returns.
The tax administrator has the opportunity to set other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the permit holder does not meet the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the permit, or cancel it with a delay.
Of the total number of 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of tax security (eg repeated beneficiaries).
The permit was revoked for ten entities, the other applicants increased the tax security, capitalized their contribution to the company or documented current accounting data, according to which they already met all the conditions for issuing the permit.
In addition to the petitioner, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must also be met by a natural person who is or is a statutory body or a natural person who is neither the petitioner's statutory body nor its member but performs this activity (chaining of legal entities as a statutory body or its member , so - called connected entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 connected entities had been inspected.
The records kept pursuant to the Act on Excise Duties (Sections 37 to 40 and Section 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) Contain data on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, taken over, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of disposal procedure (conditional exemption, import, reintroduction, conditional exemption, export, free tax circulation, own consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the consignee or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of occurrence of the event and the entry in the register;
transport of selected products (eg means of transport, carriers, transport numbers);
registration numbers of related documents;
notification of the release for free circulation of alcohol in consumer packaging marked with a control tape and information on its distribution.
A record of acceptance after transport must be made immediately after its completion.
In the case of records kept electronically, the records must be kept or allow output in the format xls, xlsx, par.
Alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a set of measures aimed at providing a detailed overview of the activities of entities (see Annex 3, Scheme A) from raw alcohol production through marking with control tape to its distribution to the final seller or authorized user of exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, production facilities for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation, are also subject to customs supervision.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of alcohol processing and production of spirits and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the handling of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labeling of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of production, receipt, stocks and release of alcohol contain information on the amount of alcohol according to the various stages of production and processing of alcohol, with the numbers of documents.
Limitation of the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and limitation of the number of packages with a broken control tape at the place of final sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other packaging with a volume of max. One liter, resp. three liters in the case of a container made of glass.
