Spirits in larger packages are considered unlabelled and prohibited.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his personal consumption, there may be a maximum of one consumer package with a broken control tape, or three, if they are equipped with a one-way valve.
Mandatory registration of a person who places alcohol in consumer packaging products with at least 15% by volume of alcohol for free circulation and is: an importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under conditional tax exemption, provided that personal and technical conditions are met .
Personal conditions - reliability, integrity and non-expression of a ban on activity - must be met by the applicant and a person in the position of a statutory body or a responsible representative.
The applicant must provide a deposit of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (ie approx. € 3,700 to € 185,000), depending on the expected amount of control strips collected.
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for marking alcohol and equipping the place of marking or the tax warehouse with a camera monitoring device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
Registration markings of the control tape are introduced for the marking of spirits with a volume greater than 0.06 liters.
When transporting control tapes, the registration mark of the control tapes must be stated in the transport documents or customs declaration at export.
Until 30 November 2013, the control tape contained a ten-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration sampling number, a code for the application for the allocation of control tapes and a classification code according to the level of ethanol volume concentration.
From 1 December 2013, the control tape now contains two types of identifiers and the amount of alcohol in the consumer package expressed in milliliters of ethanol at 20 ° C, rounded down to the nearest milliliter.
The record of control tapes for marking spirits contains daily records of individual methods of handling control tapes according to registration codes, as well as documents on the basis of which the entry was made.
In the event of destruction, loss or theft of specific control tapes, their holder is obliged to notify the tax administrator electronically of the registration code of the control tapes concerned and their number by the next working day after the decisive fact.
Introduction of a new factual nature of torts and adjustment of the amount of sanctions imposed for breaches of legal regulations in the handling of control tapes.
Sanctions can be imposed up to the amount of excise duty or exceed it up to ten times (eg in case of destruction or loss of control tapes in excess of 0.1% of the total quantity of an individual control tape order, in case of non-return of the control tape within the statutory period).
Restriction of the handling of control tapes only to registered holders, who may not pass them on to another person, except for their provision to a foreign supplier for the purpose of marking spirits in consumer packaging produced outside the Czech Republic.
Exported control tapes must be placed on the consumer package and re-imported no later than nine months after receipt from the tax administrator.
Mandatory registration of an alcohol distributor in consumer packaging, provided that similar personal conditions are met as for the person obliged to mark alcohol and with the obligation to pay a deposit of up to CZK 5,000,000 (ie approx. € 185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in consumer packaging.
Authorized persons are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or to final sellers, or they may sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency administrator, an administrative body, organizational units of the state or unregistered persons during the execution of tax execution.
Notices on the release of alcohol or sale in consumer packaging for free circulation are required to be sent to alcohol administrators and distributors immediately the day after the decisive fact by the tax administrator via the information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or in compliance with xml content.
The notification shall include the number of control tapes used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the percentage by volume of alcohol, the European Commodity Code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller, as well as the product name and production batch.
In 2014 and 2015, tax entities sent approximately 10.5 million notifications.
Mandatory concession (specific form of trade license) not only for the production and processing of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or another legal or entrepreneurial natural person for his own internal use.
Concessioned trades can be performed only after a decision has been issued by the Trades Licensing Office if the professional competence and other conditions are met.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit for tax administrators is an overview of sellers and their establishments and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, in 2014, for the field including the production, processing of fermented alcohol, potable alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales, approx. and in 2015 approx. 104 thous. concessions.
Inspections of compliance with legal regulations in the area of ​​handling excisable products in the Czech Republic are also ensured by the following: trade licensing authorities, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, and the Czech Trade Inspection Authority.
If it finds that there has been a breach of duty or a breach of the prohibition, it shall immediately inform the excise duty administrator.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has introduced a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex 3, Scheme B), to which mineral oils subject to excise duty are subject, but also selected mineral oils not subject to excise duty, which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from the production of mineral oil through storage, transport, labeling and coloring of selected mineral oils, labeling of some other mineral oils to delivery to the final consumer or user and in some cases the consumption of mineral oils.
The supervision of the customs authorities also includes the production of marking substances for the marking of mineral oils and the handling of these substances.
Mineral oils listed under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (other kerosene), 2710 19 29 (other intermediate oils not mentioned elsewhere) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49 are subject to the marking and coloring of selected mineral oils. if their marking is prohibited.
The labeling of some other mineral oils is subject to, for example, benzene, toluene, xylene and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion.
It is possible to mark and color selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marking substance only with the permission of the tax administrator.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring the handling of special mineral oils, which is a group of mineral oils falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 1999 (ie lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion), the kinematic viscosity at 40 ° C of which is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and having at least one of the following characteristics: flash point less than 150 ° C, distillation at least 20% by volume, including losses, up to 350 ° C, by distillation.
These mineral oils have been misused as an additive in finished fuels, especially diesel, or have been used or sold directly to power engines because their physical properties are very similar.
Entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 liters must register with the tax administrator.
In order to be registered, the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be met, which applies at all times 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
3 Council Regulation (EEC) No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 Eg. when using mineral oil as a fuel (except for water voyages, unless they are private recreational craft) or as a component for the production of fuels, if the marking is detrimental to their use.
registration.
As of 30 November 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations; four registrations were canceled at the proposal of the registration holder.
The electronic records must contain detailed information on the receipt, own consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, notification numbers acquired by the tax authorities, places of storage and consumption, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption or, on sale, place of delivery and customer registration number.
Notification of any acquisition of special mineral oil must be made to the tax administrator 24 to 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the special mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of consumption or information on the sale or transfer shall be reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed in the relevant year shall be submitted by the entity together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notification of the purpose of use and marking, the place of storage or consumption, and the identification of the person to whom the special mineral oil is resold or transferred shall be given before each change.
Notifications are submitted electronically via intelligent forms or a PDF data box.
In 2015, persons handling special mineral oils submitted 630 notifications.
The tax administrator must declare the seizure and confiscation of special mineral oils or a means of transport in cases where he finds out the handling of special mineral oils without registration or when the registered person fails to fulfill his notification obligation.
As in the case of non-compliance with the obligations in respect of the transport of products subject to excise duty, these deficiencies cannot be remedied subsequently.
Registration of a fuel distributor is mandatory for persons who sell or are authorized to sell fuel.
Only persons meeting the following criteria may be registered fuel distributors:
Mandatory concession of the trade license office (specific form of trade license).
The customs office examines the application for a concession, or the appointment of a responsible representative, which examines whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or members of the statutory body of the applicant - legal entity and the appointed responsible representative meet the condition of reliability.
If these persons meet the condition of reliability, the customs office issues a favorable opinion.
A reliable person is a person of good character, namely in terms of criminal property, customs and tax law.
The condition for issuing a concession is professional competence.
Indebtedness of the same circle of persons as in the case of reliability.
A debt-free person is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will duly and timely fulfill his payment obligations to the state, ie he has no arrears on the state budget and general health insurance.
A fuel distributor may not be prohibited from being judged by a court or administrative authority.
The fuel distributor must not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit (or bank guarantee) in the amount of CZK 20,000,000 (ie approx. € 740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (ie approx. € 370,000) after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and fulfillment of other conditions .
The distributor is obliged to submit the notification of fuel distribution to the customs office within 20 days after the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification must contain information on the individual purchase and sale of fuels.
The reported data are data on business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The right to a refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
A refund of excise duty on mineral oils can only be claimed for an activity that is clearly related to the activity carried out on land.
In 2015, it was about 64 thousand. of claims for tax refund in the total amount of CZK 1,172,844,680 (ie € 43,401,720).
Since 2017, the government of the Czech Republic has also introduced a refund of excise duty on fuel to farmers with animal production.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats will be able to claim this right.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products at the old tax rate
In response to the long-term failure to achieve budgeted revenues from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced, with effect from 1 December 2014, restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid using tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco label means its placement on a unit package (Section 116 of the Act on Excise Duties).
The production of the tobacco product in the state intended for the final consumer is decisive for the application of the rate of excise duty, and it does not have to be removed from storage, delivery, dispatch or sale, or sale to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterizing the rate of excise duty is indicated on the tobacco label together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, the label also indicates the number of pieces in the package, respectively. amount of smoking tobacco in kilograms.
The tobacco label has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the resale of unit packets of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco label with the previous (old) tax rate was set until the last day of the second calendar month following the entry into force of the new rate of excise duty.
The development of tobacco labeling in 2014 and a comparison with previous years show that tobacco manufacturers have significantly pre-supplied tobacco products with an "old" tax rate each year, effectively shifting the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Raw tobacco tax
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the production of tobacco products without the permission of the tax administrator and non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as a measure against tax fraud.
With effect from 1 July 2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, delivered to another Member State or a third country or for which the origin, purpose of use or person to whom the raw material has been or is intended has been established is subject to excise duty. tobacco delivered.
Restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco
Measures such as supervision of the transport and production of tobacco products, marking of unit packets with control tape and restrictions on sales at defined places have been supplemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Production facilities for the processing of tobacco raw materials and the production of tobacco products are not subject to customs supervision.
Raw tobacco may be stored for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products only by a registered person, but such tobacco may not be further processed or processed.
A registered person can only be a person who meets the personal conditions of the applicant, statutory body and responsible representative, which applies throughout the registration.
The conditions of registration are: a) authorization to operate a trade enabling the activity of a person storing raw tobacco, b) reliability, c) indebtedness, d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been banned from carrying out activities, e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, f) providing a deposit of CZK 20,000,000 (ie approx. € 740,000).
The electronic records must contain the date of receipt or issue of raw tobacco, the number of the document, the identification of the trading partner, information on the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of each acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco must be made to the tax authorities 24 to 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
Data on the trading partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the storage address, the purpose of use and the details of the carrier shall be reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity of raw tobacco received or dispatched in the relevant year shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications are submitted electronically via a data box in PDF format.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the prescribed particulars.
Excise tax legislation in the Slovak Republic
The legal framework regulating the area of ​​excise duties in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation, and thus co-creates its uniform tax system.
Individual types of excise duties are exhaustively determined by the legislation of the Slovak Republic, which is similar to the legislation of neighboring countries.
Definition of legal regulations in the Slovak Republic
Legislative regulation of excise duties is ensured by four laws according to individual tax subjects.
Harmonization was achieved by the adoption of the following acts on excise duties: Act No. 98/2004 Coll., On excise duty on mineral oils, Act No. 106/2004 Coll., On excise duty on tobacco products, Act No. 530 / 2011 Coll., On excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No. 609/2007 Coll., On excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All laws on excise duties are regulations of substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No. 563/2009 Coll., On Tax Administration (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulates tax administration, rights and obligations of tax entities and other persons.
This legal framework transposed the individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118 / EC of 16 December 2008 on the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12 / EEC, and transposed the provisions of other European Community directives and legislation.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Slovak Republic
Since 2011, the legislation concerning the administration of excise duties has undergone several fundamental changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS system, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duty under the duty suspension arrangement has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system, where these transports are monitored in real time.
Within the EMCS electronic system, the institute of suspending access of tax subjects to the EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The customs office has the possibility to suspend access precisely when there is a justified fear of overdue or unspecified tax from previous tax periods and its unenforceability.
This concerns the due date of the tax, as the transport of excise goods requires the lodging of a security, which, however, is released upon termination of the transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A fundamental change in the administration of the excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility of using so-called red diesel was abolished.
The designated gas oil, commonly also called red diesel, was a mineral oil.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific purposes defined by law, such as agriculture, and its use was favored by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of abolishing red oil was to reduce the public finance deficit, simplify the taxation system for mineral oils and reduce the administrative burden on the businesses involved.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely the fuel retailer.
The purpose of this legal change was to introduce the obligation to keep records for all gas stations.
Transparency of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely the fuel distributor and the fuel consumer.
The change contributed to the elimination of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and clarified the movement of these fuels (see Annex 4, Scheme A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
In the Slovak Republic, however, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to be labeled.
Excise duty on tobacco products
As part of the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw materials, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Materials Act was extended and a new tax entity was introduced - a tobacco raw materials trader.
The tobacco raw material is not a harmonized tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, the obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products was introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for labeling consumer packages of tobacco products.
The control marks are cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control marks must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically, via the information system for the collection of control marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax subject and the tax administrator.
One state printing house of control stamps was established - in the Kremnice Mint.
The performance of tax supervision over the printing of control marks was also introduced.
The changes significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system of printing stamps strengthens the system of inspection of goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, which can be used to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
Unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd place is the checksum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th- 12th place is a decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
The control mark intended to mark cigarettes must also indicate the price of the cigarettes, the mark for the validity of the rate of excise duty, the number of cigarettes in the consumer package and the length of the cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer, because the original three provisions of substantive law were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The Act was drafted mainly due to the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of taxation of alcoholic beverages, solutions for their production, monitoring of movement, tax security, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, streamline tax administration, reduce administrative burdens for small and medium-sized businesses.
The new way of solving the problem of taxation of individual types of alcoholic beverages introduced the application of a uniform rate of excise duty on alcoholic beverages and took into account the volume percentage of the actual alcohol content.
For sparkling wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the volume percentage of the actual alcoholic strength of the finished product shall be taken into account.
The beer concentration is also expressed as a volume percentage of the actual alcohol content of the finished product.
The category of small producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which consists in the exemption from excise duty for an individual who produces sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household in a maximum quantity of 1,000 liters per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for labeling consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control marks must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically, via the information system for the collection of control marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax subject and the tax administrator.
One state printing house of control stamps was established - in the Kremnice Mint.
The performance of tax supervision over the printing of control marks was also introduced.
The changes significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Scheme B) and the elimination of counterfeiting of control marks.
The new system of printing stamps strengthens the system of inspection of goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, which can be used to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
Unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd place is the checksum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a check mark or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th- 12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one joint act No. 353/2003 Coll.
The tax on solid fuels, the tax on natural gas and some other gases and the tax on electricity are part of Act No. 261/2007 Coll.
In contrast, in the Slovak Republic, each excise duty is regulated by a special law, except for the law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, which includes a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates the excise tax on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, as of 1 January 2015, the issuance of permits for the handling of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Duty Act is conditional, inter alia, on proving the economic stability of applicants, which the customs authorities verify annually by performing a financial analysis.
In the Slovak Republic, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding on waiving or reducing tax security.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic performs tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control marks for marking alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printer and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of control stamps is provided by the state-owned company Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco labels and control tapes in the Czech Republic is not subject to customs supervision in the printer.
Tobacco stickers and control tapes will be taken over from the printer by the authorized territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers at this territorial workplace, and control tapes for marking alcohol are further distributed to the individual locally competent tax administrators according to the place of marking.
The legal regulations of the Czech Republic do not define the manufacturer of tobacco labels and control tapes.
In the Slovak Republic there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or its part, in the Czech Republic such an obligation is not introduced.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco label bears the excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when the tobacco labels are collected at the authorized customs office.
In contrast, in the Slovak Republic, the control mark does not include excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced in the audited period in the case of their use for agricultural crop production, so-called green diesel.
Since 2017, this tax refund has been extended to livestock production.
Such support for farmers has not been introduced in the Slovak Republic (it existed until 31 December 2010 as so-called red diesel).
To strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of CZK 20 million (ie € 740 thousand) was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic.
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1,891 entities in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (ie a decrease of 1,717 tax entities).
A similar institute of a fuel distributor has been introduced in the Slovak Republic, but without the deposit required to ensure the excise duty on mineral oils.
In 2014, 303 distributors were registered in the Slovak Republic and in 2015, 407 distributors were registered.
In the Slovak Republic, the institute of a fuel seller and a fuel consumer has been established, to which a permit is issued by the locally competent customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to labeling; in the Slovak Republic, after the abolition of so-called red diesel, the labeling of mineral oils is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the control tape for marking alcohol contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of alcohol and a twelve-digit registration code with an indication of the spirits of the spirit, according to which the records of control tapes are kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the control tape shall be entered in the register on the following working day.
The tape holder is obliged to notify their use within the same period.
In the Slovak Republic, the control mark intended for marking alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique twelve-digit identification number, which, if used, is communicated to the tax administrator once a month and serves to verify the authenticity of the control mark.
The records contain the number of collected, used and claimed control marks.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have introduced the institute of compulsory registration, resp. alcohol distributor records.
In the Slovak Republic, the registration is conditioned by the fulfillment of conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; an annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least € 100,000 or a paid-up share capital of at least € 100,000; minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining a registration is conditioned, among other things, by depositing a deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (ie € 185,000) in favor of the tax administrator for the entire period of validity of the registration.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
In the Slovak Republic, the permanent presence of a tax administrator is required for the production of alcohol, not only in consumer packaging.
In the Czech Republic, in the production of alcohol in consumer packaging, a special form of registration of a person obliged to mark alcohol is required, subject to a deposit in favor of the tax administrator in the amount of CZK 100,000 (ie € 3,700) up to CZK 5,000,000 (ie € 185,000). ) according to the number of control tapes removed and the installation of a monitoring device with continuous access by the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic far exceeds the minimum EU requirements for the subject and administration of excise duties and responds to the identified risks from other Member States as well as to the risks identified in the tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax administrations to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, as part of the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw materials (eg leaves), an excise tax on raw tobacco was introduced in addition to EU legislation, resp. tobacco raw materials.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw material are not a harmonized tobacco product, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic monitor their movement.
The SAO CR and the SAO SR may recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability of applicants for permits under the Excise Tax Act has proved its worth, as it reduces the risks of tax arrears.
For this reason, both control institutions recommend applying such inspections also in the conditions of the Slovak Republic.
The distribution of control stamps in the Slovak Republic is more efficient than in the Czech Republic, because it does not burden the customs authorities with costs related to transport between the printer and the customer of control tapes and tobacco labels.
The Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the existence and location of technological equipment for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, it is more efficient to collect the tax on tobacco products, because the order of the tobacco label itself is a tax return with subsequent payment of the tax.
Thanks to the introduction of the "fuel seller" and "fuel consumer" institutes, the Financial Administration in the Slovak Republic has a better overview of fuel sales points.
The introduction of mandatory labeling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic enables easier control of the misuse of mineral oils with a reduced tax rate, resp. exempt from tax.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and in the Slovak Republic (2014), a new control tape was introduced, resp. stamp containing the identification code.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation has waived its introduction.
Impacts cannot yet be assessed due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
Introduction of effective labeling of consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark, resp. tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO SR and the SAO CR may recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States as well.
The position of the Slovak Republic on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterized by a pro-client approach, which does not block the financial resources of tax subjects.
On the other hand, the Czech Republic's approach is rather restrictive, as it introduces a deposit burdening the cash flow of tax subjects, but further reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Development of revenues from excise duties
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the state in order to increase state budget revenues and also to regulate the amount of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to individuals and / or society (regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Commission Communication: EUROPE 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3 March 2010 under the Less Resource-Intensive Europe flagship initiative, the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, including through a tax review. energy with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfill the EC's intention, Member States should strive to shift the tax burden from the labor force to, among other things, energy and environmental taxation, in the context of greater "greening" of tax systems.
Collection of excise taxes on excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic includes collection of excise duties on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share in GDP is monitored, among others, by the Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD).
Both SAIs used the following selection criteria to query the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share in GDP decreased slightly according to OECD data.
The exchange rate of the European Central Bank of the ECB was used to convert amounts in CZK to € as at 31 December of the respective year.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against € in 2013 weakened by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25,140 to 27,425).
The main reason was the monetary policy decision of the CNB Board of Governors on 7 November 20136.
The resulting values ​​of collection of excise duties, excise duty rates and per capita income in € decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant decrease in the share of excise duties in 2014 was caused by a one-off shortfall in excise duty revenues from tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate.
The share of excise duties is also affected by the growth in the collection of income taxes, which has increased significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation in the Czech Republic.
The excise tax on mineral oils has the largest share in the total collection of excise duties (approximately 55.7% in 2015), but this fell despite the significant growth of the economy compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although in 2013 the registration of fuel distributors was introduced as a measure against tax fraud.
The trend in environmentally efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels have a negative effect on tax revenue.
The tax on natural gas, the tax on solid fuels and the tax on electricity have a negligible share, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to neighboring countries.
Unless rates are increased, their share will decline in the future due to the ever-decreasing energy intensity of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a large-scale case of tax fraud consisting in the marketing of untaxed alcohol, alcohol containing methanol or insufficiently denatured alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a number of measures against such conduct and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the collection from 2012 by € 4 million.
The share of the tobacco tax has increased as a result of rising rates.
The basic rates of excise duties changed between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on tobacco products, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64 / EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
Due to the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, excluding the tax on tobacco products, fell significantly. For tobacco products, it increased only slightly.
In relation to price growth, GDP or living standards, the indexation of the rate of excise duties is not set, so the functions of excise duties consisting in the regulation of socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With the economic growth of the Czech Republic and the growth of living standards, real excise tax rates are decreasing.
7 Indexation - automatic adjustment of a certain economic variable to inflation, this adjustment takes place on the basis of a law or a contract (for pensions paid by the state, it is called valorisation).
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
The current legislative regulation of excise duties in the Slovak Republic does not address the indexation of the level of excise duties on the development of consumer prices, because they are fixed.

Of all the excise taxes introduced in Slovakia, the largest share in the annual tax revenues of the state budget is the excise tax on mineral oils, while its share did not fall below 52% in the entire audited period.
The second largest share is reported by the excise duty on tobacco products.
On average, this tax accounts for approximately 32% of the total excise duty collection.
Between 2012 and 2015, there was an increase in the collection of excise duty per capita in the Slovak Republic.
This development is due to the growth of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The growth in the collection of excise duties per capita in the Slovak Republic is constant and corresponds to the development of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decline in per capita income is influenced by the CNB's intervention in the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which in the Czech Republic is about 2.7 times, resp. 2.8 times higher, but per capita in the Czech Republic, the collection for these selected products is only about 1/3 higher.
The reason is the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK against € for foreign consumers.
The tax on mineral oils is also due to greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, the growing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border shopping have a significant impact.
Evaluation Real excise duty rates in the Czech Republic declined as a result of CNB interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in total tax revenues is not rising and there is no shift from labor taxation to consumption taxation of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved values ​​of the share of excise duties are consistently above the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is mainly affected by changes in excise duty rates, the development of the economic condition and the behavior of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures, which the state subsidizes in various forms, will have to be replaced by other revenues or reductions in state expenditures.
The non-introduction of indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic reduces their regulatory functions and insufficiently supports the EU's goals of a Europe less dependent on environmentally unsustainable resources and on reducing its dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic reflects the higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is affected by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the relationship between expenditures and revenues related to the administration of excise duties, ie it expresses the amount of expenditures per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The effectiveness of the tax administrator in tax administration affects the scope and organizational structure of the tax administrator, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of electronic activities.
The determination of the efficiency of administrative costs of tax administration by the method of conversion coefficient is based on the number of employees participating in the administration of excise duties in a line-managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is performed, among other activities, by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is an independent organizational unit of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration is provided by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs administration bodies are an internal organizational unit, costs and revenues are included in aggregate for the entire organizational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility of comparing the efficiency of the administration of excise duties, the expenditures and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were also included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative acts performed mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial inspections are performed by other public administration bodies, but their importance is negligible.
The administration of excise duties is performed mainly by the following departments:
General Directorate of Customs
Department 23 TAX
Department 231 - Tax Methodology monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures the interpretation of legal regulations, methodically manages and coordinates: the implementation of tax administration agendas and related regulations, especially tax proceedings and related control and supervisory activities, transport administration of selected products;
Department 232 - ELO and Search performs searches and methodically manages transport controls of selected products and ensures international cooperation between ELO and EMCS;
Department 233 - Tax Controls methodically manages and coordinates the performance of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Department 301 - Legal performs methodological activities in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative proceedings, the process of tax audits, registration proceedings, finding proceedings, payment of taxes, fines for late claim of tax, penalties and interest;
Department 302 - Administrative activities performs decision-making activities in cases where the legislation stipulates the competence of the GDC, eg deciding on the delegation of the entity's local affiliation to another competent tax administrator, deciding on attraction, ie taking over the case by a superior tax administrator, appealing against decisions of customs offices and examines incentives for inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Department 303 - Revenue and Enforcement Administration methodically manages, coordinates and performs the fulfillment of tasks within the framework of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the fulfillment of tasks in the area of ​​insolvency proceedings;
Department 60 ANALYZES AND INFORMATION SUPPORT
Department 601 - Risk and Criminal Analyzes provides and performs risk analyzes and participates in the management of executive risks and the planning of control activities and control actions;
Department 604 - Financial Analysis performs financial analysis in the customs administration, especially within the permitting procedure.
Customs offices perform activities within the agenda in various places in the region and the agendas are scattered in several places:
Department 02 - Analyzes and information support, which performs risk analyzes, management of risk profiles and collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Section 1 LEGAL
Department 11 - Legal and administrative activities, which prepares documents, opinions and submission reports for the appellate body, issues decisions on permits in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the law on mandatory labeling of alcohol and the law on alcohol, decides on ensuring payment for tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Department 3 - TAX
Department 31 - Tax, which carries out the agendas of: tax supervision of tax subjects, eg control of compliance with the conditions set out in issued permits, supervision of functionality and correctness of production facilities for alcohol production and determination of quantity and concentration of alcohol produced, expert supervision of alcohol denaturation, physical checks in the field of excise administration; non-tax inspections in the area of ​​inspections on the basis of laws indirectly related to excise duties, in particular inspection of mandatory labeling and coloring of selected mineral oils, inspection of taxation of selected products, inspection of labeling of tobacco products, inspection of sellers or buyers in violation of prices and other price regulations, performs acts in connection with the Act on Fuels, performs acts in connection with the Act on Mandatory Labeling of Alcohol and the Act on Alcohol, performs acts in connection with the fulfillment of the obligation of the minimum amount of biofuels for free tax circulation for transport purposes; registration of economic entities for taxes, registration of persons obliged to mark alcohol and distributors of alcohol and registration of fuel distributors; tax administration, in particular conducting tax proceedings in the matter of assessment and prescription, or refund of tax, monitoring of tax security and its use for tax payment, conducting searches;
Department 39 - Tobacco Labels and Control Tapes - is an organizational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and performs activities in the area of ​​ordering, production and distribution and disposal of tobacco labels and control tapes.
Representatives of the customs office and the GDC are present at the disposal of returned / damaged tobacco labels, who supervise the disposal process and draw up a record of the disposal.
In the case of control tapes for the marking of alcohol, the director of the customs office appoints a three-member commission for the disposal of discarded uncollected / returned control tapes by shredding by an internal procedure.
After the physical shredding of the control tapes, the chairman of the liquidation commission shall ensure the recording of data on the destroyed control tapes;
Committee 5 - CONTROL,
Department 52 - Tax Audits performs tax audits;
Committee 6 - SUPERVISION
Department 61 - Supervision of entities supervises entities at points of sale, eg control of sales of spirits and tobacco products;
Department 62 - Mobile Surveillance controls the transport of selected products along the way.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a demanding transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS program.
The establishment of the FR SR was also reflected in the composition of employees of the newly established departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In connection with the performance of excise tax administration, activities related to excise tax administration within the organizational structure of the FR SR were integrated into a larger number of different sections and related departments.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Customs and Tax Section of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic Department of Excise Duties (all-Slovak competence):
excise duty department - directs and coordinates activities in the field of excise tax administration; prepares expert opinions; submits proposals and comments on legislative changes; issues decisions on the delegation of local jurisdiction to taxable persons; assigns and cancels registration subscription numbers;
Tax Supervision Department - directs and coordinates activities in the area of ​​tax supervision and tax control; performs tax supervision;
ELO and SPD systems department - directs and coordinates the activities of mutual administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through the SEED and MVS systems; provides management and updates in SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
Control Stamps Department - directs activities in the field of printing and handling of control stamps; performs tax supervision over the loading and disposal of printing sheets and control stamps in the printer.
Department of the Vice President of Financial Administration
Department of Remedies for Excise Duties and Customs (nationwide competence):
Excise Tax Appeals Department - reviews the decisions of customs offices on the basis of ordinary and extraordinary remedies applied; appeal proceedings at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The Customs Offices section was established during 2012; it directly involved the individual customs offices (9 customs offices), which have a territorial jurisdiction determined by the higher territorial units, with the exception of one customs office, which was set up, inter alia, to carry out tasks related to the Community's external border.
Customs offices:
excise duties department - performance of methodological activities in relation to branches of customs offices and stations of customs offices; for selected entities, the tax administrator performs direct actions, and this decides on registration (tax warehouse, authorized recipient, repeated, registered consignor), the amount of tax security, determines and refunds the tax, performs tax supervision and tax control; decides on the waiver of the tax security; decides to waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee in a tax warehouse for alcohol;
legal department - decision-making activity in the matter of tax violations; activities related to ordinary and extraordinary remedies; tax enforcement proceedings;
branch of the customs office - decides on registration (with the exception of the tax warehouse, the authorized recipient for repeated receipt, the registered consignor), the amount of tax security; prescribes and refunds the tax; performs tax supervision and tax control; decides on security and confiscation of goods;
customs office - performance of tax supervision over the holding and movement of goods subject to excise duty; ensures the performance of permanent tax supervision in the tax warehouse for alcohol; decides on security and confiscation of goods.
Expenditures of the Slovak financial administration on the administration of excise duties are constantly growing, as, with the exception of wage growth, investments in effective tax administration and electronic financial administration are increasing.
Although excise revenue was growing, spending was growing faster due to IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
Wage expenditures in the Slovak Republic are significantly affected by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol, which is not applied by the Czech Republic.
Expenditures of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on the administration of excise duties between 2012 and 2015 increased more significantly in 2015, this growth was mainly due to an increase in wage expenditures and expenditures on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise duties also grew at approximately the same rate.
Compared to the Slovak Republic, wage expenditures in the Czech Republic are positively affected by the broader competencies of the customs administration, such as weighing trucks, monitoring the fulfillment of obligations in connection with tolls.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the Slovak Republic shows a slightly deteriorating trend year-on-year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditures per employee increased.
Also in the Czech Republic, the number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditures per employee grew more slowly than in the Slovak Republic.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, wage growth is a significant factor in the worsened efficiency of administrative expenditures, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a significant administrative burden in the administration of excise duties appears to be a negative factor, which is confirmed by the non-decreasing number of employees in the area of ​​excise administration.
In the Slovak Republic, however, the administration of excise duties at lower incomes is significantly more demanding on staff capacity.
Performance indicators of excise administration
The administration of excise duties is a set of activities aimed at the correct detection, determination and security of tax payment.
The main processes in the administration of excise duties are tax assessment, permitting and registration for activities, transport supervision, control and search for tax subjects.
The number of administrative acts and managed entities are indicators of the performance of the tax administrator.
The mutual relationship between the monitored indicator and the number of tax administrators expresses the efficiency of the tax administrator's activities and defines the cost of a specific activity.
Authorization and registration for the activity are a basic precondition for the handling of selected products for commercial purposes and their transport in the regime of conditional exemption from tax.
The tax administrator is obliged to perform a systematic administration of entities with a permit or registration with a focus on supervising compliance with legal regulations and conditions set by the tax administrator, to which adequate human resources must be allocated.
The monitored indicator was the number of valid permits or registrations to operate as of 31 December of each year.
The number of issued permits or registrations is not the same as the number of tax subjects.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in a matter.
The monitored administrative acts are the frequency of the most significant acts of the tax administrator (tax assertion, transport administration in EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of acts ending in a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Permission and registration for activities in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
Selected products can be produced, processed, stored, received or sent with the permission of the tax administrator to operate a tax warehouse.
If the operator of a tax warehouse has more warehouses, a permit is issued for each one separately, including securing the tax.
Securing the tax is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administrator (ie the physical presence of an official and securing the equipment by the conclusions of the tax administrator).
Permanent tax supervision does not apply in the Czech Republic.
The operator of a tax warehouse also registers for tax pursuant to Section 125 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.
Authorization to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for transport of selected products conditionally exempt from tax from the place of import to the tax warehouse, to the authorized consignee in another Member State, to the place of export in another Member State or to the consignee in another Member State. Article 4 (10) of Council Directive 2008/118 / EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include permits to acquire electricity, natural gas and solid fuels without tax, which are analogous to tax warehouse permits.
The growing distillery produces alcohol with a reduced 50% tax rate (CZK 14,300 / hl of ethanol) - fruit distillates for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the operating permit is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced tax rate can be applied to 30 liters of pure alcohol per household of a grower intended for personal consumption for the production period (July-June).
The records of the growing distillery kept by the distillery operators and made available to the tax authorities must contain information on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The authorized consignee for re-acceptance of selected products and the authorized consignee for one-time acceptance of selected products are entitled to receive or re-accept selected products in a conditional system transported from another Member State on a one-off basis with the permission of the tax administrator and specified conditions.
The eligible consignee is not the operator of the tax warehouse and may not store or dispatch the selected products under the conditional tax exemption regime.
The user of selected tax-exempt products is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or pursuant to Section 52a or Section 53 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll. sells to another user selected exempt products; users have the status of taxable persons without the obligation to register for tax.
Selected exempt products can only be received and used on the basis of a valid permit, and only from the supplier specified in the permit.
Under the permit, exempt mineral oils can be sold to another holder of a use permit or a user who is authorized to use mineral oils without a permit.
Tax-exempt mineral oils can be sold without a permit in statutory cases, such as:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 liters per calendar year, if they have been produced by the user or have been generated by the user,
selected exempt mineral oils in unit packages of a capacity not exceeding 20 liters, intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production and intended for sale to the final consumer.
Selected exempt products can be transported with proof of exemption.
The distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging is entitled to sell or otherwise transfer alcohol released for free tax circulation after mandatory registration with the tax administrator.
Based on the registration with the tax administrator and the set conditions, the storer of raw tobacco is entitled to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the production of tobacco products.
A person handling special mineral oils is entitled to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils that are in bulk or placed in packages exceeding 220 liters on the basis of registration with the tax administrator and the specified conditions.
Based on the issued concession and registration of the tax administrator, the fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel on the territory of the Czech Republic under specified conditions, with the exception of the sale of fuel from a service station.
The transport of fuel must be accompanied by a tax document, a sales document or a transport document, or a delivery plan and filling tickets.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent to the tax authorities before the start of the transport.
The service station operator is the owner of the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where, with the permission of the building authority, the sale or dispensing of fuel is usually permitted in the fuel tank.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade registers filling stations and their operators, broken down into: registered - regular sale or dispensing of fuel, usually in the fuel tanks of vehicles; with limited access - operation usually in various business premises (eg quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organizations, construction yards), the sale is carried out here for the other party to a limited extent on the basis of specific contractual relationships; non-public - fuel dispensing points only for operators' own consumption.
A service station is not a structure or device in the form of a service tank located in operation (eg on a chassis) if the fuel is dispensed only for its own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to the permission of the tax administrator and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may buy, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases released for free circulation for resale with the permission of the tax administrator.
They must also have a permit if they buy or obtain liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption in excess of 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
A tax audit is a set of actions. The subject of a tax audit is tax obligations, statements of the tax subject or other circumstances decisive for the correct determination and determination of the tax related to one tax procedure.
Tax control can be performed together for several tax proceedings of one tax subject.
Repeated tax audit can be performed only under the conditions and justification stipulated by law at the beginning of the audit.
The tax audit is carried out within the tax assessment period of three years, with the period being extended by one year under the conditions stipulated by law (eg filing of additional tax proceedings, initiation of criminal proceedings in connection with the tax in question) or pending (court proceedings , international cooperation).
The deadline for tax assessment ends no later than ten years after the deadline for filing a proper tax return.
The tax administrator is not obliged to carry out a tax audit of each tax entity.
The commencement of the tax audit sets deadlines for the possibility of submitting an additional tax return or additional statement to the tax subject (Section 141 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.) And resumes the period for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
Based on its result, the tax may be assessed ex officio.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited action (one day) in which the tax administrator searches for evidence and searches the premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and packaging of tax entities and other persons involved in tax administration, on the spot outside the premises of the tax administrator (eg at the tax entity, at the point of sale, on the road during transport).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and things, take samples, or secure them.
Based on the result of the local investigation, the tax cannot be assessed separately, but the tax subject can be invited to file an additional tax return (Section 145 (2) of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
The control of traffic data in the EMCS system is not a local inquiry.
The order of control tapes for alcohol marking can be submitted to the tax administrator by the locally competent place of marking only by a registered person obliged to mark alcohol and is performed using intelligent forms, which are automatically imported into the application of the register of alcohol markers.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the ordered quantity of control tapes and orders production.
He does not supervise the production of control tapes.
Production is provided by the State Printing House of Securities, a state-owned enterprise.
The customer of the control tapes takes over the control tapes from the tax administrator of the locally relevant place of marking.
The order of tobacco stickers for marking cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco serves as a tax return.
The value of the tobacco label corresponds to the amount of tax liability, while the customer of tobacco labels is obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their removal from the tax administrator.
The customer is obliged to calculate in the order the value corresponding to the tax liability of the ordered tobacco labels.
This period applies only if the value of the tobacco labels is ensured.
The order for tobacco labels is submitted on a form set by the Ministry of Finance in writing or via a data box with the possibility of using intelligent forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is provided by the State Printing House of Securities, a state-owned enterprise.
The authorized tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (Kutná Hora Regional Office), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, which further distributes them and further verifies their transport, storage and use by customers.
Tax returns include regular tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco labels, filed by tax entities.
Tax is not included in the customs procedure on the basis of customs declarations and the declaration of claims for a refund of tax on: mineral oils used for heat production, other petrol used in business activities other than for heat production or engine propulsion, mineral oils used for primary agricultural production .
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings for dealing with identified violations of legal regulations, which are a set of consecutive administrative acts. The international exchange of information on taxable persons (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes the form of: requests for administrative cooperation, responses to requests for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, incident reports, audit reports.
Transport under the conditional tax exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech customs office is the tax administrator of the receiving or dispatching tax warehouse or authorized recipient.
Performance indicators in Slovakia
Permission and registration for activities in the Slovak Republic
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is provided primarily by the customs authorities and the Department of Excise Duties of the Customs and Tax Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Slovak Republic, whose procedure in the administration of excise duties is regulated by individual excise duty laws and the Tax Code.
These laws stipulate not only the scope of authorization for the CA and the FR of the Slovak Republic in the administration of excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax subjects in connection with the registration or payment of excise duty.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax subjects (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, which was caused by an increase in permits issued within tax warehouses, an increase in registrations of eligible beneficiaries for re-admission and registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation specified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils, as well as the notification obligation if they are transported in bulk, resp. in packages with a capacity of more than 150 liters, resp. 230 liters, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to inspection and transport to other goods, such as anti-knock products, oxidation inhibitors, resin inhibitors, viscosity improvers, anti-corrosion products.
Mandatory information has been introduced for lubricating oils regarding the indication of their kinematic viscosity.
An approximation of the registration process for selected tax entities in the sense of national legislation in the Slovak Republic is given in the following sections of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Within the framework of the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering the operator of a tax warehouse within all subjects of excise duties, a person who wants to operate a tax warehouse must also apply for registration and issue a permit for the operation of a tax warehouse.
The final decision in the registration process is a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, by which the operator of the tax warehouse acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA issues a permit for the operation of a tax warehouse, which entitles the operator of the tax warehouse in the said tax warehouse to produce, process, store, receive or send selected products under the conditional tax exemption regime.
If the operator of the tax warehouse has tax warehouses in several places, the tax administrator will issue a separate permit for the operation of the tax warehouse for each tax warehouse.
The transport of the subject of excise duty in the conditional tax exemption regime is monitored electronically via the EMCS system.
A unique reference code is generated for each shipment, the so-called
ARC code under which the shipment can be tracked online and therefore in real time.
If the operator of the tax warehouse is also a person authorized to distribute alcohol, he is obliged to notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the alcohol packaging, the volume and volume concentration of alcohol in the alcohol packaging and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging he puts into free tax circulation, at the latest on the day of its introduction.
Registered sender
A registered consignor is a special type of taxable person who cannot be registered as a tax warehouse operator at the same time, even if he sends the subject of excise duty under a duty suspension arrangement after its release for free circulation.
Within the national legislation of the Slovak Republic when registering a registered consignor within all excise duty items, a person who wants to send the excise duty item in the conditional tax exemption regime after its release into the customs regime "free circulation" must also apply to the CA for registration and issuance of permits send the subject of excise duty in this mode.
The customs office will issue a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and at the same time will also issue a permit to send the subject of excise duty in the regime of conditional exemption from tax after its release into the customs regime "free circulation".
Growing distillery
The basic act for the operation of a growing distillery is to obtain a permit for the production of alcohol in a distillery plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the permit from the Ministry does not entitle the holder of the permit to operate a growing distillery.
In order to be able to operate a growing distillery, a person must submit an application for registration and issue a certificate of registration of the growing distillery operator to the CA.
The customs office will issue a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, which also authorizes the operator of the growing distillery to produce alcohol in the growing distillery.
The purpose of the distillery is to provide services to growers.
A growing distillery cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislature allows alcohol produced in the growing distillery to apply a reduced tax rate of 50% of the basic tax rate, ie € 540 / hl and.
The reduced rate of tax shall apply to alcohol produced in a growing distillery in a quantity not exceeding 43 l a. Per grower and his household for one production period in the tax territory.
The production period lasts from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year, and therefore it is possible to apply a reduced tax rate to the alcohol produced several times within one calendar year, because the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
This is the production of alcohol outside the conditional tax exemption regime, which in practice means that the alcohol produced is in free tax circulation.
The grower pays not only the excise duty and value added tax to the grower's distillery, but also the price for the services provided.
The growing distillery issues a removal certificate to the grower, which serves not only as proof of proof of origin and method of acquisition of alcohol, but also of payment of excise duty.
The transport of alcohol produced in this way is not subject to monitoring by the tax administrator.
Importer of consumer packaging
National legislation allows persons who intend to import consumer packaging of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country in the course of their business and to release it for free circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The importer of consumer packaging does not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA issues a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate authorizes the importer to import consumer packaging of alcohol or consumer packaging of cigarettes from the territory of a third country.
At the same time, before issuing control marks, he must lodge a tax guarantee in the amount of the tax relating to the quantity of alcohol or cigarettes which he wishes to release for free circulation.
The importer of consumer packaging must release for free tax only consumer packaging marked with a control mark.
To that end, they must present to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the control marks exported to the territory of the third country.
Upon import, the importer is obliged to have the number of control marks re-imported from the territory of a third country confirmed by the customs office of importation.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer proceeds in the sense of customs regulations, where the amount of excise duty is also part of the customs debt.
In the case of release for free circulation of consumer packaging, the tax security lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
If the importer of a consumer package of alcohol is also a person authorized to distribute alcohol, he is obliged to notify the CA electronically of the trade name of the alcohol package, the volume and volume concentration of alcohol in the alcohol package and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer package he puts into free tax circulation. , at the latest on the day of its launch.
Seller of consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for the seller of consumer packaging of alcohol.
