A person wishing to hold a marketing authorization must apply to the CA for a permit and meet the legal conditions (trade license; integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes; no marketing authorization has been revoked for ten years; not in liquidation). nor in bankruptcy).
As this is a consumer package of alcohol in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
To prove the method of acquiring consumer packaging of alcohol, for example, an invoice is sufficient, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorization.
For each establishment, the permit holder is obliged to keep records for the number of received consumer packaging of alcohol, number of issued consumer packaging of alcohol, stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol as of the last day of the month and records of shortage or surplus in received and issued consumer packaging of alcohol. .
The holder of the authorization is obliged to purchase alcohol or otherwise take it in the course of business activity only from a person authorized for distribution.
Distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute, a distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person who intends to be a distribution permit must apply to the CA for a distribution permit.
The applicant must meet the legal conditions (trade license for trade; storage area exceeds 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol at least € 100,000 or paid-up share capital of at least € 100,000; minimum number of 10 employees; no arrears to customs) he has no arrears on compulsory levies, integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes, he has not been deprived of a marketing authorization for ten years;
As this is a consumer package of alcohol in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorization, is sufficient to prove the method of acquiring the consumer packaging of alcohol.
The holder of the distribution authorization is obliged to keep records for each establishment for the calendar month of the number of received consumer packaging of alcohol, the number of issued consumer packaging of alcohol, stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol on the last day of the month and records of shortage or surplus in the number of received and issued consumer packaging of alcohol.
The holder of the distribution authorization is obliged to purchase alcohol in consumer packaging only from another person authorized for distribution.
The person authorized for distribution notifies the data for each calendar month electronically, by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel seller
In order to monitor fuels in free tax circulation, as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity was introduced, namely the fuel retailer.
There is no special regulation governing filling stations in the Slovak Republic.
Therefore, filling stations are incorporated in the national legislation of the Slovak Republic as sellers of fuels.
A person who wants to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free tax circulation as part of a business activity in the tax territory is obliged to apply to the CA for a sales permit and submit a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with a suitable a certified measuring device enabling the quantity of mineral oil to be measured on receipt and dispensing, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the seller of fuels is a tax warehouse operator, an authorized consignee or a registered consignor, the CA will also automatically issue a permit for the sale of fuels to registered persons.
The fuel seller is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep records of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG for a calendar month and is also obliged to notify the CA of the new fuel supplier (distributor).
The fuel seller is obliged by law to purchase or otherwise take fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
However, when delivering fuels via a tank truck, the distributor prints a so-called bottle from the measuring device built into the tank truck when refueling the seller.
That document shall contain, in addition to information on quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
To prove the method of acquiring fuel, for example, an invoice is sufficient, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax administrator.
The tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods when performing tax supervision over mineral oils.
Above all, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks during transport, which is why hauliers use secondary roads, bypassing the toll collection system due to the difficulty of monitoring actual transports.
Transport of mineral oils in rebuilt double-bottomed tanks is also carried out.
It often happens that illegal transports are accompanied by a vehicle, which the carriers report possible mobile patrols in order to change the route and avoid roadside checks.
There is also a mixing of fuels with light fuel oils, respectively. waste oils.
Fuel distributor
In order to monitor fuels in free tax circulation, as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity was introduced, namely the fuel distributor.
A person who intends to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in free tax circulation in the tax territory as part of his business activity is obliged to apply to the customs office for a distribution permit before the start of distribution and submit a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with a suitable verified measuring device. equipment, as well as a list of suppliers and customers.
In addition to other legal obligations, the fuel distributor is obliged to keep separate records for each establishment of purchased petrol and diesel, diesel or LPG for a calendar month.
The fuel distributor is obliged by law to purchase or otherwise take fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
A fuel distributor may only sell in the tax territory to a fuel distributor, a registered person or a fuel consumer.
However, when delivering fuels via a tank truck, the distributor prints to the fuel retailer, resp. consumers of fuels, the so-called bottling from a measuring device built into a tank truck.
That document shall contain, in addition to information on quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
To prove the method of acquiring fuels, for example, an invoice is sufficient, which also contains the number of the distributor of fuels, resp. registered persons assigned by the tax administrator.
Fuel consumer
The fuel consumer has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG for his own consumption in the tax territory for free consumption and stores this mineral oil in a storage facility with a capacity of 15,000 liters or more must notify the customs office of this fact at the latest before the first placing in the storage area. device.
The customs office shall register fuel consumers.
In addition to the legal facts, he is obliged to state the address of the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
The storage facility must be verified and equipped with a measuring device enabling the amount of fuel (level indicator, measuring rod) to be measured during receipt and issue.
The tank must meet technical standards.
The fuel consumer must purchase fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for transport.
However, when delivering fuels via a tank truck, the distributor prints a so-called bottle from the measuring device built into the tank truck when refueling the consumer.
That document shall contain, in addition to information on quantities, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the traffic inspectorate.
To prove the method of acquiring fuel, for example, an invoice is sufficient, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the tax administrator.
The tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods during the tax supervision of mineral oils.
A small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer within the business and meets the legal conditions.
Provided that the conditions laid down by law are met, a small independent brewery can apply a reduced tax rate, ie € 2.652 per hl / percentage of the actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to 200,000 hl of beer.
As this is a beer production outside the conditional tax exemption regime, an accompanying document is not required for transport, as it is in free tax circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, these are small family businesses, which also run restaurants or pubs, in which they offer beer of their own production for sale.
Administrative tasks in the Slovak Republic
This subchapter describes the performance of tax supervision of excise tax administration for selected tax entities in the sense of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative operations (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, which was caused by the number of transport operations in the EMCS system.
On the other hand, the largest year-on-year decline was recorded in 2014, by as much as 4.3%, which was due to a smaller number of completed tax audits and a smaller number of filed tax returns.
This decrease concerned legislative changes.
Tax inspections
By performing a tax audit, the CA ascertains or verifies the facts decisive for the correct determination of the tax.
When performing tax audits, CA employees prove themselves by an authorization to perform tax audits, which contains, among other things, the purpose and subject of the audit and the scope of audited tax periods.
In practice, this means that the controlled tax period can be one month, but also more tax periods.
The scope of audited tax periods is determined by the CA.
The tax audit begins with the writing of a record of the commencement of the tax audit.
The CA will confirm the receipt of the documents.
The CA is obliged to return the borrowed documents within 30 days of the end of the tax audit.
The CA employee prepares a report from the tax audit.
If the tax audit finds a difference in the sum that the audited tax entity was to pay, report or for which it claimed a tax refund, the CA shall send the audited tax entity, together with the report, also an invitation to comment on the findings stated in the protocol.
The tax audit is completed on the day of delivery of the protocol.
The deadline for carrying out a tax audit is a maximum of one year from the date of its commencement.
Tax control of registered persons and selected registered persons will be performed as required, but at least once until the date of termination of the right to determine the tax, which is 5 years.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic issued an internal governing act, which adjusted the above-mentioned deadlines due to the uniform procedure of the tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
The local investigation
A local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator, in the framework of which it searches for evidence, examines and ascertains facts that are necessary for the purposes of tax administration.
The CA employee writes a record of the local investigation and submits a copy to the tax subject.
When carrying out a local investigation, a CA employee has the right to unrestricted access to land, operating buildings, rooms and places, including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The settlement of the quantity of alcohol produced is ascertained in the form of a local survey.
The ascertained facts are the basis for the performance of tax control.
Also during the local investigation, the CA is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the case.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic issued an internal governing act, which regulated the performance of tax supervision and local investigation for individual items of excise duties due to the unification of the tax administrator's procedures.
Permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1 May 2004, there was also a change in the area of ​​excise tax administration.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in the administration of excise duty on alcohol, improvement of the business environment in the area and the introduction of legislative instruments for more effective suppression of the gray economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in connection with excise tax administration.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the tax administrator in the area of ​​excise tax administration from tax offices to customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administrator to be present in the tax warehouse for alcohol.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation exhaustively defines that it is only possible to receive, dispense, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse in the presence of a CA employee.
This does not apply to a tax warehouse that receives, stores or sends alcohol only in consumer packaging of alcohol.
At the same time, the CA arises the obligation to secure employees in the tax warehouse so that the receipt, issue, production or processing of alcohol is not restricted.
The tax warehouse operator is obliged to ensure the working environment for CA employees.
Based on the contract concluded with the FR of the Slovak Republic for the provided premises, the CA pays the rental costs to the operator of the tax warehouse on a monthly basis.
In a tax warehouse during the production, processing or storage of alcohol, the alcohol storage plant must be adapted in such a way that the quantities of alcohol produced, processed alcohol, stored alcohol, including stocks of alcohol and alcohol contained therein, can be determined at any time.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
If the alcohol is not received, issued, produced or processed in the tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of an employee of the customs office, while it is obliged to secure this space with the closure of the customs office.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often, as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators use the legal option within the meaning of Act No. 467/2002 Coll., On the production and marketing of alcohol, and use production facilities for the production of alcohol in a distillery for growing distillery and also for the purposes of a distillery, which must be a tax warehouse.
The performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol is ensured by approximately 250 customs officers.
Issuing vouchers for the collection of control stamps for alcohol
The basic act for the collection of control stamps is to send a request to the customs office for the assignment of a registration collection number and to issue a voucher for the collection of control stamps for alcohol.
Alcoholic beverages, which are alcohol, means goods of the combined nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength of more than 1.2% volume.
The control mark is intended for marking consumer packaging of alcohol.
Consumer packaging of alcohol is considered to be a closed consumer package filled with alcohol intended for direct human consumption.
Consumer packaging of Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be put into free tax circulation in the tax territory only if it is marked with a control mark.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorized consignee and the importer of the consumer packaging, who will put it into free tax circulation, may mark the consumer packaging with alcohol with a control mark.
The control mark contains, among other things, an identification number, which consists of a 14-digit numerical character. The identification number contains the registration number (1st-6th place of the numerical sign), the volume of alcohol (7th-11th place of the numerical sign) and the volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer package (12th-14th place of the numerical sign).
Original model of the alcohol control mark:
The registration number is assigned by the CA to each customer separately.
Only a control mark whose identification number corresponds to the volume of the consumer package, the volume concentration of the alcohol in the consumer package and the customer's control mark may be used to mark the consumer packaging of alcohol.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced the introduction of a new information system for control marks.
The aim of the new information system of control marks was to simplify and computerize the system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control marks intended for labeling consumer packaging of alcohol.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorized consignee, the importer of the consumer packaging and the consignee (customer) of the alcohol may mark the consumer packaging with alcohol as a control mark.
A buyer of control marks who wishes to obtain control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of control stamps is obliged to request their issuance, report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and keep records of control stamps.
The number of ordered pieces of control stamps may not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
The tax administrator also communicates with the buyers of control marks through the electronic system of control marks, especially when announcing the number of control marks that the customer of control stamps can take, resp. when determining the date of receipt of the control stamps by the customer of the control stamps in the printer.
Prior to taking over the control stamps, the customer of the control stamps is obliged to deposit funds on the account of the tax administrator corresponding to the price of the control marks which he may collect and the amount of which shall be notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the control stamp takes into account the amount of compensation to the printer. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice is authorized to print inspection marks.
FŘ SR performs tax supervision over the handling of control marks and their liquidation in the printer.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing house when handling control marks.
FŘ SR ensures the sale of control stamps to customers of control stamps in the printer.
It is only possible to remove control marks in the printer from an employee of the Finance Directorate.
Issuing vouchers for the collection of control marks for tobacco products
The buyer of the control stamp must ask the CA to assign a registration collection number and issue a voucher for the collection of the control stamp.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes may be put into free tax circulation only if it is marked with a control mark.
It is only possible to mark consumer packaging of cigarettes with a control mark in the company that produces cigarettes.
Only the operator of a tax warehouse, an authorized recipient or importer of tobacco products who wishes to release tobacco products for free circulation in the tax territory may be a customer of control marks.
Only a control mark, the details of which correspond to the relevant price of the cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the pack, the length of the cigarettes, the indication of the validity of the tax rate and the registration number, may be used to indicate the consumer pack.
Consumer packs of cigarettes may be sold for final consumption only at the price indicated on the control mark.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced the introduction of a new information system for control marks.
The aim of the new control mark information system was to simplify and computerize the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for marking consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A buyer of control marks who wishes to obtain control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of control stamps is obliged to request their issuance, report data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and keep records of control stamps.
The state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice is authorized to print inspection marks.
FŘ SR performs tax supervision over the handling of control marks and their liquidation in the printer.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing house when handling control marks.
FŘ SR ensures the sale of control stamps to customers of control stamps in the printer.
It is only possible to remove control marks in the printer from an employee of the Finance Directorate.
The operator of the tax warehouse or the importer of tobacco products may mark the consumer packaging of tobacco with a control mark.
The operator of the tax warehouse, the importer of tobacco products or the authorized consignee may mark the consumer packaging of cigars or cigarillos with a control mark.
Only the control mark, the details of which correspond to the symbol for the validity of the rate of excise duty, shall be used to indicate the consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos.
It is only possible to mark consumer packaging of cigarettes with a control mark in the company that manufactured them.
The number of ordered pieces of control stamps may not be less than 500 pieces or a multiple thereof.
The CA shall electronically notify the customer of control stamps no later than three working days of the number of control stamps that it may collect, the price of control stamps and the account number of the FR SR.
The CA may reduce the number of ordered control marks if circumstances have arisen on the basis of which it can be reasonably assumed that tax regulations may be violated.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic will determine the date of acceptance of control marks by the customer of control marks, but no later than within 10 days.
The FR SR will announce the date of acceptance of control stamps to the customer of control stamps via the electronic system of control stamps.
Control stamps are issued by the Financial Directorate exclusively in the printing house, but only after the receipt of funds corresponding to their price to the relevant account specified in the electronic notification of the customs office.
The customer of control stamps is obliged to keep records of control stamps separately in the electronic system of control stamps, broken down into cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Pursuant to Council Regulation (EU) No. 389/2012, the ELO and SPD Systems Department of the Excise Tax Department of the FR SR is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information on the basis of a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and relevant financial administrations.
These are, in particular, requests for verification of excise administration bodies, requests for information on excise administration and also requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications takes place in electronic form within the EMCS system.
The following actions are included in administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on the administration of excise duties, request for confirmation of registration in SEED); response to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Authorization and registration
In the Slovak Republic, permanent tax supervision is applied to alcohol warehouses, in the Czech Republic this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administrator through a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are a tax warehouse, in the Slovak Republic they are only registered by the tax administrator.
The institute of a registered consignor has been introduced in the Slovak Republic, which is included in tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In the Slovak Republic, it is possible to burn 43 l with a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in the case of growing burning.
In contrast, in the Czech Republic, the reduced rate of tax on alcohol can be applied only for 30 l and.
The growing distillery in the Slovak Republic must have a permit not only from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also from the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, growing distilleries are only permitted by the Ministry of Agriculture.
In the Slovak Republic, in addition to the operator of a tax warehouse, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol is also carried out by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The importer's authorization is conditional on the applicant's registration with the excise duty administrator.
In the Czech Republic, no special permission of the tax administrator is required to import consumer packaging of alcohol.
In the Slovak Republic, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is conditioned by the issuance of a tax administrator's permit for the seller.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep records of, among other things, the purchase and sale.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for final sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of alcohol by the Trade Licensing Office; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In the Slovak Republic, the seller of fuels must have a permit from the tax administrator to sell them.
National legislation in the Slovak Republic does not regulate filling stations by any special regulation; all activities related to filling stations are regulated only in the Act on Excise Duty on Mineral Oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by a special law on fuels, but the tax administrator does not issue any permits for the sale of fuels.
Gas stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In the Slovak Republic, it is not technically possible to obtain a list of filling stations from the financial management system.
In the Slovak Republic, there has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits in 2013 decreased significantly due to the introduction of a deposit for fuel distributors.
Administrative tasks
In the Slovak Republic, substantive legal regulations stipulate the obligation to perform tax audits of selected tax entities.
This issue is specified in more detail by an internal governing act issued by the Ministry of Justice of the Slovak Republic due to the application of a uniform procedure of tax administrators in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, substantive legal regulations do not regulate the obligation to perform tax audits; procedural law regulations only stipulate the possibility of carrying out audits by the deadline for tax assessment at the latest.
The reason for large differences in the number of performed tax inspections and local investigations in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is the fact that the internal governing act of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Slovak Republic stipulates in which cases and within which deadlines or its return verified in particular by a local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative acts in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 due to an increase in the number of transports in the EMCS system and at the same time due to an increase in the number of filed tax returns.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of administrative operations between 2012 and 2015 had a slightly increasing tendency, which was influenced by the increasing number of transports in the EMCS system and at the same time by the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the number of comparable permits and the registration of tax subjects were affected by different legislation.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period.
In the Slovak Republic, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds compared to the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for approximately the same number of administrative acts.
From the above, it can be stated that the Slovak Republic is more focused on the performance of administrative tasks by the tax administrator, such as the performance of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, more emphasis is placed on remote monitoring, such as monitoring devices, direct data transmission via a web interface and risk analysis.
Electronic administrative tasks
Electronic administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
The tax return can be filed via the data box.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced so-called interactive forms of tax returns, which, however, can no longer be processed automatically.
The data must be further transferred to the personal tax account of the tax subject.
The benefit is the reduction of the error rate of filed tax returns (DAP), which saves the actions of the tax administrator related to the procedure for corrections of incorrectly filed DAP.
The GDC is working on a new application for electronic DAP processing.
Through smart forms, it is also possible to: file tax applications or registrations and notify changes of data, claim a refund, comply with notification obligations for the handling of special mineral oils, the handling of raw tobacco and the fulfillment of biofuel obligations.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax subjects in the ORO WebKlient information system, which is available for registered subjects for registration of data specified by the tax administrator.
The transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the conditional tax exemption regime must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
The transport of selected products in free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be carried out with a document proving their taxation, proof of exemption from excise duty, customs decision to release selected products into customs, simplified accompanying document or other decision on excise duty.
The required content of the data is determined by legal regulations.
To facilitate the fulfillment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (§ 5 and § 6 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.).
It allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to a data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique twelve-digit identification code (JIK).
The JIK serves the purpose of control by the customs authorities on the road and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
At the largest operator of a fuel tax warehouse in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of fuel into free tax circulation, CS ČR has online access to an electronic registration system in which the entity automatically stores issued tax documents.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, ie an electronic system for recording and monitoring the transport of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70% of the existing EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be a user-friendly environment for declarants and customs officers.
It will also be connected to the system of global guarantees, to the register of tax subjects or to the system of risk analysis.
The system should provide an overview of free circulation traffic between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of written documents without registration and sharing of reference numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure of registration of transports of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen primarily in the misuse of the simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronization of administrative tasks in the Slovak Republic
When administering excise duties, the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic uses electronic communication when monitoring the movement of goods in the EMCS system in the regime of conditional tax exemption, control stamps, filing tax returns and also when registering and registering tax subjects.
In 2014, one-way electronic communication between tax entities and the tax administrator was also introduced, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
As part of electronic communication, after entering access data, the tax subject has access to a personal internet zone, the so-called electronic personal mailbox, which is intended for communication with the financial administration.
Within this zone, the taxable person has access to an electronic filing system, through which he submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents related to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication via the personal internet zone does not apply to all tax entities.
National legislation defines tax entities that are required to communicate with the tax administrator electronically.
These are mainly payers of value added tax, tax advisors representing the tax entity and lawyers representing the tax entity.
During the audit, the SAO SR also dealt with the issue of the extent of the electronic administration of excise duties.
These were only fully electronic transactions, namely tax returns and electronic communication within ELO.
Apart from the transport carried out in the EMCS system, there has been an increase in the computerization of selected comparable administrative tasks, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In the Slovak Republic, fully electronic processing of the tax return has already been introduced, from its submission to the registration of the tax liability.
In the Czech Republic, electronic processing of tax returns is not set.
In the Czech Republic, it is possible for tax subjects to insert mandatory documents for individual transports in free tax circulation on the website.
In the future, the reporting of transport in free tax circulation in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system is being prepared.
Evaluation
The system of reporting transports in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of legislation.
This can be recommended as a good practice.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
Due to good practice in the Slovak Republic in the field of electronic tax returns, the SAO SR and the SAO CR recommend to complete the electronic processing of tax returns in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organizational structure and personnel in the field of excise duties
The organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has undergone fundamental changes.
Organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
Since 1 January 2013, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic consists of the General Directorate of Customs and customs offices, which are administrative offices and organizational units of the state.
The GDC is the accounting unit for the whole customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been performing the comprehensive administration of excise duties since 2004 as one of the many competencies it provides.
CS CR also performs:
(a) control:
ശശ in the field of road transport (weighing of lorries, payment of tolls for the use of roads, fulfillment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and in matters of international passenger transport),
ശശ waste and packaging material management,
ശശ safety of imported food,
ശശ in the field of consumer protection and protection of intellectual property rights,
ശശ employment of foreigners,
b) customs administration - this is a comprehensive application of customs regulations, trade policy measures and formalities in the import and export of goods,
c) collection and enforcement of pecuniary benefits imposed by other public administration bodies within the framework of divided administration,
d) activities of a police authority (authorized customs authorities) in proceedings on criminal offenses committed in violation of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is a tax administrator.
The scope of competencies (concurrence of control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, but there are economies of scale, as the public administration does not have to spend on the position of the control group for each subject of control separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden on inspected persons is reduced by repeated inspections.
10 From 1 December 2016, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic also performs the competence to verify the fulfillment of obligations in the registration of sales (§ 2 para. 2 of Act No. 112/2016 Coll., On the registration of sales) and from 1 January 2017 the supervision of compliance with the Act. and the conditions for the operation of gambling, including the imposition of sanctions (Section 116 of Act No. 186/2016 Coll., on gambling).
As part of the Modernization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic project, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-tier structure to a two-tier structure with effect from 1 January 2013, while the middle article of the procedure (customs directorates) was abolished.
The GDC spent approximately CZK 51 million (ie approximately € 2,031,000) on the project.
Since 1 January 2013, the CS CR consists of the GDC and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organizational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competencies are stipulated by law, excise taxes are administered by all customs offices through departments and territorial offices.
Territorial workplaces are internal organizational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is authorized to establish and abolish territorial workplaces and determine their material scope by a decree.
Legal regulations do not stipulate any competences for territorial workplaces; territorial workplaces perform the competencies of the customs office on its behalf.
Organizational structure until 31 December 2012
Organizational structure since 1 January 2013
Until 31 December 2012, the administration of excise duties was performed by the GDC, eight CAs and 58 CA departments (including branches), ie a total of 67 departments and divisions.
As of 1 January 2016, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the GDC and 51 departments at the CA and their territorial workplaces, as well as eight workplaces of the GDC legal department and CA departments providing mobile supervision, ie approximately 60 positions.
The costs of the CS CR most significantly affect wage expenditures.
As a result of the reorganization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there were no savings in human resources.
The performance of the main processes is ensured by customs officers in an employment relationship in accordance with the Act on the Employment of Members of the Security Forces.
The possibility to reduce the numbers of these members in the Czech Republic is very limited, because according to the provisions of § 42 paragraph 1 of Act No. 361/2003 Coll., On the employment of members of the security forces, they can be dismissed from employment only in exhaustively defined cases.
Reduction of posts due to organizational changes in the security corps is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to provide members with appropriate posts within the corps, or to secure posts with another security corps (eg Police, Prison Services), otherwise reassign them to the advance for the temporarily unclassified, in which members of the security forces are entitled to 80% of the average service income according to the law.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
Organizational structure of the excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic
As part of the program statement for 2012 to 2016, the Government of the Slovak Republic has set as one of its priorities the completion of tax administration reform through the UNITAS program, which will provide additional budgetary resources by unifying the collection of taxes, duties and levies and suppressing tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic into the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the creation of a financial administration.
The Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic was established on 1 January 2012 by Act No. 333/2011 Coll., On state administration bodies in the field of taxes, fees and customs, as amended, as a budgetary organization based in Banská Bystrica and connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The FR SR, the CA and the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration in the sense of Act No. 199/2004 Coll., The Customs Act and on Amendments to Certain Acts, as amended, are customs authorities if they perform tasks pursuant to customs regulations.
Pursuant to Act No. 333/2011 Coll., On state administration bodies in the area of ​​taxes, fees and customs, as amended, together with the tax authorities they form the financial administration.
The new organizational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competence Center for Financial Operations, tax offices, the Tax Office for selected tax entities, branches of tax offices, contact points of tax offices, customs offices, branches of customs offices (tax office, tax office, combined office, customs office) and customs station.
The main mission of the FR SR is to efficiently collect and administer taxes and duties, ie also excise taxes, to fulfill the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the FR SR is the President of the Financial Administration, who is appointed and removed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The President of the Financial Administration is responsible for the activities of the entire financial administration, and thus also for the activities of the FR SR, which he manages and represents in full.
Organizational structure of the FR SR from 1 January 2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in the territory of the Slovak Republic, activities and processes in the area of ​​excise tax administration are provided not only by customs offices (38 branches) and customs offices (18 stations) but also by excise departments (9 departments) and legal departments (9 departments).

Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Within the organizational structure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic, in 2015, in addition to the FR SR, the administration of excise duties was dealt with by 74 organizational units with a total number of 1,300 employees; these departments are managed by almost 48,000 tax entities.
Within the organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, in 2015 the administration of excise duties was dealt with by approximately 60 organizational units with a total number of 1,011 employees, which are managed by approximately 114,000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual activities of the excise tax administration is divided between several personnel-independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is handled through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax control) in the area of ​​excise tax administration is divided between the excise tax department and the customs office branch, within which the same employees of the tax administrator often deal with this agenda.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, approximately one third of the number of tax subjects per total number of employees in the area of ​​excise tax administration is compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the impact of a larger number of employees on the efficiency of excise administration is not clear.
EMCS system
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 establishing an electronic system for the movement and tracking of excisable products, the aim of introducing an electronic tracking system for selected products was to to carry out the prescribed controls, to facilitate the intra-Community movement of goods under suspension of excise duty.
When introducing the system, Member States should allow economic operators, in particular small and medium-sized enterprises active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of that EP and Council Decision allows for the inclusion in the EMCS of national specifications, national databases forming part of the system and such hardware or software as the Member State considers necessary to ensure full use of the system in its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionality of the EMCS system
In the Czech Republic, the EMCS system was preceded by the Selected Product Registration (EVV) system, which was operated from May 2004 until the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented with European and national functionalities (see Annex No. 5).
The so-called customs module and declarant module were introduced in the Czech Republic.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
In addition to the Community system, in the Czech Republic, the EMCS system monitors shipments in the regime of conditional tax exemption initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
After approval of the notification of receipt of a consignment intended for a single consignee for a single receipt, the system ensures the automatic sending of information to the register of tax subjects with the subsequent revocation of the permit.
The system fully ensures the administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including the sending of responses with an attachment in any format and the provision of translations.
It is also possible to receive a message on the manual termination of the export in ECS (in the EU, only the forwarding of the automatically generated message is implemented).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS will not allow the approval of an e-AD or notification of acceptance without a response from the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available free of charge for tax subjects, it takes the form of a web application in which the user logs in with the username and password (coordinates) that are assigned to him after registration with the CS CR.
Each action against the EMCS customs module must be provided with a valid electronic signature in the declaring EMCS module.
The declarant module allows tax subjects to directly record data on started and completed transports in the conditional tax exemption regime, and thus tax subjects do not have to spend funds to acquire the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module enable reading and storing data off-line (saves time for frequently used data), filling in recipient data based on SEED ID control and requiring mandatory filling in of data that is optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also makes it possible to block the provision of excise duty in the corresponding amount of taxable performance for each consignment sent from the Czech Republic in real time until the end of the transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS system.
Without a sufficient amount of security, it is not possible to send the e-AD proposal from the EMCS declarant module for approval to the office of departure.
Each warranty has a unique number and includes the ARC of the shipment (including the amount of the blocked security) for which it was used.
The taxable person can manage his guarantees directly in the declarant module EMCS, where he sees the current amount of blocked and unblocked excise tax guarantees.
Expenditure on setting up and using the EMCS
The development of the EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight performance contracts from 2006 to 2017 in the total amount of CZK 46,791,924.60 (ie € 1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices from 2006 to the end of 2015 for the total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (ie € 1,640,401.10) excluding VAT.
In the audited period, expenses in the amount of CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (ie € 547,438.99) were incurred to upgrade the EMCS system.
The amount spent on the EMCS upgrade in the audited period and converted to one transport inserted into the EMCS is on average CZK 16.49 (ie € 0.62), excluding national transport, these expenditures are calculated per transport between the Czech Republic and EU Member States 24 .40 CZK (ie 0.92 €).
EMCS technical support was provided on the basis of four performance contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support in the amount of CZK 7,499,675 (ie € 281,389.77), including value added tax, was invoiced.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on one transport submitted to the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (ie € 0.23).
The invoices for development and technical support related to the national solution and they were used to develop the EVV application, which was already operated by the GDC before the EMCS system itself.
Invoices were paid as part of program funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services and for other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under a duty suspension arrangement.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document - SAD, which was used before the effectiveness of this system, thus ensuring better control and management of traffic.
It has been introduced in the Slovak Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented with requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, so-called
ARC code, under which the traffic can be monitored online, ie in real time.
Development and functionality of the EMCS system
The EMCS system ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by those taxable persons who are authorized to use the EMCS system, which greatly reduces the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest development of functionalities occurred in 2011, when the EMCS system was fully put into operation (see Annex No. 6).
Expenditure on setting up and using the EMCS
The introduction of the EMCS system was implemented as another module of the SysNeD application equipment, and therefore it is not possible to determine exactly the amount of costs for its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of the EMCS was to replace a system based on paper administration.
The benefit of the EMCS system is a comprehensive overview of transport between individual Member States within the EU from the announcement of the start of transport to its end - a significant reduction in administrative costs for tax administrations and tax entities for processing, transmitting and archiving documents.
In the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic, a national functionality was introduced into the EMCS system enabling the monitoring of traffic in a conditional system between two places in the Czech Republic, resp. in SR.
In addition, automatic monitoring and excise guarantee functionality is applied in the Czech Republic.
A national functionality is also introduced, which monitors the riskiness of the tax subject, resp. transport, followed by a mandatory response from the tax administrator.
The Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic register a comparable number of transports within the EU in the EMCS system.
However, expenditures in the Slovak Republic on the upgrade of this system in the years 2012 to 2015 were € 744,310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic.
The SAO SR obtained data from the FR SR of the upgrade of the EMCS system only for the period from 2011, although this system was introduced and operated earlier.
Nevertheless, the expenses incurred for the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic were by € 188,134.44 higher than the expenses for the introduction and upgrade of the EMCS system for about ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
During the audited period, the volume of expenditures related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic in terms of one shipment 2.3 times exceeds the expenditures of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation between the SAO CR and the SAO SR met the objectives.
Both control institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the system of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
It was found that despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in both tax systems that affect the efficiency of excise administration.
During parallel audits, examples of good practice were identified that could help reduce tax fraud, and their importance will increase with increasing tax rates.
Procedures have also been identified to reduce the costs of excise administration.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons, unless mutually coordinated in-depth inspections are carried out at the tax administrator.
The role of supreme audit institutions in this is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of the value added tax administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Foreword
The 1977 Lima Declaration emphasizes that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial transactions.
The declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled as much as possible.
The European Organization of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers the tax to be one of the most important components of public revenue.
VI. The EUROSAI Congress, held in Bonn in 2005, dealt with the audit of public revenues carried out by the SAI.
An important step on the way to optimizing the SAI's control activities is the development of a specific strategy for the audit of public revenues.
This concerns in particular taxes as the largest source of public revenue, which is most prone to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of another state's SAIs.
An example is the audit of internationally organized fraud, which causes significant revenue losses in many countries.
In order to combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs that carry out inspections in this area must be willing to work more closely together.
Right on VI. The EUROSAI Congress in Bonn gave rise to the idea of ​​carrying out an audit of the value added tax ('VAT') administration and the VIES system in cooperation with the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
Careful preparation followed, when both parties first had to get acquainted with the legal environment and procedures for VAT administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was made, which were included in the control program.
Achieving efficient and effective VAT administration is a long-term challenge and individual states (especially the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We are convinced that the results of our audit can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrations, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international information exchange.
Report on the results of parallel inspections of the value added tax administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 - 2005 - 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Administration of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic to the European Union
(D) Verification of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the audit in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of financial authorities in the administration of value added tax after the Czech Republic's integration into the single internal market of the European Union ("EU") associated with the free movement of goods and services and to verify the use of VIES, in particular when monitoring the exercise of the right to exemption from value added tax in intra-Community supplies.
(D) The purpose of the audit was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax with a special focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the above-mentioned regulations.
The result should be a report on the weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
Value Added Information Exchange System The inspections were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter "SAO") and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter "BRH") in mutual cooperation on the basis of an agreement concluded between the two auditing institutions on 8 June 2006. .
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected business transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter "CR") and the Federal Republic of Germany ("Germany"), the use of information obtained through international cooperation between tax administrations and comparison of VAT administration systems of both countries. .
The joint final report on the results of audits was prepared in accordance with European Directive No. 31 for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards.
The audited period was the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The parallel control in the area of ​​VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was performed on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
In addition to the main point - the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 - the audit covered other topics, such as taxpayer registration, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely connected with the main point.
In addition, the audit included the legal situation in the field of international bus and coach transport and the comparison of some statistics.
A comparison of the VAT administration systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, taxpayers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for business transactions in Germany.
If a German taxpayer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different ways of registration cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International bus passenger transport.
In the Czech Republic, international bus transport of passengers is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, part of the transport that takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonize the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2).
3) Tax returns for VAT.
While in the Czech Republic taxpayers file VAT returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany taxpayers are obliged to file so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they must file an annual VAT return. .
Unlike in the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are obliged to file preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to file VAT returns in the Czech Republic electronically would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic the payers submit summary reports to the tax authorities, in Germany the payers submit summary reports to the CLO.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have the data from the summary reports available immediately after their submission.
The German tax authorities only have the information from the recapitulative statements available after they have been processed at the CLO.
The fight against VAT fraud requires that up-to-date information on intra-Community transactions be made available as soon as possible.
Monthly submission of recapitulative statements would shorten the time lag between the date of the transaction and the update of the data in VIES.
This would then allow for a timely verification of taxation in the Member State of origin (see 4.4).
This would, however, require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for the recapitulative statement.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for received requests for information.
The German CLO does not follow the elapsed time.
As a result, the German tax administration processed a significantly lower percentage of applications received within the deadline.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent alert (see 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (RMS), which has its strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, both SAIs examined selected cases of intra-Community transactions carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together with the use of the legislation for the CLO, thirty-one cases of business transactions were examined, in which there were doubts about their execution or suspicion of VAT evasion.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained through international cooperation and assessed the VAT liability of taxpayers.
In these cases, the payers either unjustifiably claimed the right to exemption of the supply from VAT, or did not admit the acquisition of goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used due to different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases were found where payers incorrectly reported business transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the data in VIES were incorrect and the tax administrations had to examine these cases (see 6.).
The course of the control action
The course of control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out in the period from June 2006 to March 2007 by Department II - Department of State Budget Revenues and Territorial Departments of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The audited entities were: the Ministry of Finance (hereinafter "MoF") and 10 tax offices - the Tax Office in Humpolec, the Tax Office in Jihlava, the Tax Office in Kadan, the Tax Office in Liberec, the Tax Office in Nymburk, the Tax Office in Otrokovice, the Tax Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 4, the Financial Office in Sokolov and the Financial Office in Třinec.
The audit conclusion from this audit was approved by the SAO Board on 23 April 2007.
The course of the control action in Germany
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and February 2007 by the Indirect Taxation Audit Group and the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
The inspection was part of the inspection plan for 2006 and was therefore notified to the Federal Ministry of Finance in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases of selected BRHs and later elected SAOs, BRH had to notify a number of federal states of inspections.
In addition to interviews with the Federal Ministry of Finance and the CLO, inspections were carried out in the following Länder:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine-Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich - FI for corporations / legal entities (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich V, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg-center (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-north (Hamburg-Nord) and Hamburg for large companies (Hamburg für Großunternehmen), Hannover-Nord (Hannover-north), Winsen-Luhe, Bonn center (Bonn- Innenstadt), Cologne (Köln-Mitte), Cologne-Porz (Köln-Porz), Cologne South (Köln-Süd), Sankt Augustin, Pirmasens, Bautzen (Bautzen), Chemnitz South (Chemnitz-Süd), Dresden II (Dresden II), Freiberg, Leipzig I and Zschopau.
In addition, negotiations took place with the Augsburg-Stadt tax office, Aurich, Düsseldorf-Altstadt, Eisleben, Kelheim and Verden.
The report on control findings was submitted to the Ministry of Finance in May 2007.
Cooperation of both control institutions
As part of the preparation of parallel inspections, several meetings of representatives of both inspection institutions took place in the period before their commencement.
The participants of these meetings got acquainted with the organization of tax administrations, with the legislative regulation of VAT issues and with the system of VAT administration in both countries.
At the meeting held in May 2006, the topics of the testing phase were agreed.
The results of the test phase were evaluated at another joint meeting in August 2006.
During this meeting, a schedule for further work was agreed and the following topics for parallel inspections were identified:
1. Registration of VAT payers.
2.
International bus passenger transport - legislation in the Czech Republic and Germany.
3. International exchange of information, especially the procedure of tax administrators in processing requests for information and examination of selected problematic cases listed in requests for information and spontaneous information transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany.
4. Tax returns for VAT.
5.
Summary reports.
6.
Statistical data on delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
7. Risk management in the field of VAT.
At the joint audit day of the SAO and the BRH, which took place in December 2006, both parties became acquainted with the course of the audit in the Czech Republic and Germany and discussed the results of parallel audits to date.
A report on the results of parallel inspections of the VAT administration between the Czech Republic and Germany was prepared at a working meeting in July 2007.
4. Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., On the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 337/1992 Coll.”), A tax subject means a taxpayer, a taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person who is a tax entity defined by law.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421,865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
As of 1 December 2005, the number of tax entities registered for VAT increased to 457,590.
A taxable person who has his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) in the next 12 consecutive calendar months, becomes a payer from the 1st day of the third month following month in which it exceeded the registration limit (Section 94, Paragraph 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 235/2004 Coll.”).
This person is obliged to submit the application for registration within 15 days after the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow the registration of a taxable person so-called retroactively in cases where the reason for registration is exceeding the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with the right to deduct may become a taxpayer, even if he does not exceed CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if he fulfills any of the other conditions specified in Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not meet any of the conditions stipulated by law may apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
By delivering the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator, the registration procedure is initiated pursuant to Act No. 337/1992 Coll.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also state on the VAT registration application the date on which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator will check the data communicated by the tax subject, ie the completed application for registration with all attachments.
If he has doubts about the data, he shall invite the taxable person to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After verifying that the tax entity meets the conditions for registration, the tax administrator will issue a decision in the form of a certificate stating that the tax entity is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter "VAT number").
The tax administrator shall state on the certificate the effective date of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT tax period.
The tax period is a calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period is a calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and will notify the tax administrator of this change.
THIS segment IS intentionally LEFT blank
The assignment of a VAT number in a registration certificate is always of a constitutive nature and the tax subject is obliged to state it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (eg Act No. 235/2004 Coll. issuance of tax documents).
The VAT number contains the code "CZ" and the main part, which consists of a general identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number, or another general identifier, if so provided by a special law, and in the case of a legal entity, an identification number (provisions of Section 33, Paragraph 12 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation even at the request of the tax administrator, the locally competent tax administrator shall register it ex officio without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issuance of a Certificate of Registration ex officio, which is delivered to the tax subject.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has obtained a business license is assigned a VAT number at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The tax entity uses the same VAT number even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
Pursuant to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., Which is effective from 1 January 2005, the tax administrator may, in the event of non-compliance with the VAT registration obligation, impose on the taxable person compensation up to 10% of total income or income for taxable transactions. , which this person carried out unjustifiably without tax, for the period from the date on which he was supposed to be a registered payer by law to the date on which he became a registered payer based on the decision of the tax administrator (provisions of § 98 par. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Sb.).
Payment of the amount thus determined is considered a tax payment (Section 98, Paragraph 3 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), Ie it is not a sanction.
Cancellation of the VAT payer's registration if the conditions stipulated by law are met is possible for two reasons:
1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover that does not reach the registration limit (§ 106 paragraph 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to apply for cancellation of the registration at the earliest after 1 year from the effective date stated on the registration certificate.
2) Cancellation of registration “ex officio” (Section 106, Paragraph 7 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), If: a) the taxpayer has not performed without notification of a reason to the tax administrator for a period of 12 consecutive months of performance, b) the payer fails to fulfill his obligations arising from Act No. 235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic or a foreign taxable person who carries out transactions with the place of supply in the country and is a person obliged to declare and pay tax on this performance pursuant to Section 108 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. (so-called “non-established payer”), becomes the payer on the day of this performance.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the Tax Office for Prague 1 no later than the date of the performance.
In the application for registration, she is obliged to state all VAT numbers that have been assigned to her in other Member States or in a third country.
If a "non-established" payer submits an application for registration later than on the date of the first taxable supply in the Czech Republic, the Tax Office for Prague 1 will register it retroactively, because according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax entity became a VAT payer on the day of the first taxable supply in the Czech Republic.
During retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires from tax subjects proof that the performance has been performed (invoices or explanatory letters).
If a “non-established” tax entity applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable supply takes place, then the Tax Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the supply will take place.
