As at 31 December 2004, 473 “non-established” payers were registered at the Tax Office for Prague 1, of which 124 were payers from Germany, and as at 31 December 2005, 951 “non-established” payers were registered, of which 233 were from Germany.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 106, Paragraph 9 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a “non-established” taxpayer as of 31 January of the following calendar year, if this taxpayer did not incur any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The SAO's inspection revealed that if a “non-established” taxpayer files a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, ie in accordance with the legal regulation within the deadline for filing a tax return, the tax office often does not have it available on 31 January.
In cases where the facts decisive for the possibility of canceling the registration with the tax office are known later than 31 January, it is no longer possible in the Czech Republic to cancel the VAT registration in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§§ 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter "AO"), anyone who carries out business activities is obliged to inform the city / municipal authority or the relevant tax office.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after starting a business.
This information is processed by the city / municipal office for the tax office.
If the tax office finds a company that has started an activity but has not registered, the relevant tax office can register this payer ex officio - even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-tax residents are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in § 2 of the German VAT Act ("UStG").
This obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover they generate.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax offices for entrepreneurs living abroad.
For example, for those based in the Czech Republic, the relevant Tax Office is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of April 30, 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; as of March 1, 2006, a total of 1,050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
The BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-independent freelancers based in the new eastern EU member states.
As work permits for employees from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these freelancers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
These companies do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs laid down in Paragraph 2 of the UStG, as they are usually dependent on a single employer who determines their working hours and the way in which they carry out their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must fill in a questionnaire of the relevant tax office, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities he performs.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding for all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of tax authorities or by departments with a general focus, which are responsible for assessing taxpayers.
This form is used to assess the risk of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information on the relevant tax office, the next three (or four) provide information on the relevant department at the tax office, the other five (or four) are to distinguish payers, the last being always the check digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to engage in intra-Community trade, he needs a VAT ID in order to receive a tax-exempt intra-Community supply.
The CLO assigns a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and if he has a tax number for VAT purposes.
The CLO automatically assigns VAT IDs to businesses when taxpayers indicate an intra-Community supply in their VAT return.
The VAT ID structure is a country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
The registration of an entrepreneur may be canceled: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activity), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all financial years) and 2. if the tax administration realizes that he is no longer in business .
The validity of a VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of a VAT number.
In these cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the CLO about the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the validity of the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT law (§ 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not required to pay VAT if 1. the turnover plus applicable VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. it is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000 in the following year .
So-called small entrepreneurs ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice VAT to other entrepreneurs and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small businesses must be registered with the tax office and must file an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that he will not apply the provisions of Paragraph 19 (1) of the UStG.
This declaration is binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For tax non-residents, it is possible to appoint tax representatives (§ 22a UStG).
It is a prerequisite that they carry out exclusively tax-exempt business transactions and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfill the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who does not have to register for VAT.
Invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If the tax subject in the Czech Republic does not exceed the set limit, it has the option to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration procedure is standardized in Germany, but as a result of different organizational models in the federal states, differences may occur.
In the Czech Republic, the taxpayer is assigned a VAT number at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same VAT number for intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, the taxpayer is assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for business transactions in Germany.
If a German taxpayer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and the BRH have found, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-Community transactions.
On the other hand, the two-tier system allows for retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax office about their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax period, in particular an accurate estimate of the VAT liability.
As different ways of registration cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU.
The German Parliament has recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (TIN).
The Federal Tax Office will assign a VAT number at the birth of a natural person.
This VAT number will be valid for the entire life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will ask for an economic VAT number, which will be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the assignment of the VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of an IT tool for VAT number management has not yet been completed.
International bus passenger transport
Legal regulation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. With effect from 1 May 2004, the transport of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax.
This transport is exempt from VAT, even if it is carried out by traders who are registered for tax purposes in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
Return transport is considered a separate transport.
If "non-established" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out any economic activity other than international bus transport of persons, they are not obliged to register in the Czech Republic as VAT payers.
International passenger transport was exempt from VAT in the Czech Republic on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V, chap. Article 5 (1) (a) (b) where it is stated:
"For the purposes of Article 28 (3) (a), (b) of Directive 77/388 / EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt from value added tax in respect of the international carriage of passengers pursuant to point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 28 (4) of the Directive is fulfilled or the exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier. "
Description of legislation in Germany
Pursuant to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in § 3b (1) of the German VAT Act, the place of supply of passenger transport (ie transport services) is the route (ie the place) where the transport takes place .
The German tax system therefore does not distinguish between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable supply of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If a tax non-resident transports passengers via Germany, then that part of the route which takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable supply of transport.
Before performing his services in Germany, a tax non-resident must notify his intention to provide passenger transport to the relevant tax office.
The tax office will register this tax non-resident for tax (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach listed in the taxpayer's notice.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable supplies of transport in the German VAT return.
As of March 1, 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers who were engaged in passenger transport.
If the transport of passengers is provided to a tax resident who is a person liable for VAT, the tax non-resident does not have to pay VAT to the tax office himself.
Instead, the entity liable to pay VAT to the tax office and the net amount invoiced to the non-resident taxpayer is the resident tax resident; this process is known as "reverse charge" and is in line with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC.
In addition to the notification of a non-resident taxpayer and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have several means of assessing the correctness of the taxable supplies of passenger transport services granted.
The mobile control groups of the customs office audit the certificates of buses with a permit (license) for foreign transport, which are used for the transport of passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile audit teams send an audit report to the relevant tax office.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile inspection team is entitled to demand payment of VAT from the bus driver before continuing with the next transport.
A tax non-resident may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts as to the accuracy of the VAT return, it may announce its intention to carry out an audit, which must be carried out at the tax office's office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 ( see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident taxpayer refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308 / EEC.
If a VAT return or non-resident's tax obligations are to be reviewed, the BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labor-intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable passenger services.
In particular, an audit of a non-resident's tax accounts incurs disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration must carry out an audit of foreign accounting, which means not only the need for knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger transport that takes place in Germany.
On the other hand, a tax non-resident may not only accept the right to carry out an inspection, which belongs to his national tax administration, but also the right to carry out an audit by other Member States in which he carries passengers.
In addition, in each Member State in which there is only one supply of passenger transport, the taxpayer is required to comply with all the tax obligations applicable to him in those Member States, in all the languages ​​and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
Actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore imposes disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, passenger transport between individual EU member states, resp. between Member States and third countries, on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax.
In Germany, the part of the transport that takes place on German territory is a taxable supply.
If this transport is provided for the first time by a non-established payer in Germany, he is obliged to notify the relevant tax office in advance of the provision of the transport.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable provision of part of the transport in the tax return.
The implementation of the law is very time consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are engaged in passenger transport.
Compared to the effort, the tax revenue, if realized, is rather low.
Member States which levy VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112 / EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate VAT costs, the supply of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the country where the shipment starts or where the provider is located.
Such taxation would require an amendment to Council Directive 2006/112 / EC.
Tax returns for VAT
Filing and processing of tax returns for VAT in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to file a VAT return within 25 days after the end of the tax period on the form prescribed by the Ministry of Finance, even if he has not incurred a tax liability, unless otherwise provided by law.
The actual tax liability is payable within the deadline for filing a VAT return, with the exception of the tax assessed in connection with the import of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., For which the tax due date is determined by customs regulations.
If a refund of the over - deduction results in a refundable overpayment, it shall be returned to the payer without request within 30 days of the assessment of the over - deduction.
The time limit does not apply in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings concerning the taxpayer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73, Paragraph 11 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the right to deduct tax can be exercised in a regular VAT return no later than for the last tax period of the calendar year in which the right to deduct tax could have been exercised.
After the expiration of this period, the right to deduct tax can be further exercised within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the right to deduct tax could have been exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible by filing an additional VAT return.
Amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1 January 2005, it allows the filing of an additional tax return for VAT only for the period when the right to deduct tax could be exercised for the first time.
The taxpayer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return if a) increases the tax liability by the sum of corrections, b) makes a correction that does not change the last known tax liability, but only the data previously claimed by the tax entity, c) corrects the tax rate and amount according to § 49 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
The taxpayer can submit an additional tax return for VAT if he reduces the tax liability by the sum of corrections.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The filing of a VAT tax return in electronic form can be done either via the Internet or on a technical data carrier.
Submission via the Internet can be performed as a submission with a data message provided with a guaranteed electronic signature or as a submission with a data message without a guaranteed electronic signature.
In the case of submission with a data message not provided with a guaranteed electronic signature, submission in writing is still required, ie delivery of a computer report to the tax administrator (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values ​​of intra-Community supplies / acquisitions of goods.
The values ​​of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The values ​​of supplies of goods to other Member States to persons registered for tax purposes in other Member States are compared with the data given in the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech taxpayers.
The values ​​of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from taxable persons in other Member States are compared with the values ​​obtained through VIES from recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
The tax office is carrying out a test of the credibility of tax returns for VAT within the ADIS system.
This test is performed automatically, as VAT returns cannot be assessed without performing the test.
The credibility test includes the calculation of credibility criteria and the evaluation of risky types of VAT tax returns.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 37, Paragraph 1 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll. the tax office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to fulfill a non-monetary obligation arising from this or a special tax law or imposed by a decision pursuant to this law within a specified period.
Automated tax information system, which the FI uses for technical support of tax administration.
The SAO's audit revealed that the tax authorities generally did not use the option to impose a fine on taxpayers for failing to file a VAT return.
Filing and processing of tax returns for VAT in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small businesses who are not required to pay VAT must file an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which the VAT is incurred (Paragraph 18 (2) of the UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6,136 in the previous calendar year or in the case of a newly established business, the relevant entrepreneur is obliged to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
A taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if a tax refund of more than EUR 6 136 has been made in the previous year (Paragraph 18 (2a) UStG).
VAT returns do not have to be submitted if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax period in which the VAT arose.
The tax refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FI.
There are no deadlines (according to the law) for processing tax returns and refunding excessive VAT deductions.
For the purpose of timely tax refund, it is possible to offer security for the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT law provides for the possibility of extending that period (Paragraph 18 (6) of the UStG).
Such an extension must be requested separately.
It allows you to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT liability one month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the entrepreneur must file a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the entrepreneur cannot correct an erroneous preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
Correction of the annual VAT return in favor or against the payer is possible during the following 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally only be corrected in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are required to file preliminary VAT returns electronically.
Tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid undue hardship.
The submission of an annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If it is done without certification, the payer must submit the declaration once again on paper with personal signatures.
If the payer does not file a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late submission, a penalty may be imposed on the payer (maximum 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25,000).
During the previous inspection, the BRH found that the tax authorities often did not impose this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
Therefore, the standard fine does not meet its objective of reducing the average delay, especially when filing an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values ​​of intra-Community supplies / acquisitions of goods.
The values ​​of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate line in the tax return / VAT.
In the case of VAT returns submitted on paper, copies must be made either through a scanner or by specially authorized staff.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically are immediately available to a tax office employee.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, the RMS staff will go through it and select cases that meet certain criteria.
Selected VAT returns must be checked by an employee of the tax office on the basis of an inspection report prepared by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration must roughly estimate the amount of VAT that the taxpayer must pay, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers file a VAT return within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
Depending on the amount of the payer's turnover, the tax period is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month.
In Germany, taxpayers file preliminary tax returns for VAT, depending on the tax obligations in the previous year, either within 10 days after the end of the calendar quarter or month.
Payers are required to file an annual tax return by 31 May of the following year.
The obligation to file an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the taxpayer is able to correct errors in (monthly preliminary) tax returns by submitting a single annual VAT return;
- if the payer corrects the granted intra-Community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the recapitulative statement is submitted;
- the Länder do not normally compare VIES data on intra-Community acquisitions of German taxpayers before processing their annual VAT return.
In accordance with the registration (see 4.1.3), German taxpayers are required to file an annual VAT return, regardless of the amount of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German tax authority to verify the maximum turnover limit for small businesses.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare annual VAT returns with direct tax returns and final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of a payer's turnover only from filed income tax returns.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as “SH”) is submitted in accordance with the provisions of Section 102 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. a taxable person who has made a supply of goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State.
Data on the value of delivered goods are always given in the Czech currency, broken down by individual tax subjects, stating their VAT IDs, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on provided services are not entered in the SH.
SH are submitted by payers with a monthly and quarterly tax period for each calendar quarter within 25 days after its end to the locally competent tax office.
Correction of erroneous data is performed in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
Incorrect data stated in the SH are always replaced by data stated in the subsequent SH.
As well as tax returns, taxpayers can also file SH in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not submit SH or subsequent SH and had them according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. to submit, the tax administrator shall invite him to file it and at the same time shall instruct him on the consequences in case of non-submission of the SH or subsequent SH, ie that the tax administrator is pursuant to § 37 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll. entitled to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for non-compliance with non-monetary obligations.
The SAO's audit revealed that the tax authorities generally did not use the option to impose a fine on payers for non-compliance with their legal obligations.
Especially in the case of filing a SH, tax subjects are not sufficiently motivated to fulfill their obligations, because failure to file a SH does not affect the VAT tax liability.
The tax administrator is obliged according to § 102 par. 5 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. check the data in the SH, or in the subsequent SH, remove any ambiguities and use the data to determine the tax liability.
In the event of a discrepancy between the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payer with a monthly tax period) or relevant (payer with a quarterly tax period) VAT return, the tax administrator should verify the correctness of the declared tax liability stated in the VAT return.
Incorrect data in the SH shall be removed by the tax subject by submitting the subsequent SH itself, or it may be requested to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the data on the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
- the payer does not prove the data stated in the SH (or subsequent SH), correcting them by submitting a subsequent SH,
- the tax administrator has proved that the data provided by the payer in the SH or the subsequent SH are not true.
By inserting a correction without submitting a subsequent SH, the tax administrator does not replace the taxpayer's submission, but only modifies the data in the VIES database so that they are current, complete and accurate.
SH data are sent to the Member States concerned.
They may be sent and received only by a national financial administration designated to cooperate with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic, this function is performed by the Ministry of Finance, Department of International Cooperation in VAT Administration (CLO).
O_MCTL is an automatic message that the CLO receives from other Member States.
Contains any incorrect VAT IDs listed in the submitted SH lines.
If an incorrect VAT ID is used in one of the transferred current SH or subsequent SH lines, an entry is made in the incorrect VAT ID table.
The table contains the so-called "VAT ID Doubt Notification".
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare VAT and state the values ​​of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of discrepancies in the value of acquired goods declared by the Czech taxpayer in his VAT return and in the value of delivered goods as stated by payers from other Member States in their SH are sent from the CLO to the tax office for verification.
Tax administrators are obliged to investigate irregularities.
There are three possible situations:
a) The value declared by the Czech taxpayer in the relevant lines of VAT tax returns is lower than the value of the supply declared by EU taxpayers.
In this case, the tax administrator will verify the accuracy of the data.
b) The amount of the difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself submits an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator whether, despite this fact, he will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States, which the Czech taxpayer stated in the relevant lines of the VAT return, is higher than the value of the delivered goods declared by the EU taxpayer.
Here, too, it is up to the administrator to verify the accuracy of the data.
After verifying the difference and clarifying the reasons for its occurrence, the tax administrator shall enter the result of the verification into ADIS.
The scan results are transferred back to the CLO.
The number of cases sent from the CLO to tax authorities for verification for individual quarters of 2005 is shown in Graph No. 1 (source note: Ministry of Finance).
Graph 1 above shows that the number of cases transferred from the CLO to tax authorities decreased in the individual quarters of 2005.
There was a significant decrease in the number in the 4th quarter of 2005. The CLO increased the minimum financial limit, inter alia with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between the data from VAT tax returns and the data from the EU does not always have to be caused by an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It can also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error caused by the fact that certain types of transactions may be entered in the SH in different ways in individual EU Member States.
The most common reasons for discrepancies in the values ​​of reported transactions found at audited financial authorities are listed in Table 1.
Submission and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intra-Community deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or participate in tripartite transactions are required to submit quarterly SHs listing intra-Community deliveries by recipient (§ 18a (1) UStG).
The SH must be submitted by the 10th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this period is allowed in the case of preliminary VAT returns, this also applies to SH.
SH must be delivered to CLO.
From 1 January 2007, they must be submitted electronically.
Exceptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realize that incorrect data are provided in the SH, they are obliged to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not file a SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of this report.
Part of this procedure is: - the first reminder - the second reminder associated with the threat of a fine / penalty and - the imposition of a penalty.
Although the German Tax Code allows for the imposition of a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (Paragraph 329 AO), the CLO imposes fines in three steps, in the amounts of EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a (1) (5) of the UStG provides that payers act unlawfully if they deliberately or negligently fail to file the SH properly, file it incompletely, do not file it in time or if they do not correct or repair the SH at all.
This offense can be punished by a fine of up to EUR 5,000.
Data on intra-Community supplies cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office, as the processing of SH is the sole task of the CLO.
SH data is stored only in the CLO system.
Data from the SH are therefore visually available to the tax office only after their processing at the CLO.
The deadlines for processing SH are set out in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Data from SH must be stored within three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
In case of incorrect VAT IDs in the SH of German payers, the CLO will receive the O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
The CLO contacts a specific entrepreneur and asks him for the correct data.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
During the inspection, the BRH found that most entrepreneurs corrected the VAT ID at the request of the CLO.
However, the challenge, threat and imposition of three additional fines takes too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in a cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The tax office rejected the exemption of reported intra-Community supplies in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file the corrected SH with the CLO, as the tax authorities cannot correct the data in VIES themselves.
The BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the submission of the corrected SH, so that the payers often did not comply with the request.
Due to the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, the comparison of the data on the supply of goods declared in the VAT return and in the SH will not take place before the submission of these data to the CLO of other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied in the preparation of a VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed at CLO.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then submitted to the Member States concerned.
This data is used for the purposes of control of acquisitions by tax authorities.
Once entered into the system, the CLO checks them based on comparisons with data from previous calendar quarters.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is created and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the purposes of the assessment procedure then checks this data with data on intra-Community acquisitions.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who are not fully entitled to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State file SH within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter with the locally competent tax office.
The tax authorities process the SH and transmit the data to the CLO.
The values ​​of deliveries of goods to another Member State stated by taxpayers in the SH are compared at the tax authorities with the values ​​of deliveries of goods to another Member State stated by these taxpayers in VAT tax returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made an intra-Community supply are required to submit a SH on a quarterly basis, by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers submit to CLO, from 1 January 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities have the information from the SH available only after it has been processed at the CLO.
Payers from the Czech Republic and Germany only state the delivery of goods in the SH, the provision of services is not stated in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the erroneous lines submitted by SH themselves.
As a result of this limited access to German VIES data, the incorrect VAT ID was not corrected, even though the payer provided the FA with the correct VAT ID.
The German tax administration does not compare the data on intra-Community supplies, which are given in the VAT return of the German taxpayer and his SH.
The differences between the data of the two reports are usually not detected before the German CLO provides data from VIES to other Member States.
Given the findings of the BRH, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the transmitted data in VIES.
Data on the supply of goods to Czech taxpayers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech taxpayers in their VAT tax returns.
The comparison is performed by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are forwarded to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in taxpayers' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax authorities control the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions of other payers only if the RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is intended for control anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities of the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
Combating carousel fraud requires constantly updated information on intra-Community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, especially VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if payers submit SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, as most taxpayers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file monthly VAT returns - and SH does not require any additional information than the tax return.
To avoid bureaucratic costs, filing a SH may be linked to filing a VAT return.
However, the obligation to submit SH on a monthly basis would cause more time discrepancies between the reporting of intra-Community supply and intra-Community acquisition and could increase the flow of data between CLOs.
In 2006, the German federal government considered the general provisions of the monthly SHs.
Its implementation failed due to the doubts of the federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of VIES data to the CLOs of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the obligation to submit monthly SHs and monthly data transmission were to be effective, a monthly update of VIES would require a European standard for monthly SHs.
Statistical data on delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In foreign trade, Germany is the Czech Republic's most important trading partner.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions in goods between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT numbers or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports submitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for individual quarters of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show significant differences.
These differences may be due to the different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO relates their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO relates their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL message was received.
International level 3 information exchange
Implementation of international exchange of information in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-Community commercial transactions and the payers who have carried out such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between two basic categories of exchange of information, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without previous applications.
The international exchange of information on request is carried out in the form of so-called requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "FDI"), using standardized SCAC forms.
Tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI, resp. the replies to the FDI received through the CFO of the CLO, which translates the information provided on the standardized SCAC forms into a foreign language and sends it to other Member States.
The CLO also ensures the receipt of ŽOI from other Member States and the responses to sent ŽOI, their translation into Czech and distribution to the locally competent tax administrators for settlement.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 sets a maximum time limit for the processing of FDI at 3 months from the receipt of the application.
All SOIs handed over during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany were subject to the SAO inspection.
Out of the total number of 94 ŽOIs received in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 cases (ie 74.5%) were settled within the set three-month period, another 23 cases (ie 24.5%) were settled after this period and for the remaining 1 case the reply was not sent to Germany until the SAO's inspection.
More detailed information on the deadlines within which responses to the ZOI received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic is given in Graph No. 2.
Out of the total number of 335 ŽOI sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (ie 40.6%) received a response within the set three-month period, another 179 (ie 53.4%) requests were answered after this period and 19 cases ( ie 5.7%) the response from Germany was not delivered until the SAO's inspection (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine from the submitted data when the response from Germany was delivered).
More detailed information on the deadlines within which responses to the ZOI sent to Germany were delivered to the Czech Republic is given in Graph No. 3.
The percentage expression of the values ​​of intra-community transactions, stated in the ŽOI transferred between the Czech Republic and Germany, is shown in Graph No. 4.
As can be seen from the graph above, the value of business transactions examined through the FDI was most often in the range above EUR 60,000.
The international exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic, resp. structured automatic exchange of information, or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax administrators from other Member States are often provided with information that may be relevant to them in the administration of VAT without prior request.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at the CLO.
The information is transmitted electronically between Member States.
"Automatic exchange" according to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request, at pre-established regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as that information becomes available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of an automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax administrator from the form of the Report on the Delivery of a New Means of Transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
When processing the above-mentioned form, the tax administrator fills in the necessary data into a specially created template and immediately transmits it to the contact person at the financial directorate where this data is collected and within the set deadline, ie no later than two months from the end of the quarter in which the information was available to the CLO for further processing and transfer to other Member States.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales, which are exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions that appear to be unjustified and information on potential "missing traders".
That information is sent to other Member States in the form of a spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of international information exchange in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the locally competent tax office.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form by e-mail directly to the German CLO, which forwards the SCAC forms to the foreign CLO.
Tax authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information in German only; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information inspected by the BRH were sent in order to ensure the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it will check the value of the supply of goods or services specified in the request for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
If there is no reasonable reason for this request, the German CLO will reject any request containing an amount lower than this set limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)], if these texts are not in German or English.
To respond to a request for information, the CLO sends the request to the relevant tax office with reference to the three-month deadline.
There are no further deadlines for processing applications at specific organizational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor elapsed time limits, it lacks sufficient staff capacity to alert the tax authorities to responding to blank information requests.
The tax authorities will obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit, which covers any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only cover one recent business transaction.
This short and typ explicit type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has proved its usefulness in investigating individual taxable business transactions.
As part of the automatic exchange without prior request, Germany provides other Member States with information - on the VAT IDs assigned to payers resident in other Member States, - on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, Germany has undertaken to provide the following information to other Member States through a structured automatic exchange:
a. Supply of new means of transport to businesses without using their VAT ID, b. dispatch or catalog sale in other Member States which is not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intra-Community acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d intra-Community supply of goods which the German payer did not report in SH because he treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. a potential "missing trader" who carried out intra-Community transactions regardless of the validity of their VAT ID, f. traders ”or those recipients who misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The sending of ŽOI or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the locally competent financial authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech - English) and translates the sent information into English, resp. German language, the German tax authorities follow the instruction to write the ZOI or spontaneous information only in German on a monolingual form.
The German CLO does not translate German texts.
By inspecting ZOIs submitted between the Czech Republic and Germany in the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration processed 74.5% of received applications within the set three-month period, while ZOIs sent to Germany were processed by the German tax administration. within the set time limit only in 40.6% of cases.
Although the German CLO draws the attention of the tax authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not follow the elapsed deadlines.
The result of missing alerts is a large number of delayed responses to the ZOI.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended to make regular notifications to the CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO is now alerting the tax authorities to reply to unfinished replies to the FDI.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at various organizational levels of the tax administration deal with VAT risk management.
Within the Ministry of Finance, the following departments deal with the issue of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The VAT Methodology and Performance Department and within it the Risk Risk Management Department, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates the trends of these risks at the domestic and Community level.
Nationwide, it coordinates the functioning of the role of VAT Credibility and the use of data from the VIES system in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-Community transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, conceptually processes risk management in the area of ​​VAT and cooperates in this area with the relevant EU institutions and other Member States.
The Department of International Cooperation in VAT Administration, which, inter alia, ensures the exchange of information in the field of VAT, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyzes data from other Member States contained in VIES, provides public information and provides other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of the Council Regulation. (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT numbers or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports submitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for individual quarters of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show significant differences.
These differences may be due to the different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO relates their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO relates their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL message was received.
The Tax Audit and Search Methodology Department, which, among other things, performs risk analysis within the methodological management of tax audits and, in accordance with risk analysis, sets priorities for tax audits in financial directorate plans, prepares risk analyzes to reduce tax evasion, including gathering knowledge gained during administration. taxes and other sources and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Search departments are set up in the financial directorates, which, among other things, search for tax entities and areas that are at risk of tax fraud (eg online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), search for unregistered tax entities for tax evasion (eg in the field of internet services, job placement, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of links to chain fraud and transmission of information to territorial financial authorities.
Specialized control departments have been set up at selected 12 tax offices.
They have regional competence, tax inspections outside the territorial competence of financial authorities are performed on the basis of authorization.
The need to set up a specialized tax audit department arose on the basis of the increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which occur mainly in entities linked to chains.
These departments focus on the control of tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and tax entities of a large scope of activities in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms for reducing VAT risks have been integrated into the ADIS system: - the role Credibility of VAT returns, used to evaluate the riskiness of submitted tax returns, VIES, through which tax administrations have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, among other things: - to verify the validity of VAT ID of payers from other Member States, - to obtain from other Member States the values ​​of goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in SH by all his suppliers from other Member States, carry out a formal check of the data provided by payers from the Czech Republic in the SH before sending these data to other Member States, - generate a list of payers for which the data on supplies of goods to other Member States stated in VAT tax returns do not match the data in the SH, - to generate a list of taxpayers for whom the value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States stated in the VAT returns does not match the data declared in the SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
As part of the activity to reduce the risks of tax evasion, tax administrators have access to the registers of state administration bodies such as the Commercial Register, the Real Estate Cadastre, the Register of Motor Vehicles, the Register of Trade Licensing, etc.
More detailed information is given in chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal (federal) structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (especially the CLO) and the tax administrations of 16 federal states participate in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At CLO level, the ST I 2 unit (hereinafter referred to as “KUSS” - the coordination unit for special VAT audits and tax investigations) collects the findings of the audit concerning tax fraud in a special database called OPUS.
KUSS, in cooperation with tax authorities, has introduced a new database called ZAUBER intended for the transmission of the names of companies of tax fraudsters "missing traders".
KUSS coordinates related cases of domestic and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of KUSS is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other CLO and MoF departments are entrusted with RMS-related duties and powers.
At CLO level, a formal control of the composition of VAT IDs of other Member States in the SH submitted by German payers is introduced.
This formal check is carried out before providing the data from the SH to other Member States, in order to improve the comprehensibility and use of the provided VIES data (see 4.4.2).
The validation of the VAT IDs listed in the SH is performed on the basis of the O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure for correcting an invalid VAT ID, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS at CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and generates several types of control reports based on several characteristics that usually appear in so-called carousel trading operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders".
The Länder tax authorities are instructed to prepare these inspection reports and, in some cases, to report on the results of their CLO findings.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if the existence of a tax fraud case is to be assumed with sufficient probability (instead of focusing exclusively on the company's turnover).
The BRH therefore suggested to the Ministry of Finance that various characteristics be taken into account when processing the reports.
The RMS should also address other factors, such as the taxpayer's payment behavior (morale), industry (economic activities) or shareholder structure.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the federal states and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, the RMS generates a list of those taxpayers who have declared intra-Community supplies in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the complete SH submission.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-Community acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with VIES data.
The Länder tax administrations try to avoid comparing quarterly data, as this comparison would reveal too much inconsistent data, which is attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or fraud; for example:
- different timing of the intra-Community transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
- different accounting for sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing VAT and VIES data, many Länder have introduced RMS elements that are based on VAT data and certain other facts (such as company name structure, shareholder age, number of employees and taxpayer's payment behavior / morale). ).
Bavaria has introduced a rules-based RMS that allows a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to program their own rules for identifying potential tax fraudsters.
This RMS is applied at the moment when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
The competent tax office will therefore receive a recommendation drawn up by the RMS before VAT is assessed.
As this RMS is not able to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules based on the feedback from the tax authorities.
The Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania administrative district has programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data from tax files in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
Based on these data, RMS is able to determine the characteristics of tax evasion.
Once a month, RMS creates a list of tax files that are suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities use this list as a basis for deciding on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
Following the audit, auditors must report their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The North Rhine-Westphalia administrative region uses an adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large amount of data under consideration of VAT returns and some other facts, this neural-fuzzy system or data-mining system calculates the probability that a certain taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential fraudsters.
Local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for control and report the control findings to the data processing center.
The implementation of one of these three RMSs in the other Länder is ongoing.
Given that none of these three RMSs is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems to be useful in tackling tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and the BRH found that each Member State developed its own RMS.
Like the different approaches in the three Länder of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
EU Member States' tax authorities are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud - is not proving to be a national problem, but rather a European one.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State but in several States.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
VAT losses caused by fraud in the EU do not have to affect the Member State of the fraud initiator.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and discussion on RMS.
Selected audit findings when verifying business transactions
As part of cooperation on the implementation of parallel audits, the SAO and the BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions that were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
Furthermore, both audit institutions jointly examined the implementation of several business transactions in which there were doubts about their implementation, respectively. inconsistencies in the way taxpayers from both countries reported these business transactions in their VAT returns, resp. SH.
At the request of the BRH, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases concerning business transactions carried out between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
Furthermore, in 43 cases, the SAO examined the values ​​of intra-Community transactions with Germany, which Czech taxpayers reported in their tax returns and SH, on the basis of BRH notifications.
At the request of the SAO, the BRH examined a total of 23 cases concerning business transactions carried out between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the CLO.
Examination of selected cases revealed, among other things, that the different way of registration in the EU Member States leads to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to the data in VIES, the Czech payer was to acquire in III. quarter of 2004 from a German payer of goods worth EUR 60,500.
As the Czech taxpayer reported the acquisition of goods only in the value corresponding to EUR 29,869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the delivered goods.
In response to the ZOI delivered from Germany, the German side stated that in II. In the fourth quarter of 2004, the German payer supplied goods to the Czech payer in the amount of EUR 27,381; quarter in the amount of EUR 31,997 and in IV. quarter of 2004 in the amount of EUR 10 276.
The reply further showed that the VAT ID of the German taxpayer was only valid from 28 September 2004, but in 2006 the German CLO retroactively issued a VAT ID certificate from 1 May 2004 following an additional application by the German taxpayer for a VAT ID certificate. .
The German payer repaired SH.
Based on this information, the Czech payer was acquiring the goods.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer, on the basis of the tax administrator's investigation, filed additional VAT returns for individual tax periods in 2004, increasing the value of goods acquired from other Member States and claiming VAT deduction. acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax administrator could not unambiguously determine whether they also included the values ​​of supplies from the above-mentioned German supplier.
Based on the SAO 's request, the BRH found that the German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, as he did not request a VAT ID during registration, he was only assigned an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although it is usually not possible in Germany to assign a VAT ID retroactively, in this case a German tax official assigned the above VAT ID retroactively to the above German taxpayer on 1 May 2004.
The German CLO assigns a VAT ID retroactively, unless the German entrepreneur has caused a delay in allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by the CLO after the VAT ID payer's request.
In this case, the CLO assigns the VAT ID retroactively because the trader does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community supplies under § 6 of the German VAT Act.
Conversely, a German recipient does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier in order to declare an intra-Community acquisition.
Due to these different procedures between Member States, the German CLO retroactively assigned a VAT ID in this particular case.
2.
As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested verification of the German VAT payer's registration.
VIES indicated the date of registration on 5 March 2005, while the confirmation of registration of the German payer issued by the locally competent German tax office indicated the date on 1 October 2004.
In a reply received from Germany, the German side stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1 October 2004, but that the VAT ID had not been provided to it in Germany for organizational reasons until 16 February 2005.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator, the SAO found out that the Czech tax administrator had performed a VAT inspection of the Czech taxpayer for tax period III. quarter 2004 to II. quarter of 2005.
Through this inspection, the tax office found that the Czech taxpayer included in the VAT return services in the amount of CZK 9,897 (EUR 314) provided to the German taxpayer in the period before his registration for VAT (ie before 1 October 2004).
For the tax period III. In the fourth quarter of 2004, the tax office assessed VAT to the tax subject in the amount of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
Based on the SAO's request, the BRH found out that the German taxpayer was assigned a VAT ID only on 16 February 2005, when he informed the tax office about his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the taxpayer reported an intra-Community acquisition from the Czech Republic in the amount of EUR 160 (approx. CZK 5,000).
3. The Czech taxpayer reported in the tax return for VAT for September 2004 and SH for III. quarter of 2004 delivery of goods worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) to a German payer.
During the verification of the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax administrator found out that his registration was valid from 11 November 2004, ie only after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech taxpayer submitted an additional DAP to VAT, in which he reported the tax base from domestic transactions in the amount of CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) and VAT in the amount of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692), which he paid.
Inquiring with the locally competent tax office in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that the Czech taxpayer had subsequently filed a request for reopening of proceedings concerning an additional VAT return and submitted as evidence a confirmation from the German tax administration stating that the German taxpayer had been taxed since 1 January. 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the German taxpayer's registration within the international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany showed that the German taxpayer was assigned a VAT ID only on 11 November 2004, ie after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the application for reopening of the proceedings.
The BRH found that in this case it was not an intra-Community acquisition of goods, because the German taxpayer did not obtain a VAT ID until 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient recognized the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and reported VAT on that acquisition when it claimed a refund of input tax of the same amount.
However, as there would be no change in the value of the VAT which the German taxpayer was required to pay, the German tax authorities did not correct the information in his VAT return.
The BRH also found that the name of the German taxpayer, mentioned in the ŽOI, was changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, as a result of which two German tax entities were confused.
This change in the name of the German taxpayer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech taxpayer in the first quarter of 2005 in the amount of EUR 22,686 from a German taxpayer.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that this administrator had conducted a local investigation with the Czech taxpayer, verifying that the delivery of goods had taken place and that the Czech taxpayer had invoiced and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech taxpayer did not declare the acquisition of goods in the VAT return, because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found out that the German taxpayer was registered for VAT for intra-Community transactions only on 21 April 2005, ie only after the delivery to the Czech taxpayer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German taxpayer's registration certificate so that, if necessary, he could take steps to assess the tax.
The Czech Tax Office assessed the given business transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer from Germany, and therefore did not additionally assess the tax on the Czech payer from the said business transaction.
The BRH found that, under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for the intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier only needs to have the VAT ID of the acquirer from another Member State and must be able to prove the transport of the goods to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, it was therefore an intra-Community transaction and VAT should be assessed in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed this transaction, as the supply of the machine at that value was not the basic object of the German supplier's business.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to respond to R & D & I which concern intra - Community transactions of less than EUR 15 000:.
According to VIES data in III. quarter of 2004 to purchase goods worth EUR 12,561 from a German payer.
The Czech tax administrator performed a tax audit of the tax subject for this tax period.
As part of international administrative cooperation, he requested the German tax authorities to verify the supply of those goods using the SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never traded with the German company and that the acquisition of the goods had not been accounted for in his accounts.
The German tax authorities rejected the request for the provision of evidence - contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents, on the grounds that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no further explanatory justification was provided.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence for the additional assessment of the tax on the acquired goods, he terminated the tax audit without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed in the original amount.
Based on the SAO's request, the BRH found that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (§ 22 a - e UStG).
The German taxpayer declared those supplies in his annual VAT return and in SH.
He was granted the right to exemption from delivery.
Based on the BRH's notification, the German tax office will send to the Czech Republic the documents necessary for the additional assessment of the tax on the acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
As mentioned in Chapter 4.6.1, responses to the ZOI sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the set three - month deadline more often than responses from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO found that the Czech Tax Administration sent a request for information to Germany on 5 October 2005 concerning the verification of the value of the goods supplied in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German taxpayer reported in SH for this period the supply of goods to the Czech taxpayer in the amount of EUR 86,307, but the Czech taxpayer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only in the value corresponding to EUR 35,314.
In its reply to the ZOI, delivered to the Czech Republic on 9 May 2006, ie after the expiry of the deadline for processing set out in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German side stated that the request could not be processed because German company was terminated at the end of 2005.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not meet the deadline for the settlement of the ZOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the documents necessary for tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator requested, by means of an SCAC form, an inspection of the supply of cars in the amount of EUR 1,265,554 to a German taxpayer, which took place in III. and IV. quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that no reply to the SOI had been received from Germany until the time of the inspection.
The SAO also found out by asking the locally competent tax administrator that the Czech taxpayer did not include in the VAT return the supply of new means of transport for the said German taxpayer in the amount of CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375,472).
The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity submitted a subsequent SH.
Based on the SAO's request, the BRH found that, for technical reasons, the German CLO had not handed over the above-mentioned ŽOI to the locally competent tax office for verification.
Following the notification of the BRH, an inspection was carried out in Germany at the German acquirer, during which it was found that the acquisition of all cars was properly taxed and that the cars in question were sold to another payer in Germany.
8. According to the data from VIES, the Czech payer was to acquire in IV. quarter of 2004 from a German payer a passenger car worth EUR 48,500.
The Czech payer did not admit the acquisition of these goods.
By inquiring with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that the Czech taxpayer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
The tax returns were not filed by the Czech taxpayer even after the summons of the tax administrator, therefore on 23 May 2005 the tax office assessed him with VAT in the amount of CZK 0 for the period from October to December 2004.
On 2 June 2005, CLO drew attention to the above-mentioned delivery from a German payer.
As the Czech taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, the tax administrator sent the ŽOI to Germany concerning the above-mentioned delivery.
As the reply to the ZOI was not delivered to the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known until the end of the SAO's inspection how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained by the international exchange.
As of 23 August 2005, the Tax Office canceled the VAT registration of the Czech taxpayer due to non-fulfillment of obligations arising from the VAT Act.
In some cases, only a partial reply was sent to the ŽOI, because the control performed by the tax authorities at the payers was not completed at the time of the SAO and BRH inspection:
