11.
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer was to acquire goods worth EUR 35,716 from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005, but the Czech payer did not admit this acquisition.
As the Czech taxpayer did not co-operate with the tax administrator and did not carry out any activities at the company's registered office, the Czech tax administrator requested to verify in the international exchange of information how the German taxpayer communicated with the Czech taxpayer.
The reply to the ŽOI received from Germany showed that, according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech tax entity is unknown at the communicated address and that the goods were taken over by the agreed carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only delivered goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent a false confirmation to the German payer about the payment of EUR 155,153 in favor of the German payer.
After finding fraud by the Czech acquirer, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the delivered material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7,916.
Inquiring with the locally competent tax office in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the tax administrator, on the basis of information obtained, assessed the Czech VAT payer for the acquisition of goods from other Member States in the amount of CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).
Based on the SAO's request, the BRH confirmed that the German supplier reported the delivery of goods to the Czech payer after repairs only in the amount of EUR 7,916.
According to the German legal situation, the German taxpayer reported the adjusted values ​​of the goods and the reduction in the taxable amount in the quarter in which the correction took place.

12.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested, using the SCAC form, to verify the supply of goods and services effected in III. quarter of 2005.
According to this ŽOI, in this period the Czech payer was to deliver goods to the German payer in the total value of EUR 396,126 and provide services in the amount of EUR 11,885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech taxpayer in order to verify this supply.
In response to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech taxpayer had supplied the German taxpayer with a production line, including assembly.
The individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech payer before the accession of the Czech Republic to the EU, and after 1 May 2004, the line was assembled on the basis of an order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.
And III. In the first quarter of 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for EUR 107,100 for assembly and EUR 11,885 for services.
The German payer took over the issued invoices, but did not acknowledge them and did not pay them.
The SAO also found out by asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that all invoices were duly registered in the Czech taxpayer's accounts.
In tax returns for VAT for III. In the quarter of 2005, only the amounts that were documented by the Czech payer and that relate to invoicing after 1 May 2004 are listed.
BRH found that, based on a response from the Czech tax administration, the locally competent tax office in Germany came to the conclusion that the transaction involved the delivery of goods from a Czech taxpayer to a German taxpayer, including assembly services.
In this special case, the place of so-called performance of work is where the production line was assembled.
According to the German VAT law, the German recipient of the supplied service is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient can claim a VAT deduction from the same amount.
As there would be no change in the value of the VAT which the German taxpayer was required to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax authorities.
13. According to data from VIES, the Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer C in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify this supply.
In its reply to the ŽOI, the German side stated that already in 2004 the German payer C delivered this machine to the Czech payer B, who, however, was to return this machine to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but transported to the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, the reply to the request for information showed that in February 2005 the German payer C sold the machine to the Czech payer A.
This payer took over the machine at the seat of the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
As the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-community delivery of goods.
By asking the tax administrator of the locally competent payer B, the SAO found that, according to VIES data, the German payer C had supplied in III. quarter of 2004 to the Czech payer B goods (another machine) in the amount of 88,027 EUR.
Payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the locally competent tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the ZOI to Germany.
According to the reply to this request, the machine was delivered.
By further investigation of payer B, the Czech tax administrator found that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in payer B 's accounts and that it could be a machine of the same type as that supplied by Czech payer C to Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax administrator locally responsible for payer A carried out a local investigation at this payer.
The tax administrator had at his disposal the invoice of the German payer C dated 7 February 2005, on which the payer A was listed as the customer of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that payer A did not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payer A had a leasing contract with another Czech company, where the subject of the lease was a machine of the same type.
The machine was handed over from the leasing company on February 9, 2005, and the machine was transported by the leasing company.
The Czech tax office did not use the information contained in the reply to the request for information to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found out that the German payer C did not deliver the machine worth EUR 88,027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not recognize the VAT exemption for German taxpayer C and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D delivered the machine to Czech payer B.
According to German law, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that the German payer C stated in its SH for the first quarter of 2005 the delivery of a machine worth EUR 58,000 to the Czech payer A.
This supply was not verified during the tax audit carried out by the German tax office.

14.

The ŽOI further stated that the German payer had not carried out any active business activity since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had conducted a local investigation with the Czech taxpayer.
According to the executive of the Czech company, in the above case it was probably a claim of a German taxpayer against the German tax administration, which was filed by the Czech taxpayer as a partner of a German company with the German tax office.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator does not yet have any information that the German tax administration would address the issue relating to the Czech taxpayer.
According to the available information, it was not a supply of goods, nevertheless the stated value is still included in the VIES system as an intra-Community supply of goods to a Czech payer from Germany.

17.
The German payer had in IV. quarter of 2004 to deliver to the Czech payer goods worth EUR 11,600.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested confirmation of whether the Czech taxpayer actually existed, as the alleged partner of the German taxpayer had set up several fictitious companies in Germany.
During the verification of the business transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of the goods to the tax office.
According to the Czech payer, however, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were resold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer submitted documents on the sale of goods for January 2005.
The Czech taxpayer was not registered in Germany as a VAT payer, he did not declare or pay tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic or in Germany.
All these facts indicated tax evasion in Germany and the Czech tax administrator informed them to the German tax administration in response to the ZOI.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer, on the basis of the investigations carried out, submitted an additional tax return for VAT for IV. quarter of 2004, in which he included the value of the acquisition of goods from, inter alia, a German taxpayer and at the same time claimed the right to deduct tax on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
He did not state VAT from the sale of goods in Germany in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return after the local investigation without change.
According to the Czech legislation, in this case it was not the acquisition of goods from other Member States, because the goods were not sent or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore made an incorrect conclusion to the local investigation.
The BRH found that immediately after receiving the reply to the ŽOI, which stated that the goods had not left Germany, the German tax administrator corrected the German taxpayer's tax return and demanded VAT of EUR 1,600 from him.
In addition, the competent tax office has sent a notification to the tax office of the actual consignee to ensure that the resale of the goods is properly taxed.

18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech taxpayer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47,400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
Attached to the application was a copy of the certificate of registration of the Czech VAT payer.
A copy of the passport of the person who, as has been said, was to transport the car was also attached.
During the investigation, the Czech tax administrator found out that the passport was stolen, the person listed in it did not import any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax administrator.
This information was included by the Czech tax administrator in the reply to the ŽOI together with the statement that he could not confirm the acquisition of the goods - the car in question.
The SAO, inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found out that the Czech taxpayer was not domiciled at the address specified in the Commercial Register and that the company's executive officer was non-contact.
Following the reprimand proceedings for the February 2005 tax period, the Czech tax administrator imposed a tax liability of CZK 0 on the Czech taxpayer.
Further investigation by the Czech tax administrator found that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity, which bought it through an advertisement on the Internet.
The BRH found that the locally competent German tax administrator, on the basis of the Czech reply to the ŽOI, would not recognize the German taxpayer's right to exemption from this supply from VAT.
19. During the audit, the German tax office was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3000 between the value of the acquired goods reported in the taxpayer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was stated that the Czech payer was to deliver during the IV. quarter to 2004 to the first quarter of 2005 to a German payer of goods worth EUR 89,424.
As the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax administrator requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the framework of the international exchange of information.
In response to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the sole executive officer of the Czech company had been deleted from the Commercial Register on 8 July 2005 and the new executive officer had not been registered.
The German consignee of the goods appeared to be a relative of a partner in Czech society.
The Czech taxpayer filed tax returns for VAT and SH, which was signed by an unauthorized person - the said partner of the company - after deleting the executive officer from the Commercial Register.
The accountant of the Czech taxpayer confirmed to the tax administrator that the company's partner deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash receipts were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic, by asking the locally competent tax office, found out that the tax administrator recognized the Czech taxpayer as IV. In the first quarter of 2004, entitlement to exemption from VAT on the supply of goods to another Member State in the amount of CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) and in the first quarter of 2005 in the amount of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548).
The BRH found that the German tax administrator had not corrected the German acquirer's VAT return because a German judge had in the meantime confirmed the insolvency of the German taxpayer.
As the previous audit did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to enforce the assessed tax liability.
20. According to data in VIES, a German payer purchased goods worth EUR 4,251,196 from the Czech Republic in 2005, after purchasing goods worth EUR 43,274 in the previous year.
The German taxpayer did not report an intra-Community acquisition in the 2004 tax return or in the 2005 tax return.
In addition, it did not show adequate supplies.
Due to these differences, the German tax office sent the ŽOI for the 4th quarter of 2005 and the 1st quarter of 2006.
In these two quarters, the Czech supplier reported in SH an intra-Community supply of goods to a German payer in the total amount of CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6 September 2006, the ŽOI was delivered, in which the German side requested to check whether the intra-Community supplies declared by the Czech payer had taken place.
In response to this ŽOI, the Czech Tax Administration stated that it was not possible to comply with the German party's request because the Czech taxpayer had no executive.
As follows from the materials provided by the SAO by the relevant tax administrator, on 30 March 2006 a protocol was drawn up with the executive of the Czech taxpayer on the commencement of the VAT audit for IV. quarter of 2004 and January to December 2005.
The taxpayer was also invited by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above periods, but did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the sole executive officer of the Czech payer ceased to hold office on 16 May 2006, and no new executive officer was appointed.
As of April 2006, the Czech taxpayer has stopped filing VAT returns.
As part of its audit, the SAO, in cooperation with the BRH, examined, among other things, several cases of intra-Community supplies made between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the cases examined was exchanged between the two SAIs through the CLOs of both countries.
21. A Czech company (eCR) which is not resident in Germany has informed the relevant tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Due to this information, the company has been registered since June 2005, but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) received an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind turbines and for the supply of these wind turbines in the name, at the risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to the lack of its own capacities, the Czech company handed over part of the order to a German payer (eD), who is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relations and the method of transporting wind turbines:
According to the German legal situation, the place of implementation of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
- A Danish businessman (eDK) sent wind farms for assembly under his own name, at his own risk and on his own account to Austria.
As the installation of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind turbines is taxable in Austria.
- As the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his own risk and at his own expense, the delivery by a German subcontractor (eDK) took place where the transport began - in Germany.
Although the wind farms were sent to another Member State and the recipient is a registered payer from another Member State, the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption because another Member State of destination is different from another Member State of the Czech company's registered office.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery to the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of the transport.
The transportation of some wind power plants was started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- The delivery of those wind power plants that are manufactured in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- Delivery of other wind turbines, which are manufactured in Germany, took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intra-Community deliveries from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-community deliveries from Germany to Austria.
The BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not report any intra - Community acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany, nor did it submit SH to the German CLO.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intra-Community supplies uniformly as intra-Community supplies from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (eCR) did not report any intra-Community deliveries to Austria, but intra-community deliveries to Denmark.
An examination of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), although this case shows no signs of tax fraud or evasion.
Furthermore, the SAO and the BRH examined the transactions in order to point out the differences between the tax return and the data from the VIES system, which were caused by different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes in legislation need time for both new and tax authorities to put new legislation into practice:
22. In SH for II. to IV. In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer reported an intra-Community delivery to a German payer in the total amount of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
During the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported an intra-Community delivery to another German payer in the total amount of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to the information provided by the SAO from the BRH, in both cases it was the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above deliveries in the SH in accordance with the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., In force in 2004.
Further examination of the above transactions, the group of auditing SAOs found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal regulation of deliveries, resp. acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intra-community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legislation in force in 2004, it was not an intra-community acquisition, but a taxable supply with the place of supply in Germany.
The difference in legal regulations in the Czech Republic was eliminated by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., Which amends certain acts in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2005.
23. In examining selected intra-Community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was further found that the Czech payer reported in SH for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2005 an intra-Community supply to a German payer in the total value of CZK 240,411,163 (EUR 8,071,823) and another Czech payer. reported in SH for the same period an intra-Community supply to a German payer in the total amount of CZK 263,470,776 (EUR 8,846,050).
According to the information provided by the SAO from the BRH, in both cases it was a supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., Effective from 1 January 2005, in the case of electricity supply, the place of performance is the place where the acquirer has its registered office, place of business or where it has an establishment for which these goods are delivered.
Therefore, in 2005, Czech payers should not indicate the supply of electricity to SH.
As the two above-mentioned payers reported an intra-Community supply of electricity in SH, the data in VIES were distorted by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation met the objectives of the BRH and the SAO.
Both SAIs have gained a deeper knowledge of VAT administration systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that the legislation in the field of VAT administration differs.
During parallel inspections, suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were identified.
It makes sense to check some of them later.
Based on the audit findings, both SAIs made recommendations regarding VAT administration.
Follow-up to these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
New experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of both control institutions are the basis for the successful implementation of the following controls of the VAT administration.
Communique
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the Results of International Cooperation in Excise Tax Administration Controls between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Foreword
The presented joint report informs about the course and result of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, focused on the administration of excise duties in the period after both countries join the European Union.
The co - operation was carried out on the basis of an agreement on co - operation in control activities, concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen with regard to the fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties, which occurred in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union on 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the European Union's internal market requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of tax-free goods until the day of their delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows for the movement of goods under fiscal supervision under a duty suspension arrangement.
The system places great demands on tax administrations and presupposes close cooperation between the competent administrative authorities of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in controls on the administration of excise duties for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of control: (Czech Republic) Administration of excise duties (Slovak Republic) Procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise duties
On 8 February 2006, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SAO-CR”) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SAO SR”) concluded an “Agreement on Cooperation in Audit Activities”.
The subject of the agreement was cooperation in parallel inspections "Excise Tax Administration", included in the SAO-CR inspection plan for 2005 under No. 05/34, and "Control of the procedure of customs authorities in excise administration", included in the SAO inspection plan SR for the year 2006 under No. 48/11.
Parallel inspections were in the nature of coordinated inspections.
The co-operation consisted in exchanging information which the contracting parties could not obtain during the control of excise administration in their territory and in preparing a joint final report on the result of controls in accordance with European implementing directives for the implementation of INTOSAI auditing standards - Directive 31.
In the territory of the Czech Republic, inspections (hereinafter referred to as the “Czech Republic”) were carried out by groups of inspectors from the state budget department and territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Western Bohemia, Northwestern Bohemia, Northeastern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia. February to 2 June 2006.
27 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The auditees were the General Directorate of Customs ("GDC") and 11 tax offices.
Within the GDC, 12 selected customs offices out of the total number of 54 were inspected.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the “SR”) was carried out by the Finance and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice branches at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
8 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel controls was to examine the customs authorities' practice in administering excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation focused on the procedure of tax administrators in supervising the transport of excisable goods, especially on the registration of started and terminated transport in the regime of conditional tax exemption, and on the exchange of information within mutual administrative assistance between excise tax administrators of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
2. Administration of excise duties
Until 31 December 2003, the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was performed by financial authorities.
From 1 January 2004, this agenda was taken over by the customs authorities, which until now collected excise duty only on imports.
Mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in the Czech Republic.
The state budget revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic totaled CZK 82.8 billion in 2004, and excise duties accounted for 19.5% of state budget revenue from taxes and fees of CZK 424.7 billion.
In 2005, state budget revenues from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the share of state budget revenues from taxes and fees in the amount of CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the revenue from the excise duty on mineral oils to the state budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it was 90.9%.
The difference compared to 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the revenue of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the Slovak Republic has been performed by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of the excise duty on mineral oil, which they have been administering since 1 January 2002.
Until then, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the tax authorities.
Mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in the Slovak Republic.
The state budget revenue from excise duties in the Slovak Republic in 2004 totaled Sk 43.4 billion, and excise duties accounted for 20.7% of total tax revenues of Sk 209.5 billion.
In 2005, state budget revenue from excise duties was Sk 50 billion, and excise duties accounted for 22.5% of total tax revenues of Sk 222.6 billion.
Graph No. 1 - Comparison of revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenues from excise taxes
Legislation in both countries is based on European Union legislation in this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12 / EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products (hereinafter "Directive 92/12 / EEC") ), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as 'Regulation No 2073/2004'), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the official accompanying document for shipments - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649/92 on the simplified accompanying document for the movement of excise goods which have been subject to excise duty suspension released for home use in the Member State of dispatch within the Community ('Regulation No 3649/92').
The basic legal regulation regulating the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll., On excise duties, as amended, (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 353/2003 Coll.”), Effective from 1 January 2004.
When administering excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are bound, inter alia, by the following generally binding legal regulations: - Act No. 98/2004 Coll., On excise duty on mineral oil, as amended (hereinafter “Act No. 98/2004 Coll. Act No. 104/2004 Coll., on excise duty on wine, as amended (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 104/2004 Coll.”), - Act No. 105/2004 On excise duty on alcohol, as amended (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 105/2004 Coll.”), - Act No. 106/2004 Coll., On excise duty on tobacco products, as amended regulations (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 106/2004 Coll.”), - Act No. 107/2004 Coll., on excise duty on beer, as amended (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 107/2004 Coll. of.").
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty between the Member States of the European Union
The conditions for the movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty are laid down in Directive 92/12 / EEC in Title III - Movement of goods, Articles 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, the transport of those goods may be carried out only by an authorized warehousekeeper, which is a natural or legal person authorized by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch excise goods.
The consignee in another Member State may be an authorized warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorized warehousekeeper, who, however, may not store or re-dispatch these products under the duty suspension arrangement.
Authorized warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic means the operator of a tax warehouse, the economic entity is the authorized consignee for repeated or one-time acceptance of products subject to excise duty.
According to Directive 92/12 / EEC, the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty is possible only with an accompanying document.
The consignment note shall be issued by the consignor in four copies before the start of the shipment, unless another copy is requested by the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch.
2.2 Procedure for starting and ending the transport of goods in the regime of conditional tax exemption between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for starting transport is regulated by the provisions of Section 25, Paragraph 3 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll., Which states, inter alia:
'Before the transport of selected products begins, the operator of the tax warehouse shall inform the customs office which is locally competent for the tax warehouse from which the transport is to commence;
the transport of selected products can only be started with the consent of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the selected products immediately after the condition of securing the tax is met ... '
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of transport only if a tax security is provided in the amount of the tax due on the transported products.
The consignor is obliged to prepare an accompanying document in five copies before the start of the transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document the consent to the commencement of transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copies No 2, 3 and 4 shall be handed over by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorizing the transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the recipient will keep copy No. 2 of the accompanying document in the Slovak Republic. On copies No. 3 and 4, he shall confirm the receipt of the products and submit both copies to the locally competent customs office.
Copy No 3, certified by the customs office, shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which he received the products.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
The transport is terminated by the acceptance of the products by the consignee.
The customs office in the Czech Republic that authorized the commencement of the transport shall decide on the release of the tax security within 5 working days after the submission of copy No. 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Graph No. 2 - Circulation of the accompanying document during transport started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic
Transport from Slovakia
Until 31 December 2005, the procedure for the transport of alcohol and tobacco products from the Slovak Republic to another Member State of the European Union was amended as follows:
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 26, Paragraph 4 of Act No. 105/2004 Coll.
'When transporting alcohol from a tax warehouse in a tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorized consignee or to a tax agent in another Member State, the consignor (supplier) shall send a copy of the first part of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the Poprad Customs Office on the day the transport begins; he shall also send this copy to the customs office in writing within five working days from the date of commencement of the shipment. "
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 22, Paragraph 4 of Act No. 106/2004 Coll.
'When transporting tobacco products from a tax warehouse in a tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorized consignee or tax agent in another Member State, the consignor ’(supplier’) shall send a copy of the first part of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the Poprad Customs Office on the day the transport begins; he shall also send this copy to the customs office in writing no later than five working days from the date of commencement of the shipment. "
When transporting other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) in the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as the “audited period”), the tax entity was not obliged to notify the Poprad Customs Office, resp. the competent customs office of departure under the duty suspension arrangement.
The tax administrator learned about the transport of these products only during a local investigation or tax inspection from the accompanying documents and from the accounting documents of the tax subject.
Before starting the transport, the consignor in the Slovak Republic is obliged to prepare an accompanying document in four copies.
Copy No. 1 shall be kept by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, he shall send a copy of copy No. 1 electronically or by fax to the Poprad Customs Office and the relevant customs office).
Copies No. 2, 3 and 4 accompany the transported goods.
According to the Czech legislation, the recipient in the Czech Republic will keep copy No. 2 of the accompanying document issued by the sender in the Slovak Republic and will confirm the receipt of the products on copies No. 3 and 4.
Confirmed copies No. 3 and 4 shall be sent to the locally competent customs office in the Czech Republic no later than the first working day after the end of the transport.
The customs office shall retain copy No 4 and return copy No 3, on which it shall verify correctness and validity, to the consignee.
The consignee shall send the certified copy No. 3 no later than the next working day after its receipt to the sender to the Slovak Republic.
Transport in the Slovak Republic is considered to be completed on the day of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The sender proves the termination of the transport by submitting copy No. 3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the consignee and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Graph No. 3 - Circulation of the accompanying document during transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in the Slovak Republic and ended in the Czech Republic
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under conditional tax exemption is obliged to send a copy of copy No. 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the locally competent consignor before commencing transport.
The document proving the termination of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products is copy No. 3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the recipient and his relevant tax administrator.
The document proving the termination of the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is copy No. 3 confirmed by the recipient.
The confirmation of the tax administrator of another Member State of the receipt of the said goods by the consignee is required if this administrator is obliged under the legislation of the Member State concerned to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Records of started and terminated transports kept by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic
There is no single electronic system for monitoring the movement of goods under the duty suspension arrangement between the Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on computerising the movement and surveillance of excisable products requires Member States and the European Commission to set up an electronic Excise Movement and Control System from 1 July 2009. ), which would allow excise administrators in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the movement of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently used only in paper form, and will help to facilitate the movement of goods under suspension of excise duty and ensure more effective control of the movement of tax-free products within all Member States.
This system will include the national transport databases of the individual Member States.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic registers all transports started and terminated on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module of Records of Selected Products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of transport carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, the tax administrator may obtain information on the commencement or termination of the transport immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in the EVV.
The customs office shall release the tax security for the transported products provided by the consignor at the moment of registration of the termination of the transport by the customs office to the locally competent consignee.
Customs offices in the Slovak Republic use a database based on the SysNed application software, which ensures the automation of their activities in the administration of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering the tax warehouse, the tax warehouse operator or the authorized recipient in the SysNed application software, this data is automatically transferred to the "System for Exchange of Excise Data" database (hereinafter referred to as "SEED").
3. Preparation and course of cooperation
The first coordination meeting of the SAO-CR representatives and the SAO SR representatives, at which a specific procedure of cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties was discussed, took place in January 2006.
Both parties became acquainted with the legislation in the field of excise duties and with the organization of the administration of excise duties in both countries.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the authorization, respectively. when initiating and terminating the movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty and the exchange of information between the excise administrators of the two countries.
At the meeting, it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak sides: - process overall data on the amount of excise goods transported from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic and vice versa, whose transport began in the audited period, - compare data on mineral oil shipments - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - code of the combined nomenclature 2207 and 2208 in the regime of conditional exemption from tax started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in the months of November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the audited periods were extended to October and November 2005, and in these months the transport of tobacco products under the conditional tax exemption regime was also subject to the inspection.
Tables No. 1 and No. 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty that were transported under the conditional tax exemption regime between Czech and Slovak tax entities in the audited period.
4. Comparison of records of transport of goods in the regime of conditional exemption from tax
The SAO-CR handed over to the Slovak side a database of transports terminated in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items to alcohol and 4 items to tobacco products.
The SAO SR handed over to the Czech side a database of transports terminated in the Slovak Republic, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 696 items related to mineral oil, 2,066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared data on transports listed in the register of started transports in the Czech Republic with data on completed transports registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are shown in Table 3.
Data on transports in November 2004 and September 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which was handed over to it by the SAO SR at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data enabling reliable reconciliation of individual transports, and therefore only 63% of started transports were managed to be assigned.
Individual shipments were assigned according to multiple data, eg shipper, consignee, date of shipment, quantity of transported products.
Data on transports started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Slovak Republic in October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93% of started transports were clearly assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the amount of mineral oils were given in liters or tonnes, depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of alcohol was in most cases given in liters, which could, however, be converted into liters of absolute alcohol on the basis of the percentage alcohol content indicated in the database.
The quantity of tobacco products was stated in pieces, in thousands and in kilograms according to the type of tobacco products.
For transports started in the Czech Republic, the completion of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or for which the data on the transported quantity of products did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
Accompanying documents for 487 shipments of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were inspected.
The inspection of these documents was carried out at the customs offices at which the SAO-CR performed the inspection.
For transport authorized by other customs offices, the accompanying documents were requested through the GDC.
The Czech side requested the Slovak side to verify the implementation of 141 shipments for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide certified copies No. 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products stated on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products listed in the database.
Furthermore, the Slovak side was provided with data on transports registered in the Slovak database, which, however, did not contain the transport database of the Czech customs administration.
The SAO SR searched for 95 transports in the database of the Slovak Customs Administration.
The verification of the remaining 46 shipments was requested by the locally competent customs offices, which proved their completion with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side copies of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which the transports were also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of transports performed by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of started transports.
The inspection of these cases revealed:
- in the Slovak transport database, 11 transports of alcohol in the total amount of 276.7 liters of alcohol realized by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 transports of alcohol in the total amount of 404.66 liters of alcohol realized in 2005 were registered.
The SAO-CR found that these were transports of taxed products for the initiation of which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The sender informed the tax administrator in writing about the start of the transport. He carried out the transport on the basis of accompanying documents, which are used for the transport of products under the conditional tax exemption regime;
- in the Slovak transport database, a total of 94 transports of mineral oils were registered, combined nomenclature code 2710 11 21, in the total volume of 173 thous. liters realized by the Czech tax entity in the period from September 2004 to December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that in the period from May 2004 to June 2005, the tax subject carried out a transport of 102 thous. liters of untaxed mineral oils without proper authorization.
The taxable person held a special permit for the receipt and use of exempt products, on the basis of which he could supply non-taxed products only to the holder of the same permit.
He did not notify the customs office in the Czech Republic of the commencement of transport and did not provide tax security in the amount of CZK 1,207,680 for the transported products.
In the period from July 2005 to December 2005, the tax subject transported 71 thous. liters of taxed mineral oils. Even in these cases, he failed to fulfill his legal obligation by notifying the customs office of the commencement of transport.
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of products released for free circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to notify the customs office of this fact in writing before commencing transport.
A taxable person taking products released for free circulation in another Member State is obliged to declare the quantity and secure the tax before taking it.
Products may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the details of which are regulated by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also allows the use of an accompanying document for transport under a duty suspension arrangement, which must, however, clearly indicate that it is a "simplified accompanying document for tax control purposes (products subject to excise duty)".
The same legal regulation of transport and acceptance of products released for free tax circulation in another Member State also applies in the Slovak Republic.
In the above cases, the tax subjects transported the products released for free tax circulation with an accompanying document for transport in the regime of conditional exemption from tax, the 3rd and 4th copies of which the recipient submitted to the tax administrator in the Slovak Republic for verification.
The customs authorities in the Slovak Republic registered these transports in the database of transports in the regime of conditional exemption from tax, as it was not stated on the accompanying documents that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the transport database of the Czech customs administration with the transport database of the Slovak customs administration and found out:
- in the databases, the quantity of transported products was stated inconsistently, eg mineral oil was stated in liters, hectoliters or kilograms; the alcohol was expressed in liters or liters of alcohol, making it difficult to compare the quantities of goods transported,
- the quantity of alcohol transported indicated on the invoices did not correspond to the quantity recorded in the databases,
- the databases did not list all the related invoices,
- in the database of the Slovak customs administration, two shipments of alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic were registered in November 2004 in the total volume of 47,237 liters of alcohol, which were not in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak side submitted copies of accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Until 30 June 2005, the conditions for cooperation between the administrations of the Member States responsible for administering excise duties were governed by Council Directive 77/799 / EEC on mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxes on insurance premiums.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004 entered into force, which lays down rules and procedures enabling the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office to liaise with the other Member States in the field of excise administration and to be responsible for exchanging information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as the "ELO CR") was established at the GDC to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union.
With effect from 1 May 2004, the ELO Office at the Poprad Customs Office provided tasks related to the administration of systems for controlling the movement of excisable goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information within mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the Slovak Republic.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of the ELO Office are performed by the ELO Department (based in Poprad) of the Excise Tax Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "ELO SR").
Pursuant to Article 3 (3) of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible in particular for: - the exchange of data held in the SEED electronic register, - the 'Early Warning System Excise' (EWSE), - requests for verification movement of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the "Movement Verification System" (hereinafter referred to as "MSS").
The content, scope and functions of the SEED, EWSE and MVS systems are regulated in Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for the exchange of information on taxable persons trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national registers of excise duty payers and allows tax administrations in the European Union to find out whether products subject to excise duty are traded by an authorized person.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information held in this database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No. 98/2004 Coll., With Section 39 of Act No. 104/2004 Coll., With Section 46 of Act No. 105/2004 Coll., With Section 40 of Act No. 106/2004 Coll., Section 39 of Act No. 107/2004 Coll., ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of operators of tax warehouses, authorized recipients and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in the Slovak Republic contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, a tax warehouse operator or an authorized consignee in the SysNed application software, which is automatically connected to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, authorized beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data is automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Customs Administration of the SR and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the audited period usually once a month, exceptionally several times a month.
The Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
The data are transferred to the SEED database in the Czech Republic from the national register, in which all persons authorized to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorizations to dispose of these products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs offices for the provision of information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through the ELO CR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excisable goods, through which the transport of risky consignments is notified.
The transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by a regulation of the European Commission and the transport assessed as risky by the tax administrator are considered risky consignments.
The exchange of information is realized in two forms:
- information - sent when the set limits are exceeded,
- warning message - sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When evaluating the degree of risk of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database to send a warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data stated in the accompanying document.
In the event that the data in the SEED database do not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee does not match or the consignee's registered office), ELO SR will prepare a warning message to send to the ELO.
When drawing up the reports, ELO follows the regulations of the Commission for Taxation and Customs, CED 317 and CED 457, which determine, inter alia, the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measurement for drawing up information and warning reports.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent one warning message to ELO CR.
In the Czech Republic, information on started shipments of products in quantities exceeding the set limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving the shipment.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates the consignment as risky on the basis of its own analysis, it will prepare a so-called warning message, which it will send to the relevant Member State via the ELO CR.
In 2005, ELO CR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
MVS - the system of control of the movement of goods - enables, through MVS applications, to control individual shipments of products subject to excise duty as well as control of the determined route of transport between the entities listed in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information takes place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is used mainly in cases where the sender receives a certified copy No. 3 of the accompanying document and requests, for example, a refund of excise duty, and in cases where the data contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the audited period, ELO SR sent 33 requests to the ELO CR.
ELO CR sent ELO SR 25 MVS applications.
The customs offices in the Czech Republic most often checked the data stated in the accompanying documents, especially the amount received, resp. of the products dispatched or whether the consignor of the products listed in the accompanying document is authorized to handle the excise goods, if this could not be verified in the international SEED database.
In both countries, the applications received by the RAC were forwarded to the customs offices locally responsible for the consignee or consignor of the excise goods.
The customs authorities checked the required data and communicated the result of the investigation to the other Member State via ELO.
6. Summary
The cooperation between the SAO-CR and the SAO SR made it possible to compare the basic legal regulations governing excise duties in both countries, the procedure of the Czech and Slovak customs authorities to start and stop the transport of products under conditional tax exemption between the two countries, records of these transports and between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 A comparison of legal regulations governing the area of ​​excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic revealed differences:
(a) in the procedure of taxable persons and tax administrations when initiating the transport of products under a duty suspension arrangement.
The tax subject in the Czech Republic may start the transport of products under the conditional tax exemption regime only with the consent of the tax administrator, who will allow the start of transport provided that the transported products have been provided with a tax security in the amount of tax due to them.
The commencement of the transport of products under the conditional tax exemption regime in the Slovak Republic is not subject to the permission of the tax administrator.
During the audited period, the tax entity was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the commencement of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
He could start transporting mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax administrator.
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under conditional tax exemption is obliged to send a copy of copy No. 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office locally competent for the consignor;
(b) within the time limits for sending copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The consignee in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy No. 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification no later than the next working day after the end of the transport.
He is obliged to send the certified copy No. 3 to the sender no later than the next working day after receiving it from the tax administrator.
The consignee in the Slovak Republic is obliged to send the sender of the products a copy No. 3 confirmed by the tax administrator and the consignee of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of transports of products in the regime of conditional tax exemption.
The content and manner of keeping these records is not regulated by law in the Czech Republic or in the Slovak Republic.
The customs authorities in both countries enter in the register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
There is currently no single electronic system for monitoring the movement of goods under suspension of excise duty between the Member States of the European Union, which would allow excise administrators in the individual Member States to obtain information on the movement of goods in real time.
Decision 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 provides for the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excisable products from 1 July 2009.
Based on the agreement on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of transports of products under the conditional tax exemption regime initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5,876 items related to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side handed over to the Czech side a database of transports of products under the conditional tax exemption regime initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3,319 items related to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on transports listed in the register of started transports in the Czech Republic with the records of transports completed in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared data on transports of goods under the conditional tax exemption regime initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of data was complicated by the fact that the quantity of transported goods was not stated uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to unambiguously assign data on individual transports in both records, the accompanying documents were checked and breaches of the conditional tax exemption regime were not detected, nor were cases of tax evasion detected.
Based on the findings of parallel controls, it can be stated that Member States can obtain valuable information from transport records to improve excise administration.
The establishment of an electronic system for the movement and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003 / EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movement under suspension of excise duty within the European Union.
Communique
This report has been prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the Chairman of the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic.
Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the ex - post control
Foreword
Taxes are generally a key source of public revenue.
It is therefore self-evident that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus on this area.
An example is value added tax (VAT) fraud.
In their case, an annual loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated in the European Union (EU).
Already in 2005, the participants of VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very good area for control cooperation, as it is the only tax harmonized within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also "SAO") and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, hereinafter also "BRH") carried out the first parallel VAT audit in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not limited to a single country but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to address this issue.
The two SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a subsequent parallel inspection.
1. Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of inspection: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up inspection)
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the audit was to examine the procedure of financial authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for resolving selected cases of business transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany ("Germany"), and to examine the procedures of tax administrations of both countries in international cooperation .
(D) The audit was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and the BRH.
The intention was also to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended for comparison with identified best practice (if any).
The audited period was the years 2006 to 2008, in the case of factual connections also the period preceding and following, until the end of the audit.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The subsequent audit of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
During previous parallel inspections, suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were detected.
Some of them required further verification.
Based on the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations regarding VAT administration.
The follow-up action was carried out to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspicious cases.
The audit also focused, for example, on selected cases of high-risk intra-Community transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of receivables and the implementation of VAT audits of large tax entities.
During the audit of VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors came to the following audit findings:
1. Recommendations from the previous inspection
• Recommendation 1: The conditions for registration of payers should be harmonized across the EU
In previous parallel audits, a comparison of VAT registration systems in the two countries revealed differences.
Due to the different problems of different registration methods, both SAIs recommended harmonizing the conditions for payer registration within the EU.
This recommendation has been made at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for an extension existing databases within the EU, including a database of VAT identification numbers.
It also amended the common standards for the registration and registration of taxpayers.
The SAIs expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as soon as possible.
However, the latest version of this document, agreed by EU Member States in the framework of ECOFIN, no longer addresses this issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of ​​common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to consider this intention to be a relevant prevention tool in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly submission of summary reports
As part of international cooperation, the previous audit recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements, thus enabling a more timely verification of the values ​​of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117 / EC amending Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions shortens the period for which recapitulative statements are lodged EU, for one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit summary reports on a monthly basis was not introduced within the set deadline in accordance with the applicable EU regulations, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany in order to increase the reliability of VIES data and consider the interconnection of the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to examine possible solutions.
The work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level Based on the results of a previous audit, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of fraud will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit found that our two Member States use different risk management systems, which have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO inspected the EUROCANET system, which enables the exchange of information within the EU, while the BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Subsequent control of selected cases of intra-community transactions
During the previous audit, business transactions were examined jointly, where there were doubts about their execution or irregularities in the reporting of business transactions in tax returns or summary reports to taxpayers from both countries.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for follow-up, which involved the intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The inspections carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned were not closed on the date of completion of our previous joint inspection.
The follow-up audit verified that most tax proceedings in connection with the selected cases of commercial transactions between taxpayers from the Czech Republic and Germany were closed and that adequate measures were taken by the Czech or German tax authorities (eg additional VAT additional assessments or avoidance of input tax refunds). ).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-Community transactions executed by EU payers, which were included in the EUROCANET system, were selected for control.
The EUROCANET system is a tool for detecting risky taxpayers within the EU.
Member States' participation in this system is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in the EUROCANET system, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant in a system if some Member States refuse active participation.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not participate in the data exchange in the EUROCANET system, it was not possible to obtain any information on which suppliers with a German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
As part of the audit, the SAO identified both cases of ordinary business transactions and cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities to control risky transactions, especially with regard to so-called missing traders, while the mere physical examination of documents can hardly prove to the tax subject any fraudulent conduct.
A similar situation for tax administrations arises when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel shops.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation and also to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively participate in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools are used to detect risky taxpayers, which have so far proved their worth to the German tax administration.
There is a need to communicate and exchange experiences between EU Member States in this area.
The EU Council reached a political agreement on a draft regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far with the use of EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new network to combat VAT fraud.
4. Mutual assistance in the recovery of claims
In the field of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling requests for international assistance in debt recovery in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and the BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs find it useful to renegotiate statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent discrepancies.
Without it, statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAIs agree that reliable statistics should include more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to carry out an analysis on the basis of more detailed statistics to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with a low recovery success rate to increase their debt recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
5. Control of large tax subjects
The SAIs analyzed the legal situation regarding VAT control for large tax entities (hereinafter also "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they collected information from tax administrations in the form of a questionnaire on areas that the SAIs consider essential for the management of this issue.
It is clear from the responses received that the situation in the two countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system in place to guide the selection of risk-prone cases, which is based on a large amount of relevant data (eg information from tax audits, data from balance sheets and profit and loss statements, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to establish a specialized financial office for the administration of VDS.
A similar system does not yet exist in Germany, which makes it difficult to manage and analyze VAT control in general.
So far, Germany has focused more on the selection of the individual cases in question, in particular on the basis of data from the VAT return and the recapitulative statement.
The analysis of these data is based on the various components of risk management that will be strengthened.
3. The course of the control action
3.1 The course of the control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out in the period from May 2009 to February 2010 by Department II. - the state budget revenue department and the territorial departments IX. Pilsen, X. Ceske Budejovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The auditees were: the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also referred to as the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter also referred to as the "FI"): the Brno II, the Brno III, the Brno IV, the Břeclav, the Domažlice, the in Hodonín, FI in Hradec Králové, FI in Cheb, FI in Jablonec nad Nisou, FI in Karlovy Vary, FI in Kralupy nad Vltavou, FI in Kraslice, FI Ostrava I, FI Ostrava III, FI in Písek, FI in Pilsen, FI for Prague 1, FI for Prague 4, FI for Prague 8, FI in Rakovník, FI in Sokolov, FI in Tábor, FI in Vysoké Mýto, FI in Zlín and FI in Žamberk.
The audit conclusion from this audit was approved by the Board of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 The course of the inspection in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the indirect tax audit service and the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
After selecting a sample of cases, a number of Länder were informed of the mission of the inspection.
In addition to interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, inspections took place in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hesse, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
