The tax files of the following tax offices were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Tax Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, negotiations took place with the tax authorities of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-South) and with the financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two control institutions
As part of the preparation of parallel inspections, a meeting of representatives of both inspection institutions took place in September 2008 to discuss and determine inspection topics.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the top officials of the two SAIs signed an agreement on cooperation in carrying out parallel inspections.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the audit teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the audit, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2-4 December 2009.
The inspection teams exchanged the findings collected so far and agreed on a timetable for drawing up a joint report.
In carrying out parallel audits, both SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report, • examination of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between Czech and German taxpayers that were not resolved during the previous parallel audit; transactions between taxpayers from the Czech Republic and Germany, which were classified as high-risk cases, • control of the procedure of tax administrations in the field of international assistance in the recovery of VAT receivables, • tax control of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel inspections was prepared during a working meeting in June 2010.
4. Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from the previous inspection
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
The conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonized within the EU
Based on the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended an adjustment of the conditions for VAT registration and the introduction of a new rule for the cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
The revised conditions should make it possible to reduce more effectively the risk of possible tax evasion in the collection of VAT.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not use the right to cancel VAT registration for taxpayers who did not fulfill their obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., On Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as the “VAT Act”).
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed a change in the provision consisting in the introduction of the obligation of tax administrators to cancel VAT registration for taxpayers in the event of repeated failure to file a VAT return.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator may cancel the registration of a taxpayer “ex offo” in cases where: a) the taxpayer has not performed without notification of the reason to the tax administrator for twelve consecutive months of performance, b) the taxpayer fails to fulfill his obligations under this Act; ) the taxpayer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous audit, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the FI for Prague 1 to cancel VAT registration as of 31 January of the following calendar year for so-called non-established payers who did not incur any obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The FI for Prague 1 often did not cancel the VAT registration for these payers, as the relevant provision set an insufficient deadline for canceling the registration.
This problem was eliminated by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a non-established taxpayer if the taxpayer did not supply any taxable goods or services or exempt goods or services with the right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
As part of international cooperation, the previous audit recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for submitting recapitulative statements.
The Council Directive reduces the period for which recapitulative statements are submitted for intra-EU transactions to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
The obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form is also newly established.
The recapitulative statement must be submitted by the taxable person even if the services for which the place of supply is determined pursuant to Section 9 (1) of the VAT Act are provided to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State and obliged to declare and pay the tax to their recipient.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8 / EC amending Directive 2006/112 / EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in order to increase the reliability of VIES data This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration compares data on intra-Community transactions reported in VAT tax returns and summary reports of Czech taxpayers automatically in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the necessary preconditions for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore one of the priority areas and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, among other things, by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator tried to determine the difference between eligible and actually collected VAT in 25 EU Member States ("EU-25") during the period 2000-2006. .
Based on an analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concludes that the estimated amount of uncollected VAT loss for this period is € 90-113 billion, with an average of 12% of eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was estimated at as much as 18%.
In the framework of international cooperation, it was stated in a previous audit that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one Member State.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO audited the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-Community transactions carried out by EU taxpayers included in the EUROCANET system were selected for control (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved by setting up the EUROFISC network, which should improve cooperation between the responsible authorities so that fraud can be detected at an early stage.
This network should later also become an important source of information in assessing the risks of intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council already approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 October 200812 and set out the basic principles that will guide the network.
EUROFISC is modeled on the already functioning EUROCANET rapid and selective information exchange system, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky business transactions and entities involved in organized VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations from the first report revealed the following findings:
Recommendation 1
The conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonized within the EU
The German tax administration has set up a well-functioning taxpayer registration system based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance drew the Commission's attention to this system in October 2007.
System improvements are performed continuously.
At present, the data from the questionnaire are processed electronically and will subsequently be used for research as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and elaboration of this issue.
The BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure the already achieved level of standards in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
On 8 April 2010, a law was adopted to transpose EU directives into national law.
This law contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of summary reports on intra-Community supplies.
These provisions entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in order to increase the reliability of VIES data and consider the interconnection of the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
A joint working group was set up consisting of staff from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance.
The Group has developed a strategy for automatically comparing data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the working group discussed a tool designed to optimize the control process for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is participating in this exchange within the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of ​​this platform and, following a written consultation of 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 action plan.
The members of the platform are further divided into subgroups that deal with individual topics, such as: • risk management tools, • influencing actions, • evaluation, • updating the risk management guide.
At the beginning of 2010, reports on the results of the activities of these subgroups were published.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and the cancellation of this registration in various countries has been addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the database of VAT identification numbers.
It also amended common minimum standards for the registration and registration of taxpayers.
The issue of registration and cancellation of registration has so far been left to the national legislation of the EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and elaboration of this issue.
The BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany did not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political agreement on the above-mentioned proposal for a Regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States have to implement national procedures and are only obliged to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee about these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has failed to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element in preventing VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts by the Commission in this direction.
Monthly submission of summary reports
As part of international cooperation, the previous audit recommended that all EU countries introduce a one-month deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements, allowing for earlier verification of the values ​​of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117 / EC amending Directive 2006/112 / EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions shortens the period for which recapitulative statements are lodged EU, for one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced the obligation to submit summary reports on a monthly basis according to a set calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in line with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany in order to increase the reliability of VIES data and consider the interconnection of the two VAT return and recapitulative statements systems
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
The work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO inspected the EUROCANET system used for the exchange of information in the EU (see Chapter 4.3).
In this area, BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected cases of intra-Community transactions
In the previous audit, the implementation of business transactions was jointly examined, in which there were doubts about their implementation, resp. inconsistencies in the way taxpayers from both countries reported these business transactions in their VAT returns, resp. summary reports.
Both audit institutions selected nine cases for ex-post control involving the intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, the audit carried out by the tax administrations of both countries was not completed during the previous joint audit.
1)
In the first quarter of 2005, the Czech payer purchased goods worth EUR 22,686 from a German payer.
This acquisition of goods was not acknowledged by the Czech taxpayer in his VAT return, as the German taxpayer was not assigned a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that under the German VAT law a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order to exempt intra-Community supplies. from VAT.
A subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that, based on an inspection carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech taxpayer filed an additional VAT return, in which he declared the acquisition of goods in the stated value and also claimed the same amount of VAT deduction in this tax return.
2)
In the 4th quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase goods worth EUR 12,561 from the German payer.
The Czech taxpayer denied the acquisition of these goods and did not state them in his VAT return.
The German tax authorities refused to cooperate on request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, as the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence, he terminated the inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed in the original amount.
Following the SAO's inspection, it found that the Czech tax administrator had received two spontaneous information from Germany pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German taxpayer had invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech taxpayer acquired the goods from the Slovak taxpayer and stated this acquisition in the regular VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
In the 4th quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase a car worth EUR 48,500 from the German payer.
The Czech taxpayer did not admit the acquisition of the goods in question.
This taxpayer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, so the tax administrator assessed VAT of CZK 0 for the quarter.
On the basis of information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax administrator invited the taxpayer to file an additional VAT return, which the taxpayer did not.
A subsequent inspection revealed that the tax administrator had performed further acts in the tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the Czech payer sold the car in question to a second-hand car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment order for the tax period of December 2004, by which he additionally assessed VAT for the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295,379.
By a resolution of the regional court, the Czech payer was abolished with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of foreclosures of the taxable debtor's eligible assets, this arrears appear to be irrecoverable.
4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005 in the total amount of EUR 198,167.
The reply to the request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that there were pending tax criminal proceedings against the German entity in Germany.
During the follow-up inspection, the BRH was informed that after the end of the tax proceedings in Germany, it was demonstrably established that the German taxpayer had been involved in fraudulent activities.
The intra-Community acquisition of goods was taxed at EUR 182 424 (2004) and EUR 369 690 (2005).
The SAO's follow-up inspection found that the Czech payer was involved in carousel transactions with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the verification of the supply of goods, a VAT audit was initiated at the Czech tax entity for the tax periods of April, May and June 2005.
Based on audit findings and information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT in the amount of CZK 703,031 for the period of May 2005 and CZK 726,551 for the period of June 2005.
5)
In February 2005, the Czech payer A was to purchase a machine from the German payer with a total value of EUR 58,000.
This German payer was to deliver a machine worth EUR 88,027 to the Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004, but payer B denied the acquisition of the goods.
A subsequent inspection by the SAO revealed that payer B had purchased the machine from a German company which had an organizational unit in the Czech Republic.
The Czech taxpayer A did not report the acquisition of goods from the German taxpayer in his VAT return.
The reply from the German tax administrator to the request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German taxpayer did not make an intra-Community supply of machinery worth EUR 58 000, but a supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
Following a follow-up inspection, the BRH found that, following a tax audit, the intra-Community supply of the machine had been reclassified as a domestic supply of the machine and the VAT exemption had been abolished.
6)
In the third quarter of 2004, the German taxpayer was to supply the Czech taxpayer with goods worth EUR 11,600.
The goods were bought and subsequently sold in 2005 in Germany.
Following the SAO's audit, it found that the Czech tax administrator had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, which wrongly stated the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods in the stated value.
The BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administrator corrected the German taxpayer's VAT return and additionally assessed VAT of EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany is subject to tax control.
The recapitulative statement of a German payer has not yet been corrected, as corrections to recapitulative statements in Germany can only be made by the payer who submitted the recapitulative statement.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No. 1798/2003 as to whether a Czech taxpayer purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47,400 from a German taxpayer in February 2005.
Following the tax proceedings for the tax period of February 2005, the Czech tax administrator imposed a tax liability of CZK 0 on the Czech taxpayer and informed the German tax administrator that he could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
A subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was canceled in 2007 due to non-fulfillment of obligations and the Czech tax administrator sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
Following the inspection, the BRH found that the German taxpayer had changed his registered office and the new locally competent tax administrator had revoked the VAT exemption for the supply of the car in question to the Czech taxpayer on the basis of the inspection.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the data in the recapitulative statement and has lodged an appeal against the decision of the tax administrator.
8)
According to data from the VIES system, the German taxpayer supplied goods to the Czech taxpayer in the period from the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005 with goods with a total value of EUR 33,205.
Following the SAO's inspection, it was found that the Czech tax administrator tried to find out the causes of the differences that arose with the Czech taxpayer in the acquisition of goods in the period from the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech taxpayer repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not explain the difference in the value of acquired goods in the amount of CZK 134,273 for the period from Q3 2004 to Q1 2005, because according to the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture business transactions for individual quarters, and therefore the tax administrator accepted the additional tax confession.
9)
In the third quarter of 2004, the German taxpayer supplied goods to the Czech taxpayer in the amount of EUR 46,854.
For the same period, the Czech payer declared an intra-Community acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14,856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of the performed supplies within the international exchange of information according to Council Regulation (EC) No. 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the supply of goods of EUR 31,998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech taxpayer in the VAT return and the data in VIES.
A subsequent audit by the SAO revealed that the Czech taxpayer had submitted an additional tax return for VAT for the tax period July 2004 to January 2007, after many urgencies.
In this tax return, the taxpayer also claimed the right to deduct VAT, which left the tax liability for the said tax period unchanged.
The follow-up audit verified that in selected cases of business transactions between taxpayers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most tax proceedings were completed and that tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Germany took adequate measures (ie additionally assessed VAT or prevented input tax refunds).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the inspection in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for the detection of risk entities within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from the EUROCANET system was compared with the relevant local tax authorities with the data on the acquirers.
Starting in the first quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic sends data on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers to the EUROCANET system.
Within the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for inspection.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States were recorded in EUROCANET.
As the German tax administration did not participate in the EUROCANET data exchange, no information could be obtained to help determine whether suppliers with a German VAT ID were assessed by the German tax administration as risky entities.
The audit revealed cases of ordinary business transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Where appropriate, tax administrations benefited from the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax authorities did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions during the verification of signal information.
The tax authorities continuously monitor such tax entities due to their inclusion in the EUROCANET system.
• During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show any deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax and VAT base in the submitted accounts, although they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed business relationships with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• The verification of business transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with the tax authorities and could not be contacted.
The locally competent tax authorities mostly examined risky tax entities and risky transactions listed in the signal information from the EUROCANET system.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities when examining risky transactions, especially in connection with the examination of so-called missing traders, and it is difficult to prove fraudulent conduct to the tax subject only from the physical control of documents.
Stricter VAT registration requirements and more flexible cancellation of registrations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of taxable persons involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered for the purpose of reporting fictitious supplies of goods within the EU or for the purpose of issuing formally correct tax documents to taxpayers who unduly draw input VAT deductions.
In cases where the involvement of taxable persons in carousel transactions and other fraud is suspected and goods are imported and exported from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation, as well as to monitor the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the final consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in the operation of EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of the system, which should be eliminated by setting up a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the inspection in Germany
The BRH analyzed the information available from the Federal Central Tax Office, which contained data from the EUROCANET system.
These data were the criteria for selecting six files of German taxpayers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to actively participate in the EUROCANET system.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but is only the recipient of EUROCANET data.
The rationale for this position is contained in the following statement: .in the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
At present, there is no legal basis for breaching the applicable rules on the confidentiality of tax information.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such data is used by other Member States within EUROCANET. '
The German tax authorities receive control information on the direct business relations of the payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in the EUROCANET system.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relations with traders from other Member States who also maintain business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in the EUROCANET system, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse active participation.
As a result, the inspection in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal large differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools for detecting fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to create a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The EU Council reached a political agreement on a draft regulation, the main benefit of which is the establishment of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained in using EUROCANET data should be part of the envisaged anti-VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experience at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought before national and European courts show that a discussion between the Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions appears to be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
4.4.1 International assistance in debt collection in the Czech Republic
The basic regulations of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU are in particular the following directives:
• Council Directive 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to operations forming part of the system of financing by the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44 / EC amending Directive 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to operations forming part of the system of financing by the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, taxes value added and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94 / EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308 / EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive No. 76/308 / EEC was implemented by Act No. 252/2000 Coll., On International Assistance in the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive No. 2001/44 / EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal system and at the same time amend the said Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., On international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims, was adopted.
The new regulation in the system of regulation of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is Commission Regulation (EC) No. 1179/2008 of 28 November 2008.
The annex to the regulation sets out new models of applications, which have been in use since 1 January 2009, and newly stipulates the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the requesting authority to confirm the conformity of the sent documents with the original document.
The main principles for providing international cooperation in debt collection:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always provided only on the basis of an application containing the prescribed requirements;
3. the assistance does not cover financial claims which are of the nature of a criminal sanction in the requested State;
4. the provision of international debt recovery assistance shall be in accordance with the national law of the requested State;
5. foreign claims do not take precedence in recovery;
6. assistance is provided only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. Principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has made no successful use of all available possibilities to recover the claim provided for by its legal system).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. it defines three forms in which assistance is provided, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
The locally competent tax office will electronically send a request for information, a request for delivery or a request for recovery of receivables together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance via the Finance Directorate.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will ensure the translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it including the annexes and send it to the competent tax administration authority of the designated state via the CCN / CSI network.
There are two basic requirements for recovery: the claim must be higher than EUR 1 500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If these requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse recovery.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Upon receipt of an application from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must acknowledge receipt of the application as soon as possible, and no later than within seven days.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for rejecting the request and state the specific provisions of the Directive which it invokes.
This notification must be sent no later than three months from the date of acknowledgment of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application has all the requisites in accordance with the law, and should immediately forward the application through the Financial Directorate to the locally competent tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator ascertains, among other things, the debtor's property, eg by obtaining extracts from the real estate cadastre, ascertaining bank accounts, verifying the registration of vehicles at the traffic inspectorate, etc.
After six months from the date of acknowledgment of receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance should communicate to the requesting authority the result of the inquiry carried out in order to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where it is not possible to enforce the claim, the requesting authority should also be informed.
Each amount recovered by the tax administrator shall be transferred to the requesting authority in CZK within one month from the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that the Czech tax administrator recovering foreign receivables may allow delay in its payment or payment in installments, if the state that requested recovery agrees.
During the recovery period, the debtor is prescribed interest or a penalty pursuant to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., On the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty belongs to the state that requested the recovery.
In the case of received recovery requests, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not forward the requests to the locally competent tax administrators for processing in time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the framework of international assistance in the recovery of receivables in the case of applications received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance had not complied with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., As it had not notified the locally competent authority of the Member State of the progress of recovery within six months from the date of receipt of the request.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistical data
The Czech Ministry of Finance in accordance with the provisions of Section 13, Paragraph 4 of Act No. 191/2004 Coll. processes, by 15 March each year, statistics for the European Commission indicating the number of requests for information, service or recovery sent or received in the previous year, indicating the amount of claims to which the requests relate.
The European Commission prepares a report on the state of debt recovery, which it submits to the EU Council and the European Parliament, on the basis of documents provided by all EU Member States.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data due to an error in the item of recovered receivables in 2008 by 5,250 thousand. EUR, by stating the incorrect value of the recovered VAT receivable (it was a shift of the decimal point after the conversion of the receivable from Czech crowns to the value in euros).
This error was subsequently reflected in the European Commission's statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including recoveries, is provided in the table below.
4.4.2 International debt recovery assistance in Germany
The legal authorization for international administrative assistance in tax matters is derived from European Community law, Council Directive 2008/55 / ​​EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Recovery Directive) and the Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (Implementing Directive ES).
In the interests of more accessible wording and clarity, the EC Debt Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76/308 / EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Debt Recovery Directive was transposed into German national law by the State Tax Collection Act (EC) of 3 May 2003.
The recovery procedure in Germany is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code emphasizes that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities in force under national jurisdiction and on the basis of the EC Law on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) lays down statutory provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
The administrative acts of the tax authorities are governed in particular by the instructions for execution and the instructions for enforcement.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with the representatives of the Länder on the principles of administrative assistance in the assessment of taxes and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general preconditions for submitting applications for recovery are the following:
• Legal requirements must be met (§ 251 and § 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of recovery have already been exhausted.
• Receivables that are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
• No more than 5 years may elapse between the issuance of the recovery order or the date on which the claim becomes final (ie it is no longer the subject of an appeal) until the date of submission of applications.
• The total amount of the claim must be higher than EUR 1,500.
Procedure for sending recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the tax authorities' executive departments to the relevant foreign authority, such as the Czech CLO, through the intermediate office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The follow-up procedure is governed by the Guidelines on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Debt Collection) of 19 January 2004.25 A working group of the Federal Government and the Provincial Governments is currently reviewing this guideline to bring it into line with the Debt Recovery Directive.
The application, including annexes, is submitted by the tax office electronically to the intermediate office.
This office will check the correctness of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it is returned to the relevant tax office.
If it meets all the requirements, it is handed over to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office will then ensure the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and will also ensure the translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving recovery requests from other EU Member States
Requests for recovery received from other Member States are registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and within 10 days they send an acknowledgment of receipt.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check whether the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these requests to the intermediate office, which then forwards them to the relevant tax authorities and monitors their settlement.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the application takes longer than 6 months, the Intermediate Office will invite you to submit a preliminary report, which must be submitted in accordance with Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94 / DG.
After checking the formal and factual details of the application, the implementing services will notify the method of recovery.
All amounts recovered must be transferred to the bank account specified in the application within one month of receipt.
Statistical data
Information on mutual assistance in the recovery of receivables between Germany and the Czech Republic in the years 2006-2008 (as of 31 December 2008) is contained in the following table.
4.4.3 Debt collection control, case studies
Within the framework of international cooperation, 21 applications for international assistance in the recovery of receivables between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for inspection.
Examination of ten selected cases revealed, among other things:
1.
On 20 October 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany to recover a VAT claim for 2004 and 2005 in the total amount of EUR 3,883, ie CZK 109,820, from a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax administrator until 26 February 2008.
In order to secure the recovered receivable, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
As it was not possible to settle the entire recovered receivable even by mortgaging the real estate, an installment calendar was agreed with the Czech tax entity with installments in the amount of min. 2,000 CZK per month.
On 31 August 2009, information on the status of recovery of the receivable was sent to the German tax administration, stating that as of 25 August 2009, this receivable had been partially recovered in installments in the amount of CZK 49,600.
This amount was sent to Germany and on 28 August 2009 another installment of CZK 3,000 was sent to Germany.
2.
On 7 January 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 180,869 in Germany, ie CZK 4,434,915, for VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the tax administrator until 27 November 2008.
By examining the ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movables, the tax administrator found that the debtor did not own any enforceable assets.
Furthermore, a local investigation revealed that the debtor did not stay at the address of permanent residence for almost a year.
His place of residence in the Czech Republic is unknown.
This notification was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 April 2009 and on 16 April 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
On 21 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for recovery of tax arrears on sales tax and accessories of a Czech tax entity in the amount of EUR 3,139, ie CZK 84,846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this receivable to the tax administrator on 6 August 2008, although on 18 February 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the receivable in Germany.
On 9 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax administrator that the request for recovery was settled by the payment of a receivable by a Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the receivable in question was also paid as part of recovery in the Czech Republic and transferred to Germany on 27 October 2008.
Due to the long time limits in which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorized tax administrator, in this case the receivable was paid twice - by the entity itself in Germany and the recovery of the receivable by the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with the BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been included in the claim from another recovery request in the amount of EUR 6,649, which was to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance registers with this company only a request for recovery of a claim in the amount of EUR 3,139, a request for recovery of a claim in the amount of EUR 6,649 does not appear in the records of the Czech Ministry of Finance with the company in question.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany to recover tax arrears from a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 39,957, ie CZK 956,654, to income tax and VAT and accessories in Germany.
On 19 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
On 1 June 2009, the debt collection procedure was initiated, and execution was ordered to order a receivable on accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and to deduct it from wages (the deduction was CZK 7,000).
During the meeting with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the receivable and considered it disputed.
The Czech tax administrator found that in the past the tax entity was willing to repay EUR 250 per month, which was not accepted by the German tax administrator.
The taxpayer promised to discuss the application with the German tax administrator in order to obtain a change in the amount of his claim.
Recovery of the receivable continued during the SAO's audit.
5.
On 19 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning a Czech tax entity which owed a total of EUR 113,444 in income tax for 2005 and turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories, ie 3 116,304 CZK.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request to the FI for Prague 1, which is responsible for tax administration for non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14 November 2008, as it was not possible to determine the locally competent tax administrator on the basis of the tax address.
During the investigation, the FI obtained information that the debtor had an income of EUR 4,704 on 19 September 2008; however, the FI could no longer issue an execution order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance submitted the request for recovery of the claim only after this date.
On 26 January 2009, the Czech tax administrator commenced recovery of the claim and issued an execution order to order a claim on the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit unions.
Recovery of the receivable continued during the SAO's audit.
6.
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in the recovery of a VAT claim and costs in the total amount of CZK 146,223,742 on 3 October 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax administration until 13 May 2008.
On 8 September 2008, the German tax administrator transferred to the Czech authorities, through the Federal Bank, the amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account in the amount of EUR 17,700, ie CZK 439,226.
During the verification of the volume of recovered receivables, an error was found in the recalculation of the amount recovered.
The amount recovered 146,223,742 CZK was converted at the rate of 1 EUR = 25,065 CZK incorrectly to 583,378 EUR.
The correct conversion of the amount recovered is EUR 5 833 781.83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech Tax Administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover a tax arrears from a Czech tax entity that owed CZK 1,970,632, ie EUR 79,847, for VAT and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax administration until 10 November 2008.
On 4 February 2009, the German tax administrator called on the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant declines in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and especially in the first half of 2009 and the associated liquidation situation, the following payments were made to cover arrears: on 4 April 2009 the amount of EUR 4,600, on 6 May 2009 2009 an amount of EUR 3 000 and on 16.6.2009 an amount of EUR 2 500.
These payments were sent to the account of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax administrator agreed with the debtor to pay an additional installment of EUR 2,500 by 30 June 2009.
8.
A request for recovery of a receivable in the total amount of EUR 398,653, ie CZK 9,832,779, including a receivable from real estate transfer tax, was delivered from the Czech Tax Administrator to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 May 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2 October 2008.
On 3 April 2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a notification from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax authorities justified the refund by stating that the real estate transfer tax was not a tax within the meaning of Article 2 (a). e), f), g) or letter (h) Council Directive 2008/55 / ​​EC.
The German tax authorities further stated that Article 2 (a) (g) relates to income tax and property taxes.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55 / ​​EC applies to taxes on income and on capital, which are listed in Article 1 (3) in conjunction with paragraph 4 of Council Directive 77/799 / EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed to prepare and submit a new application for recovery, excluding arrears of real estate transfer tax in the amount of CZK 61,759 and indicating arrears of VAT, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be resent to the German tax authority. administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a new request from the Czech tax administrator for the recovery of tax arrears concerning the same tax entity that owes CZK 7,079,735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6 February 2006, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity which owed CZK 3,445,782, ie EUR 123,328, on personal income tax and VAT.
Of this amount, CZK 1,133,967 fell on VAT.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax administration until 18 April 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax administrator the reply of the German tax administration from 9 July 2007 to 11 November 2008.
The reply stated that on 11 June 2007 the German tax administrator had issued an enforcement order to a bank account with a bank, which, however, stated that it had no business relations with the taxable person.
The German tax authorities hereby considered the application pending.
10.
On 26 September 2005, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears on VAT in the total amount of CZK 1,296,845, ie EUR 43,591.
The application from the Czech tax administrator was delivered to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10 October 2005.
On 15 December 2005, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the German tax administration.
Prior to sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax administrator executed the debtor's funds on bank accounts and deducted his salary and established a lien on the immovable property.
Requests for recovery were preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authorities on 16 March 2005.
The reply to the request for information, which the Czech tax administrator received on 16 September 2005, showed that the Czech tax entity was resident in Germany and had income from non-business activities in the amount of EUR 8,437.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20 April 2006, but did not forward it to the Czech tax administrator until 12 February 2008.
The reply stated that no recovery procedure could be initiated in Germany due to the debtor's insolvency - no assets had been identified and his income from non-business activities was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
The German tax administration thus considered the request for recovery to be processed.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the field of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States follow the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling requests for international assistance in debt recovery in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and the BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay increased attention to the management of their statistics.
In a 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of inconsistencies in statistics had decreased, although the number of requests had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important that statistical issues be re-discussed at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent discrepancies, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the two SAIs agree that reliable statistics should show the annual number of applications as well as the nature of the claims in question (ie whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) and the amount of claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyzes of the statistics provided by Member States, as this can help Member States to assess their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that debt recovery rates can be calculated broken down by Member State is considered useful by both SAIs in intensifying Member States with a lower recovery rate and trying to improve the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should be actively involved in this process.
Especially in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery of receivables to the locally competent tax administrators in time.
A similar situation was found for applications for international assistance received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance had not complied with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., On International Assistance in Debt Recovery, because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State of the progress of recovery within six months from the date of receipt. applications.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., On the administration of taxes and fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or established for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax period stated in the personal / corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or higher.
The classification of the tax entity among the VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time in 2003.
A taxable person ceases to be classified as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax periods from the end of the period in which he filed the tax return on the basis of which he was classified as a VDS, his net turnover for the tax period fell below that threshold.
A tax subject may not be excluded from the VDS records without performing a tax audit of at least one tax for one tax period.
Until the end of 2009, all VDS were inspected at least every five years.
From 2010, a written evaluation of the tax subject must be performed at least once every 2 years, and the chosen subsequent procedure must eliminate tax risks and their negative impact on the correct assessment and collection of tax.
The FI control is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator usually chooses several tax periods at once.
VDS were inspected by specialized inspection departments, which are established at a total of 13 FAs, or by employees of control departments of locally relevant FIs.
The Specialized Controls Department carries out tax audits within the scope set by the Director of the Finance Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific fields of business;
• entities for which the implementation of a tax audit is professionally and time-consuming;
• entities with a branched territorial and organizational structure;
• Entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• Entities interconnected in chains and networks where large-scale tax evasion and undue lure of excessive deductions are suspected.
The number of tax audits performed by the specialized audit departments of the FI and the results of these audits are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., On Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists in the establishment of a specialized FI with nationwide competence for selected tax entities (including legal entities established for business purposes) with a turnover of more than 2 billion. CZK).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls on large companies follow the same rules as tax controls in general, ie the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • German Fiscal Code (AO), • Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also valid.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on control are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - On-the-spot tax control. In particular, these articles lay down the rules on the admissibility of on-the-spot (ie on-premises) tax audits, their scope, division of responsibilities, form and content of the audit notice, audit principles, obligations of the taxable person to cooperate and the preconditions for conducting the final hearing. communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax inspections are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Administration Act Pursuant to Article 5.1, point 1, in conjunction with Article 19 of the Act, participation in on-site tax inspections carried out by tax authorities is mandatory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the spot on the spot and the extent of the participation of the Federal Central Tax Office in tax audits.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it selects be inspected at a time to be determined by it.
In such a case, it may declare rules for the conduct and content of inspections at the premises of these companies.
Regulations on tax audits Pursuant to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, regulations on tax audits (German abbreviation BpO 2000) were approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper chamber of the German parliament in which the federal governments are represented).
These administrative regulations apply to on-site inspections carried out by the tax authorities of the Länder as well as by the Federal Central Tax Office.
Enterprises are classified according to size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to ex-post control (Article 4.2 BpO).
Pursuant to Article 33.1 of the BpO 2000, each informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BpO 2000.
Methodical instructions
In addition to the above, the supplementary methodology for the tax administration provides the following guidelines:
• Uniform manual for special VAT inspections in Germany;
• the USLO manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of data on intra-Community trade relations kept in the VIES system;
• the ZAUBER manual, which sets out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• work aids for various and special subjects.
The classification of tax subjects is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits according to the type of business.
The data are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to be inspected - not just large ones - must be determined at regular inspection intervals.
In general, inspections of large companies are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually announced, including VAT checks.
This means that during the audit, the final validity of the audit will be mainly income taxes, excise duties and VAT - ie inspections of all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks can be performed by either tax inspectors or VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organizational structure of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by audits is usually between three and five years.
BpO 2000 assumes a control period of three years.
All taxes of the company are subject to verification.
4.5.3 Management of control of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of VDS inspections, but focused on management issues in order to gain an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT inspections at VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax administrators on areas they consider essential for the management of this issue.
• What statistical records and analyzes concerning the VAT control of VDS are available to the tax administration management?
Especially:
• Are there any statistics or records of the extent to which a distinction is made between the fight against VAT fraud and VAT control in general?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such a resolution in the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between controls designed to combat VAT fraud and general VAT controls.
• Are there any statistics or records on the timeliness of VAT controls (in relation to the time period of the transactions audited)?
Czech Republic: Records of the timeliness of inquiries with relevance for intra-Community acquisitions of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information recorded in the ADIS system also includes data on the type of query duration.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax auditors only contain information on the average time of the last audit (information on the year).
This information does not provide an overview of selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; they also have the right to carry out VDS inspections.
However, statistics produced at federal level for the VAT special control services do not provide information on the classification of taxable persons.
• Are there any statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenue generated, broken down, for example, according to the following criteria:
i. a net increase in the tax liability (eg in cases where the taxable person has unduly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only a nominal increase in the tax liability (eg transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech Tax Administration monitors the number of tax audits performed, the volumes of additionally assessed tax broken down by type of tax, by the number of audited tax entities and by the number of audited tax periods.
Other tax procedures (local investigations, reprimand proceedings) are monitored in the same way.
Time data and amounts of additionally paid taxes are recorded as a separate task.
General debt statistics are also kept broken down by type of tax, but not by declared tax or tax established by the tax administrator.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and for special VAT control departments do not distinguish between these criteria.
In addition, these differences are not distinguished by most of the tax administrations visited.
• Are there areas of control that give rise to high additional revenues?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to select taxpayers for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at the federal level for tax inspectors and for special VAT control departments do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must enter the increased tax (VAT) liability imposed by them if they exceed a certain amount.
In such a case, it must specify, for example, the nature of the assessed increase in the tax liability.
• What findings are most common?
Czech Republic:
- VDS asserts an unjustified right to deduct input tax on supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to Section 72 (1) of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to Section 75 (3) of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents that did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73 (1) of the VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Section 21 (1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It was stated that there are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at the federal level for tax inspectors and for special VAT control departments do not provide such data.
Findings concerning VAT are not recorded separately by the Länder if they result from VDS tax audits.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder have to enter the increased tax (VAT) liability imposed by them if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyze this information.
• Does the tax administration analyze areas of control that give rise to high “revenue” and draw implications for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching national audits focusing on risky commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
Uniform statistics at the federal level for tax controllers and for the special VAT control departments do not provide data on audit areas from which high "revenues" flow.
There are differing views on the analysis process as well as on case management in terms of relevance.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but their use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
The differences in the responses of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a lot of data from tax audits and data from financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to establish a specialized financial office for the administration of VDS in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows that it is more difficult to perform these tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places more emphasis on the selection of individual cases on the basis of data from submitted tax returns.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce shortfalls in VAT revenues.
As a result, the revenue from VAT collection will increase and the level of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will also improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of both SAIs on parallel inspections of the VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and the BRH.
The two SAIs became better acquainted with the systems in force in the following areas: • intra-Community transactions, • VAT risk management, in particular as regards the selection of risk-prone transactions, • assistance in recovering VAT receivables, and • VAT control for large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in the strategies for detecting cases of VAT fraud were revealed, as well as differences in the above-mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany.
Control findings were compared and best practices were identified.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to launch a debate on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6. Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Edition deadline: June 2010.
